# Verified Ballot-Access Rules — all 51 jurisdictions

**51 / 51 jurisdictions verified.** Produced by the `ballot-rules-batch` workflow (research → ground citations → consensus/adversarial judge → tiered gate), **no human counsel**. Source of truth: `ballot-access-data/verified-rules.master.json` (per-state files in `states/`).

> ⚠️ Machine-verified, not legal advice · 2024-cycle figures recompute per cycle · `CONSERVATIVE-HOLD` = held at strictest reading until the auto-drafted SoS inquiry resolves.

## Per-state detail

### Alabama
- **signatures:** AL: 5,000 valid signatures (fixed statutory, independent presidential)
- **deadline:** AL: 74 days before general election (Aug 23, 2024) — NOT Sept 6 (draft is WRONG)
- **risk:** Signature count is solid (5,000 confirmed in §17-14-31(a)); the draft DEADLINE is materially wrong — it cites Sept 6 (a repealed pre-2012 date / a party convention-certificate date Ballotpedia conflated), but the enacted law (SB324, eff. 2024) sets the independent presidential petition deadline at 74 days before the election = Aug 23, 2024. Treat the deadline as Aug 23, 2024 and verify the exact 2028 date with the SOS before relying.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 5,000 valid signatures of qualified Alabama voters — a FIXED statutory number for an independent presidential candidate under Ala. Code §17-14-31(a). This is distinct from the 3%-of-last-gubernatorial-vote rule (42,458 statewide for 2024) that governs OTHER independent candidates under §17-9-3.
  - note: Both Ballotpedia quotes verified verbatim (page line 232). Independently confirmed against the primary source: enacted SB324 §17-14-31(a) — presidential candidates may be nominated 'by written petition signed by at least 5,000 qualified voters of this state.' The draft correctly separates this from the §17-9-3 3%/42,458 general-independent rule (SOS PDF quote also verified verbatim, lines 11-18).
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.93
  - uses: 74 days before the general election. For 2024 this was August 23, 2024 (election day Nov 5, 2024). DO NOT rely on September 6 — that is the WRONG date for an independent presidential petition.
  - note: Citation quotes verified verbatim, BUT the asserted VALUE (Sept 6) is wrong. The Sept 6 Ballotpedia quote describes the party national-convention certificate-of-nomination deadline (Ballotpedia line 226) and Ballotpedia conflated it onto the independent petition (line 232); Ballot Access News notes Sept 6 was Alabama's old deadline pre-2012. Enacted SB324 (LegiScan: Passed/Enacted 2024-05-03), amending §17-14-31(b), sets the deadline for presidential certificates AND petitions at '74 days before the date of the election' (strikethrough shows change from the prior '82nd day' = Aug 15). 74 days before Nov 5, 2024 = Aug 23, 2024 — independently corroborated by Ballot Access News, WVUA23, and 1819News reporting RFK Jr.'s Aug 23 deadline. Strictest-defensible value set to the earliest applicable deadline (Aug 23, 2024) to never risk a missed filing; exact 2028 date must be re-derived (74 days before that Election Day) and confirmed with the SOS.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. The 5,000-signature independent presidential petition is a single statewide total with no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement.
  - note: Ballotpedia quote verified verbatim (line 232). Confirmed against §17-14-31(a): 'petition signed by at least 5,000 qualified voters of this state' — a flat statewide count with no geographic allocation. No distribution language anywhere in the presidential petition statute.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: UNKNOWN / no circulator-specific qualifications are specified in Alabama law. Signatures must be gathered in person; signers must be registered Alabama voters. (Conservative posture: do not assume circulators are unrestricted — verify with SOS.)
  - note: Ballotpedia quote ('All petition signatures must be gathered in person, but the code does not specify requirements for petition circulators') verified verbatim (line 398). SOS PDF 'signatures of registered Alabama voters' verified verbatim (line 11). Reviewed full Rule 820-2-4-.05 (Cornell) and enacted SB324 — neither imposes circulator age/residency requirements. The draft's UNKNOWN/no-specified-requirement framing is itself the strict, safe statement, so it is left AUTO-LIVE; an SOS inquiry is queued to close the gap.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. Petition pages require only a per-page identifying statement, pagination, and per-signer information (name, residential address, date of birth, signature) under Rule 820-2-4-.05. No circulator affidavit, witness, or notarization is required.
  - note: SOS PDF quote (Rule 820-2-4-.05(3) per-signer info) verified verbatim (lines 63-66). Cornell LII text of Rule 820-2-4-.05 verified verbatim and read in full (subsections 1-3) — contains no notary/affidavit/witness requirement. Enacted SB324 likewise imposes none for the presidential petition.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. Signatures must be gathered in person on paper petitions; a photocopiable sample form is provided by the SOS. No digital/remote-online signature system exists for an Alabama independent presidential petition.
  - note: Ballotpedia 'gathered in person' quote verified verbatim (line 398); SOS PDF 'sample petition form, which may be photo copied' verified verbatim (lines 70-72). No source indicates any electronic submission path; in-person paper is confirmed.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. There is no filing/qualifying fee for an independent candidate and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative; the 5,000-signature petition is the sole ballot-access mechanism.
  - note: SOS PDF 'There is no qualifying fee' verified verbatim (line 4). §17-14-31(a) provides the petition as the only independent path (no fee alternative mentioned). Note: the draft's quote attributes 'There is no qualifying fee' to a sentence about choosing not to run as a party candidate — the exact phrase appears verbatim at line 4 of the SOS PDF, so grounding holds.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an INDEPENDENT PRESIDENTIAL candidate filing a §17-14-31 petition of 5,000 qualified voters, please confirm the exact filing deadline for the next general election: is it 74 days before Election Day (as amended by SB324, 2024), and what is that calendar date?
  - Please confirm there are NO circulator qualification requirements (age, residency, voter-registration) for an independent presidential petition under Alabama law, and that no circulator affidavit, witness, or notarization is required on petition pages beyond Rule 820-2-4-.05's per-signer information.

### Alaska
- **signatures:** HOLD: packet self-contradicts (3,409 narrative vs 3,614 dates page) — rely on the higher 3,614
- **deadline:** HOLD: rule is 90th day before general; controlling 2028 packet date = Aug 16, 2028 (draft mis-anchored on expired Aug 7, 2024)
- **risk:** Same official packet states two different signature counts (3,409 vs 3,614) and the draft's headline deadline is an expired 2024 date; both need DOE confirmation, so default to strictest (collect to 3,614, treat Aug 16, 2028 as the deadline) until resolved.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: At least 3,614 valid signatures of qualified Alaska voters (the higher of the two conflicting figures the official B05P packet publishes). The statutory formula is 1% of the ballots cast for President at the last presidential general election; 1% of the certified 2024 total (340,981) computes to 3,409.81, which the packet narrative rounds to 'at least 3,409.' However, the same packet's Election Law Dates page states the petition must have 'at least 3,614 signatures.' Until the Division resolves the contradiction, collect to the higher 3,614 floor to avoid any risk of falling short.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed in B05P.pdf (downloaded and text-extracted; narrative at lines 67-72, dates page at lines 119-123). 340,981 confirmed as the certified 2024 AK presidential total. The draft picks 3,409 as the value and labels 3,614 a mere 'packet inconsistency' to be overridden by the formula. Adversarially, 3,614 implies a base of ~361,400, not 2024's 340,981, so it looks erroneous/stale — BUT it is published by the same controlling official source. Strict, never-risk-ballot-access posture requires relying on the HIGHER figure (3,614) pending DOE confirmation, not silently overriding it down to 3,409. Note also the 'at least one percent' floor arguably rounds UP to 3,410, not down to 3,409. Interpretation (which figure governs) cannot be settled by retrieval.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.92
  - uses: File not earlier than January 1 of the presidential election year and not later than the 90th day before the presidential general election (AS 15.30.026(a)); by 6 AAC 25.074(a) the cutoff is 5:00 p.m. prevailing time on that 90th day, in person or by registered/certified mail (return receipt requested) postmarked on or before the 90th day and received within 15 days. For the upcoming (2028) cycle, the controlling B05P packet states this date is August 16, 2028 (90 days before the November 14, 2028 general election). Treat August 16, 2028, 5:00 p.m. prevailing time as the operative deadline.
  - note: Statute + regulation quotes verbatim-confirmed (B05P lines 64-67/482-487; Cornell LII 6 AAC 25.074(a)). The statutory rule is correct. BUT the draft's headline value anchors on 'August 7, 2024' — the 90th day before the Nov 5, 2024 general, an EXPIRED date for the wrong (already-completed) cycle — while burying the actual controlling date (August 16, 2028, stated twice in the packet, lines 44/67/113/119) as a parenthetical 'for reference.' Arithmetic verified: Nov 14, 2028 minus 90 days = Aug 16, 2028. For a forward-looking 2028 ballot rule, relying on a past 2024 date is unsafe; relied value corrected to the 2028 packet date. Which cycle/date governs is an interpretation retrieval alone shouldn't decide.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. The statute requires only a statewide signature total (1% of the last presidential vote); there is no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement. Alaska has a single at-large U.S. House district.
  - note: Quote verbatim-confirmed in B05P.pdf (line 68). Independently re-derived: AS 15.30.026(a) and 6 AAC 25.074 impose a single statewide 1% requirement with no geographic distribution language anywhere in the statute, regulation, or subscriber pages. Alaska is a single at-large district, so a distribution requirement would be structurally meaningless. No adversarial counter found.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: No separate circulator requirement is found in AS 15.30.026, AS 15.30.025, or 6 AAC 25.074. The only confirmed person-eligibility requirement is that each SIGNER (subscriber) must be a qualified voter of the State of Alaska and must provide a printed name, Alaska residence address, an identifier (last 4 SSN, voter #, DOB, ADL #, or AK State ID #), signature, and date. Treat the existence/absence of a distinct circulator rule as UNCONFIRMED and verify with the Division before relying on it.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed in B05P.pdf (subscriber petition text line 366-367; subscriber-provide line 92-94). The signer requirement is solidly grounded. However, the field's core claim is a NEGATIVE/absence inference ('no separate circulator rule exists anywhere'), which two cited sources cannot conclusively establish — a separate signature-verification or petition-circulation regulation could exist outside these two documents. Under strict posture this absence is interpretation-required and should be confirmed, not asserted as settled. Strictest defensible framing: rely only on the affirmatively-grounded signer requirement; treat circulator rules as unconfirmed.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No notarized affidavit and no per-signature circulator/witness certification is required. The only required certification is a written statement signed by the submitting candidate or party, filed at submission, acknowledging the number of petition booklets or subscriber pages included (6 AAC 25.074(b)). Individual subscriber signatures are not separately notarized or witnessed.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed (B05P signed-statement text line 97-99; Cornell LII 6 AAC 25.074(b)). Independently re-derived from the regulation: 25.074(b) requires only the single 'written statement signed by the submitting candidate or party.' The subscriber pages and statute contain no notary or per-signature witness/circulator-affidavit field. The receipt form (B05P lines 221-222/346-347) likewise asks only for the candidate/party signature. No adversarial counter found. Correct.
**🟡 captureMode** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: paper. The petition is circulated on paper subscriber pages/booklets and filed as a single paper instrument, delivered either in person (by 5:00 p.m. prevailing time on the deadline) or by registered/certified mail (return receipt requested) postmarked on or before the 90th-day deadline and received within 15 days. Assume paper-only for this independent presidential petition.
  - note: Core paper claim is grounded: Cornell LII 6 AAC 25.074(a) (registered/certified mail) and B05P 'mailed to the Division of Elections Director's Office' both verbatim-confirmed. 6 AAC 25.074 plus the physical subscriber pages clearly contemplate a paper instrument. HOWEVER, the draft's added NEGATIVE assertion — 'there is NO digital/remote-online system' and 'Alaska's e-signature system is limited to initiative/referendum measures, not candidate petitions' — is NOT supported by either cited quote and is an interpretive inference about scope. Strict posture: rely only on the grounded paper requirement (which is the safe operational answer); flag the no-digital-system claim as unverified by the citations.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. There is no filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures for ballot access via the independent presidential petition; signatures are the sole qualification mechanism under AS 15.30.026. The separate 'appropriate fee' in the Division's calendar relates only to placement in the Official Election Pamphlet under AS 15.58.030(a), not to getting on the ballot.
  - note: Pamphlet-fee quote verbatim-confirmed in B05P.pdf (Election Law Dates page, lines 125-129). Independently re-derived: AS 15.30.026 conditions ballot access solely on the petition signatures; no filing fee or fee-in-lieu appears anywhere in the statute, regulation, or packet for the petition itself. The packet's only fee reference is expressly tied to the Official Election Pamphlet (AS 15.58.030(a)), a distinct downstream step. The value correctly distinguishes the two. No adversarial counter found.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the 2028 cycle, the B05P presidential candidate packet states two different signature minimums for an independent presidential petition: the narrative text says 'at least 3,409' (1% of the 340,981 ballots cast for President in 2024), while the Election Law Dates page says 'at least 3,614 signatures.' Which figure is controlling, and what total of valid signatures must an independent presidential candidate collect to be certified for the November 14, 2028 ballot?

### Arizona
- **signatures:** AZ indep pres: ~42,303 (2024 only) — RECOMPUTES each cycle, do not hardcode
- **deadline:** AZ pres-elector filing: 80-100 days before general (Aug 17, 2024); date recomputes
- **risk:** Six of seven fields verified live; signaturesRequired held because the number is cycle-specific (3% of non-affiliated registrants as of Jan 2) and the draft's new-party comparison misreads its own Ballot Access News citation (34,116=Full Party, 41,090=Candidate, neither equals 42,303).

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.86
  - uses: Treat 42,303 as the 2024-cycle figure ONLY. For any live cycle the requirement must be recomputed as 3% of Arizona registered voters who are NOT members of a qualified party, measured as of January 2 of the general-election year (A.R.S. 16-341(E)-(F)), and verified against the Secretary of State's official signature-requirement table for that cycle. Any registered AZ voter may sign regardless of party. Do NOT rely on the draft's new-party comparison.
  - note: All four quotes verified verbatim. 42,303 for 2024 is double-corroborated by azcentral (Aug 16 + Aug 19, 2024) as the SoS-reported independent statewide presidential figure. HOLD reasons: (1) the value is explicitly cycle-recomputed (3% of non-affiliated registrants as of Jan 2) and must not be hardcoded for a future cycle; (2) the draft's NOTE misreads its own Ballot Access News citation: in that table 34,116 is the 'Full Party' column and *41,090 is the 'Candidate' column for Arizona; neither is 42,303, and the draft's claim that the new-party 'Candidate' figure (34,116) is lower than the independent figure inverts the table headers. The headline number is right; the surrounding interpretation is not reliable.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: A nomination petition for the office of presidential elector must be filed with the Arizona Secretary of State not less than 80 nor more than 100 days before the general election (A.R.S. 16-341(G)). For 2024 (general election Nov 5) this was August 17, 2024 (exactly 80 days prior). The 120-150-days-before-primary window in 16-341(C) does NOT apply to presidential-elector filings. NOTE: the specific calendar date recomputes from the general-election date each cycle.
  - note: Both quotes verified verbatim. The 80-100-day rule is a bright-line statute, correctly excluding presidential-elector petitions from the primary-tied window. Aug 17, 2024 derives correctly (80 days before Nov 5, 2024) and is independently confirmed by Ballot Access News. The rule is durable and non-interpretive; only the calendar date is cycle-dependent.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. A single statewide threshold (3% of statewide non-affiliated registered voters) applies; there is no geographic/congressional-district/county distribution requirement for an independent presidential-elector petition. The petition is a single group petition naming all elector candidates, and a valid signature counts for each elector candidate (A.R.S. 16-341(G)).
  - note: Quote verified verbatim in 16-341(G). Nothing in 16-341 imposes a distribution requirement; the threshold in 16-341(E)-(F) is a flat statewide percentage. Confirmed correct and non-interpretive.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: A circulator need NOT be an Arizona resident but must otherwise be eligible/qualified to register to vote in Arizona (U.S. citizen, 18+, etc., per A.R.S. 16-101). A non-resident circulator must register as a circulator with the Secretary of State before circulating petitions (A.R.S. 16-341(G), 16-321(D)). The circulator need not be a registered Arizona voter, only eligible to register.
  - note: Both quotes verified verbatim (16-341(G) and 16-321(D)). The statutory text supports each element, including the 'eligible to register' (not 'registered') standard and the non-resident circulator-registration requirement. Non-interpretive.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No notarization of signature sheets is required; the circulator must certify on each sheet that every signer signed in the circulator's presence on the indicated date and that the circulator believes each signer was a qualified elector residing at the listed address (A.R.S. 16-321(D)). Separately, the candidate's filing must include a consent statement SIGNED by the vice-presidential running mate and each designated presidential elector, and a nomination paper for each elector must be filed (A.R.S. 16-341(J)).
  - note: Both quotes verified verbatim. AZ requires circulator certification, not notarization, of the signature sheets. The azcentral notarization failure was MICHIGAN's, not Arizona's, so it does not undercut the no-notary finding. The elector-consent requirement (16-341(J)) is correctly grounded; the West 2024 filing's missing presidential/VP nomination forms and acceptance letter are corroborated by azcentral. Non-interpretive.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: Paper. No online signature system covers an independent presidential-elector petition in Arizona. E-Qual under A.R.S. 16-318 is limited to U.S. Senate and U.S. House candidates; 16-341(N) electronic petitions are discretionary and (per the SoS) have not been authorized for presidential-elector petitions. Collect on paper signature sheets (as RFK Jr. and Cornel West did in 2024).
  - note: All three quotes verified verbatim. 16-318(B) unambiguously limits E-Qual to U.S. Senator/Representative. 16-341(N) is discretionary ('may authorize ... for statewide and legislative offices'); whether presidential-elector qualifies as 'statewide' is an open reading, BUT the operative VALUE is unaffected: no electronic system has been authorized for these petitions, so paper is correct under every reading (corroborated by the physical petition boxes filed in 2024). The residual statutory-scope question is flagged to the SoS but does not change the answer.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: None. Arizona provides no filing-fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for an independent presidential candidate; the signature petition is mandatory, and a candidate who does not file a timely, compliant nomination petition is not eligible to appear on the ballot (A.R.S. 16-341(K)).
  - note: Quote verified verbatim (it appears in 16-341(K), though the draft's prose loosely cites the fine provision as 16-341(M) — the verbatim quote and its eligibility-bar substance are correct). Arizona's fee-in-lieu mechanisms apply to partisan primary candidates, not to independent nomination petitions; there is no fee alternative for an independent presidential candidate. Non-interpretive.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent (non-party) presidential-elector nomination petition under A.R.S. 16-341(E)-(F), what is the exact certified minimum signature count for the upcoming general-election cycle, computed as 3% of registered voters who are not members of a qualified party as of January 2 of the election year, and where is that official figure published?
  - Does A.R.S. 16-341(N)'s authorization of electronic petitions 'for statewide and legislative offices' extend to independent presidential-elector petitions, or are such petitions required to be collected on paper because E-Qual under A.R.S. 16-318 is limited to U.S. Senate and U.S. House candidates?

### Arkansas
- **signatures:** AR: 5,000 valid signatures (statewide, no distribution) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** AR: petition due noon, first Monday of August (2024 = Aug 5); electors certified by Sep 15 — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** Core burden (5,000 sigs / first-Monday-of-August / no distribution / paper / no fee) is fully grounded and AUTO-LIVE. Open risk is procedural: circulator qualifications and notary/affidavit for the PRESIDENTIAL petition are not settled by primary sources (the standard SoS affidavit is expressly carved out for President/VP) — held conservative pending SoS confirmation; over-comply (qualified-elector circulators + notarize) until answered.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96

  - note: All 3 citations verbatim-confirmed: FindLaw 7-8-302(6)(A) (current as of Mar 28, 2024), ballot-access.org HB1338 post, and Ballotpedia. No litigation or post-2024 change found.

SoS verifies sufficiency within 10 days. Separately, qualifying independent candidate must certify the elector slate to the SoS by September 15 (7-8-302(6)(C)).
  - note: Statute quote verbatim in FindLaw 7-8-302(6)(A) and (6)(C); NASS independent-candidate line verbatim-confirmed (lines 117-119 of the 07/29/24 NASS summary). Verified independently that first Monday of August 2024 = Aug 5, 2024. Sep 15 elector-certification correctly sourced to (6)(C).
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.94

### California
- **signatures:** CA: 219,403 valid sigs (1% of statewide reg.); independent pres. qualifies via slate of 54 electors. AUTO-LIVE.
- **deadline:** CA: nomination papers due 5:00pm Aug 9, 2024 (E-88); circulate from Apr 26, 2024 (E-193). AUTO-LIVE.
- **risk:** 6 of 7 fields verified live; only circulatorEligibility is held — draft's "circulators must be registered CA voters" is NOT supported by ELEC 102/8451 (age 18+ is the only requirement), so do not rely on a voter-registration screen for circulators.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 219,403 valid signatures for the 2024 cycle, equal to 1% of statewide voter registration as of the last Report of Registration prior to the November 2022 General Election; recomputes each presidential cycle. No direct independent presidential line — the candidate qualifies by nominating a slate of 54 presidential electors (plus 54 alternates) via independent nomination, with the nomination papers carrying the signatures. Cal. Elections Code 8400, 8303, 8550; 2187(c)(6).
  - note: All three quotes verbatim in sources. SoS PDF states '219,403... (equivalent to 1%... prior to the November 2022 General Election)' and the 54-elector qualification path. ELEC 8400 independently confirms 1% of registered voters for statewide office; Ballotpedia independently confirms 219,403 and '1% of the total number of registered voters in the state' for 2024 independent presidential. Path-via-electors framing is correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: For the Nov 5, 2024 General Election: nomination papers circulate from Apr 26, 2024 (E-193) and must be delivered to the county elections official no later than 5:00 p.m. on Aug 9, 2024 (E-88); electors' Declarations of Candidacy also due 5:00 p.m. Aug 9, 2024 (E-88). Statutory rule: 88 days before the general election; recomputes per cycle. Cal. Elections Code 8403(a)(2), 8550.
  - note: SoS quotes verbatim. ELEC 8403(a)(2) independently confirms: for offices with no filing fee, papers circulated/delivered to county no earlier than 193 days and no later than 5 p.m. 88 days before the election. Ballotpedia confirms 8/9/2024 deadline and '5:00 p.m. 88 days prior to the election.'
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. The 1% requirement is a single statewide total; there is no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement for the independent presidential (presidential elector) nomination. Signatures are gathered and delivered county-by-county to the county where signers reside for verification, but no minimum-per-county quota applies.
  - note: Quotes verbatim. ELEC 8400 sets a single statewide 1% number for statewide office with no geographic-distribution clause; ELEC 8403(c) addresses only a void-if-insufficient mechanism and per-county delivery for verification, not a per-county minimum. No distribution rule found in primary law.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Circulators must be 18 years of age or older (Cal. Elections Code 102, 8451). The strictest reliable statement of eligibility is the age-18 requirement only. A registered voter who is a candidate may circulate and sign their own nomination papers (106(a)). Do NOT rely on a 'circulator must be a registered California voter' requirement — it is not supported by 102/8451; confirm any residency/registration condition with the SoS before screening circulators.
  - note: The grounded SoS quote supports ONLY age 18+. The draft's added claim that circulators 'must be registered voters of California (per 102/8451)' is contradicted by the actual statutes: ELEC 102 reads 'A person shall not circulate... unless the person is 18 years of age or older' and ELEC 8451 says 'Circulators shall meet the requirements of Section 102' — neither imposes a voter-registration requirement (ELEC 104(b)(3) likewise lists only age 18+ for the circulator declaration). Holding because the value asserts an unsupported, stricter-than-law requirement; relied value corrected to the defensible age-18 floor.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No notarization is required. Each section of the nomination paper must carry a circulator declaration signed in the circulator's own hand, certified under penalty of perjury (Cal. Elections Code 104); there is no notary/affidavit-before-officer requirement. All signers must be registered California voters (100, 8400), and signed papers are delivered to the county elections official where signers reside for verification before forwarding to the Secretary of State.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim. SoS summary specifies no notary. ELEC 104 independently confirms the integrity mechanism is a circulator declaration 'under penalty of perjury under the laws of the State of California' — not notarization. Draft's core 'no notarization' conclusion is correct (draft does not name 104 but asserts nothing false).
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: paper. Signatures are collected on physical nomination papers circulated to registered voters and delivered to county elections officials for verification. There is no remote-online or digitized signature system for the independent presidential (presidential elector) petition in California; the SoS Summary describes only paper nomination papers and Declarations of Candidacy filed by mail, in-person drop box, or at a county elections office.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim in the SoS PDF. SoS process is entirely physical circulation/delivery; ELEC 8400/8403 contemplate paper nomination papers. No e-signature path exists for this petition.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. No filing fee is required to file the nomination papers, and California provides no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative for the independent presidential (presidential elector) nomination — the signature petition is the sole path.
  - note: Quote verbatim: SoS PDF 'No filing fee is required from any person in order to file nomination papers.' Ballotpedia 2024 table lists filing fee 'N/A' for CA independent presidential. The no-fee/no-fee-in-lieu framing is consistent (the no-fee status is precisely why the longer E-193 circulation window in 8403(a)(2) applies).

### Colorado
- **signatures:** 12,000 total (1,500 in EACH of 8 CDs) — fixed per-district, not 5,000
- **deadline:** 117th day before general election; time-of-day in conflict (SOS 3pm vs statute 5pm) — use 3pm
- **risk:** 7 of 8 fields verify clean for an unaffiliated presidential candidate; only the deadline TIME-OF-DAY is in genuine source conflict (SOS page 3:00 p.m. vs statute effective 1/1/2025 5 p.m.) — treat 3:00 p.m. as the binding cutoff and confirm with SOS before any cycle.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 12,000 total — at least 1,500 valid signatures of registered Colorado electors in EACH of the state's 8 congressional districts (1,500 x 8 = 12,000). Fixed per-district number, not a percentage and not a flat statewide number. Signers must be registered Colorado voters who have not signed a petition for any other candidate for the same office.
  - note: Both citations verbatim. SOS PresidentPetition.html: '1,500 signatures in each of the 8 congressional district (12,000 total)'; C.R.S. 1-4-802(1)(c)(I): 'At least one thousand five hundred in each congressional district for the office of president and vice president'. Independently confirmed: CO has 8 CDs post-2020 census, so 1,500x8=12,000. The draft's flag that Ballotpedia's stale '5,000' is incorrect is itself correct — Ballotpedia line 235 still says '5,000 eligible voters' which is the pre-redistricting flat figure superseded by the per-CD schedule. Current and correct.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: File the completed petition no later than 3:00 p.m. on the 117th day before the general election. The 117-day rule is confirmed by both the statute (C.R.S. 1-4-802(1)(f)(I)) and SOS guidance; the time-of-day is in conflict (SOS guidance says 3:00 p.m.; statutory text effective 1/1/2025 says 5 p.m.). Use the EARLIER 3:00 p.m. cutoff, which satisfies both. Circulation cannot begin earlier than the 173rd day before the general election (C.R.S. 1-4-802(1)(d)(I)). For 2024 the deadline fell on 7/11/24; recomputes each cycle off the November general-election date.
  - note: All three citations verbatim. Findlaw shows the statute is split: text effective UNTIL 1/1/2025 = '3 p.m.', text effective 1/1/2025 = '5 p.m.'. The SOS web guidance still states 3:00 p.m. This is a genuine source conflict on time-of-day that retrieval cannot settle (which controls for a 2026+ cycle — updated statute or the not-yet-updated SOS page). Strictest defensible reading: file by 3:00 p.m., which complies under either rule. The 117-day count itself is not in dispute. Ballotpedia 7/11/24 / 8/7/24 dates match the footnote verbatim and are consistent with a 117-day computation off 11/5/2024.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: YES — distribution required: at least 1,500 signatures in EACH of the 8 congressional districts. Signers must be eligible electors residing within the district in which the office is to be elected. Per-CD minimum, not a statewide aggregate; signatures cannot be concentrated in one district.
  - note: C.R.S. 1-4-802(1)(c) verbatim: 'Every petition for the office of president and vice president ... must be signed by eligible electors residing within the district or political subdivision in which the officer is to be elected', combined with 1-4-802(1)(c)(I)'s 'in each congressional district' establishes a binding per-CD minimum. SOS quote verbatim. Note: 'in each congressional district' is the operative distribution language; the residency clause and the per-CD minimum together fully support the value. Current and correct.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: A petition circulator must be a citizen of the United States and at least 18 years of age. No Colorado residency requirement and no voter-registration requirement is imposed on the circulator. Paid vs. volunteer circulators must wear an identifying badge (PAID CIRCULATOR / VOLUNTEER CIRCULATOR).
  - note: C.R.S. 1-4-905(1) verbatim: 'A person shall not circulate a petition to nominate a candidate unless the person is a citizen of the United States and at least eighteen years of age.' SOS quote verbatim. Adversarial check: 1-4-905 imposes no residency/registration requirement on circulators (only US citizenship + 18+); the badge requirement in 1-4-905(6) confirms the parenthetical. Current and correct.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: BOTH a notarized circulator affidavit AND a notarized candidate acceptance are required. (1) Each petition SECTION must have attached a signed, dated, notarized circulator affidavit; the circulator must appear in the physical presence of the notary; an improperly notarized affidavit is invalid and the section cannot be accepted (C.R.S. 1-4-905(2)-(3)). (2) Before filing, the petition must have attached a notarized acceptance of nomination by the candidate (or by both joint president/VP candidates) (C.R.S. 1-4-906); SOS guidance requires the candidate/VP acceptance forms to be notarized.
  - note: All three citations verbatim. 1-4-905(2)(a): 'Each petition section must have attached a signed, notarized, and dated affidavit executed by the person who circulated the petition section'; 1-4-905(2)(b)(I)(A) confirms physical-presence; 1-4-905(2)(b)(II) makes a violating affidavit invalid; 1-4-905(3) bars acceptance without the notarized affidavit. 1-4-906 verbatim on the notarized candidate acceptance. SOS notarization quote verbatim. Current and correct.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. The unaffiliated presidential petition is paper-only: SOS must approve the petition format before circulation, the petition is circulated on paper, each section requires a wet-ink notarized circulator affidavit (circulator physically present before the notary), and the completed petition plus notarized acceptance forms are hand-delivered to the SOS Elections Division in Denver (1700 Broadway, Suite 550). No online/remote-signing or digitized-capture system covers an unaffiliated presidential nominating petition in Colorado.
  - note: All three citations verbatim. SOS: 'Petition formats must be approved by the Secretary of State's office prior to circulation' and 'Hand deliver petition and acceptance forms to:' (Denver address printed on page). 1-4-905(2)(b)(I)(A) physical-presence notarization verbatim. The negative existence claim (no e-signing) is strongly supported by the wet-ink/physical-presence/hand-delivery requirements; no contrary source found. Current and correct for the unaffiliated presidential route.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: None for the unaffiliated presidential route. There is no filing-fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for an unaffiliated presidential candidate; the nominating petition (1,500/CD, 12,000 total) is the only path onto the general-election ballot. The petition-or-fee CHOICE applies only to major-party presidential PRIMARY candidates (C.R.S. 1-4-1204), not to general-election access for an independent. Minor-party note: forming a NEW minor party requires a separate statewide petition of at least 10,000 registered electors filed by the 2nd Friday in January of the election year; a QPO candidate petitions under the same 1-4-802 schedule. An individual independent uses the 1-4-802 unaffiliated path and pays no fee.
  - note: Citations verbatim: SOS 'Submit the notarized acceptance of petition nomination forms with the completed petition.' and QPO FAQ 'Be signed by at least 10,000 registered electors in Colorado; and' (also confirms '2nd Friday in January of the election year'). Adversarial check: the SOS PresidentPetition.html unaffiliated workflow lists no fee step and no fee-in-lieu option; 1-4-802 sets signatures as the sole requirement with no fee alternative. The 1-4-1204 primary fee/petition choice is a separate major-party primary mechanism not available to an independent. Current and correct. (The cited SOS quote supports the 'petition is the path' framing rather than a fee, which is the correct grounding for a negative-existence claim.)

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an unaffiliated presidential nominating petition under C.R.S. 1-4-802(1)(f)(I), is the filing cutoff on the 117th day before the general election 3:00 p.m. (per your PresidentPetition.html guidance) or 5:00 p.m. (per the statutory text effective Jan 1, 2025)? Please confirm the exact wall-clock deadline currently enforced.

### Connecticut
- **signatures:** 7,500 wet-ink signatures (lesser of 1% of last presidential vote or 7,500; 1% of 1,759,010 = ~17,590, so 7,500 governs)
- **deadline:** SOTS by 4:00pm Jul 29, 2026; town clerk by 4:00pm Aug 5, 2026 (90th day before Nov 3, 2026)
- **risk:** All citations grounded verbatim against the 2026 ED-607, 2020 FAQ, candidate-ballot-access page, and Ballotpedia; the four hard operative rules (count, deadline, no distribution quota, witness/notary, paper-only) are AUTO-LIVE, but two fields assert legal NEGATIVES (no circulator residency requirement; no filing fee) that retrieval cannot conclusively settle, so they are held conservative pending SOS confirmation.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Lesser of (1) 1% of the votes cast for the same office at the last preceding election, or (2) 7,500. For an independent presidential candidate the operative number is 7,500, because 1% of Connecticut's 2024 presidential vote (1,759,010 total) is ~17,590, far above 7,500. The petition for the office of presidential elector must list seven candidates for Presidential Elector plus a candidate for President and a candidate for Vice-President. The Elections Services Division computes the exact figure at issuance, but the law prevails.
  - note: Both ED-607 quotes (lesser-of-1%-or-7,500; seven electors + Pres + VP) found verbatim at lines 98-104 and 62-64; Ballotpedia quote found verbatim. Independently confirmed 7,500 is operative: CT 2024 presidential total = 1,759,010 (Wikipedia), 1% = 17,590 > 7,500. Operative number is statutory, not interpretation-dependent.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Not later than 4:00 p.m. on the 90th day preceding the regular election. For the November 3, 2026 general election: submit to the Secretary of the State by 4:00 p.m. July 29, 2026; after July 29, pages may be submitted only to the town clerk of the signers' town of voting residence by 4:00 p.m. August 5, 2026. Withdrawals of signatures also run to Aug 5, 2026.
  - note: ED-607 quote (Jul 29 SOTS / Aug 5 town clerk) found verbatim at lines 158-160; FAQ 90-day-rule quote found verbatim at line 66. Document states the specific 2026 dates authoritatively, consistent with the Nov 3, 2026 general election. Town-clerk Aug 5 date aligns with the 90-day rule; SOTS path closes a week earlier.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. Connecticut imposes no congressional-district or county signature-distribution quota. The only geographic constraints are (1) each signer must be an elector eligible to vote for all offices/candidates listed (statewide for president) and (2) no single page may be circulated among electors of more than one town (a per-page town-verification mechanic, not a distribution requirement).
  - note: Both ED-607 quotes found verbatim (signer-eligibility at lines 109-111; one-town-per-page at lines 116-119). No district/county quota appears anywhere in the instructions; the one-town-per-page rule is correctly characterized as a town-clerk verification mechanic, not a geographic distribution requirement.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: Each circulator must be a United States citizen, at least 18 years of age, and not on parole for conviction of a felony; a candidate may circulate and sign his or her own petition. STRICTEST POSTURE pending SOS confirmation: treat in-state residency as potentially required and prefer Connecticut-resident circulators, because the asserted absence of any residency requirement is an inference from the form's silence (it asks circulators to state name/street/town/STATE of residence) rather than an affirmative statement of no-residency.
  - note: Affirmative criteria (US citizen, 18+, not on felony parole) found verbatim in ED-607 (lines 90-91) and FAQ (lines 51-52); 'candidate may circulate own' grounded in FAQ. But 'no in-state residency requirement' is a NEGATIVE inferred from the form asking for state of residence; retrieval cannot conclusively confirm no residency rule exists. Held conservative to avoid ballot-access risk from out-of-state circulators; SOS inquiry added.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Each page must carry the circulator's Statement of Residence and Eligibility and of the Authenticity of Signatures, signed under penalties of false statement, attesting each signer signed in the circulator's presence and was known to or identified to the circulator. That statement must be signed in the presence of an authorized officer (town clerk, Secretary of the State, notary public, judge of a court of record, family support magistrate, clerk/deputy clerk of a court with a seal, commissioner of deeds, Connecticut justice of the peace, or a Connecticut-admitted attorney), who must certify the circulator signed before him and was known/identified. Pages lacking the statement and certification are not accepted. This is a notarization-type attestation, not a self-notarized affidavit.
  - note: Both ED-607 quotes found verbatim (attestation language at lines 138-141; list of authorized officers at lines 143-146). The officer-certification requirement and the rejection of pages lacking it (lines 149-151) confirm this is an officer-witnessed attestation, accurately characterized.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Independent (nominating-petition) presidential signatures must be wet-ink on the official Petition Signature Page distributed by the Secretary of the State, or on duplicates of pages issued by the SOTS; each page is town-specific and physically certified by the town clerk/registrars against the registry list. The SOTS DocuSign system applies only to primary petitions, certificates of party endorsement, 15% eligibility, and minor-party nominations with statewide ballot access, not to independent nominating-petition signature collection.
  - note: ED-607 'official Petition Signature Page... or duplicates' quote found verbatim at lines 119-121; candidate-ballot-access DocuSign-scope quote found verbatim. Core operative fact (signatures = wet-ink paper) is solidly grounded and not interpretation-dependent. The secondary sub-claim that 'only ED-602b may be emailed' is not directly substantiated by the sources but does not affect the operative captureMode.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: Treat collecting the required 7,500 signatures as the sole and exclusive path onto the ballot for an independent/petitioning presidential candidate; assume NO filing fee and NO fee-based alternative, but confirm with the SOS before relying on the absence of any fee. No filing fee or fee alternative appears in the 2026 ED-607 instructions or the 2020/2026 FAQ, but the cited quote substantiates only the signature count, not the no-fee proposition.
  - note: The attached citation quote (signature-count FAQ language) was found verbatim, so citation integrity holds, BUT that quote addresses signature counts, not fees, so it does not affirmatively substantiate 'no fee.' The 'None' claim is a NEGATIVE inferred from the sources' silence on fees. Substantively CT has no nominating-petition filing fee, but a negative cannot be conclusively settled by retrieval; held conservative and SOS inquiry added.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Does Connecticut impose any in-state residency requirement on circulators of an independent presidential nominating petition, or may an out-of-state U.S. citizen (18+, not on felony parole) lawfully circulate and certify petition pages?
  - Is there any filing fee, deposit, or fee-based alternative associated with an independent presidential nominating petition, or is collecting the required signatures the sole path onto the general-election ballot?

### Delaware
- **signatures:** DE: 1% of statewide registration (Dec 31 prior yr) — HOLD on the "~7,600" number; rely on the formula, confirm exact count w/ Commissioner
- **deadline:** DE: Petition + sworn non-affiliation declaration due by close of business Sept 1 of election year (circulate Jan 1–Jul 15) — LIVE
- **risk:** Core legal rule (1% statewide, Sept 1 deadline, notarized circulator affidavit, paper-only, no fee) is fully grounded in 15 Del. C. 3002 + DE elections office; two holds — the specific ~7,600 signature count is unverified and possibly low (use the 1% formula, not a fixed number), and circulator eligibility is statutorily silent (assume strict: adult DE registered-voter circulators) pending Commissioner confirmation.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Not less than 1% of the total number of voters registered statewide in Delaware as of December 31 of the year immediately preceding the general election year (15 Del. C. 3002(b)). This is a recomputed percentage with no fixed statutory number; do NOT plan to a specific count such as ~7,600. Treat the required number as the 1% formula applied to the certified statewide registration total for the actual cycle, and confirm the exact figure with the State Election Commissioner before relying on it. Path: unaffiliated-candidate nominating petition; president is a statewide office.
  - note: Legal rule fully grounded: statute quote (15 Del. C. 3002(b)) and DE elections-office quote both appear VERBATIM at the cited pages; Ballotpedia corroborates the 1% statewide basis. Adversarial re-derivation confirms the 1% formula is correct and current. HOLD is driven solely by the embedded, self-disclaimed estimate 'roughly 7,600 signatures (~760,000 registrants).' This number is NOT from a primary source and I could not independently verify it (web search was intermittently unavailable). Recent DE statewide registration has run well above 760k (plausibly ~770k-790k+), so 1% could be ~7,700-7,900 — meaning 7,600 may UNDERSTATE the requirement, a ballot-access risk. Stripped the hard number; relied value is the formula only.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: The nominating petition and the sworn unaffiliated-candidate declaration of non-affiliation must be filed on or before the close of the official business day on September 1 of the general election year, with the State Election Commissioner (president is a statewide office) per 15 Del. C. 3002(b). Separately, the petition may be circulated and executed only between January 1 and July 15 of the election year (15 Del. C. 3002(d)).
  - note: Statute quote (3002(b)) appears VERBATIM at delcode.delaware.gov/title15/c030; Ballotpedia quote (Sept 1 filing; Jan 1-Jul 15 circulation) appears VERBATIM in the saved page (line 231). Independently re-derived: 3002(b) text confirms Sept 1 close-of-business filing; 3002(d) confirms the Jan 1-Jul 15 circulation window. Clean calendar facts, no interpretation. Added the circulation window to reliedValue because it is a hard companion constraint the draft mentioned only under distributionRule.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. A single statewide 1% threshold applies with no per-county or per-congressional-district minimum quota. Signatures are collected on county-segregated petition sheets — each signer must sign the petition prepared for the county in which that voter is registered, and each county's petition is filed with and verified by that county's Department of Elections (15 Del. C. 3002(d)). This is an organizational/filing rule, not a minimum-per-county distribution requirement.
  - note: Statute quote (3002(d): 'Such petition shall be circulated and executed between January 1 and July 15... Each registered voter signing shall do so upon a petition prepared for the county in which that registered voter is registered, and the petition shall be filed with the Department. The signatures and other information thereon shall be verified by the department receiving the petition.') appears VERBATIM. Re-derivation confirms no per-county minimum exists in Chapter 30; the county-segregation is purely organizational. Characterization is accurate.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: Treat circulators conservatively: use circulators who are adults, Delaware residents, and themselves registered Delaware voters, and who can appear before a notary to swear they witnessed each signature (15 Del. C. 3002(c)(4)), pending written confirmation from the State Election Commissioner. The statute imposes no EXPRESS age/residency/voter-registration requirement on the circulator, but its silence does not rule out requirements in the Commissioner's prescribed petition form or regulations; the strict assumption avoids any risk of signature/petition rejection. Each SIGNER must be a registered Delaware voter on the date of signing (3002(e)(1)).
  - note: Citation grounded: the quote '(1) The signer was not a registered voter on the date the signer signed the petition;' appears VERBATIM in 3002(e). The draft's value is 'UNKNOWN' for circulator qualifications, which matches the statute text (3002 has no circulator-eligibility clause; only the notarized witness statement in 3002(c)(4)). HOLD because correctness hinges on absence-of-evidence: retrieval cannot confirm that the Commissioner's prescribed form/regs impose no circulator requirements, and 'UNKNOWN' is not a safe operational value. Over-comply with the strictest plausible practice and ask the Commissioner directly (see sosInquiries).
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Yes. The nominating petition must contain a sworn notarized statement of the person circulating the petition that they witnessed the placing of each signature (15 Del. C. 3002(c)(4)). Separately, the candidate must file a sworn declaration (with the State Election Commissioner for a statewide/presidential candidate) stating non-affiliation with any political party for at least 90 days before filing (3002(b)). Each signer must also acknowledge that knowingly entering false information may subject the signer to perjury prosecution (3002(c)(3)).
  - note: Both statute quotes appear VERBATIM at delcode.delaware.gov/title15/c030: 3002(c)(4) notarized circulator-witness statement, and 3002(b) the sworn non-affiliation declaration to the State Election Commissioner for statewide candidates. The perjury acknowledgment (3002(c)(3)) is also present in the retrieved text. Re-derivation confirms all three. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Wet-ink paper petition only. Each signer provides signature, printed name, registration address, Social Security number, and date (15 Del. C. 3002(c)(2)), on county-segregated paper petition sheets with a notarized circulator certification, filed with and verified against the permanent registration record by the county Department of Elections. The Department provides the unaffiliated petition as a downloadable PDF to be printed, circulated, and physically filed; there is no digital/online submission path for this petition.
  - note: Statute quote ('Signature, printed name, address at which registered, social security number and date on which signed by signer;') appears VERBATIM in 3002(c)(2); elections-office quote ('Complete Petition for Unaffiliated Candidate to Secure Ballot Status by September 1st of a general election year.') appears VERBATIM. The operative value 'paper' is correct and is also the strict/safe answer. The 'NO digital system' claim is a negative I cannot exhaustively prove, but it is strongly supported (SSN + notarized wet-ink witness + downloadable PDF form), and it does not loosen any requirement, so AUTO-LIVE on the value 'paper'.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: None. There is no filing fee in lieu of, or in addition to, signatures for the unaffiliated (independent) path; the signature petition is the sole means of ballot qualification. Filing fees (no more than 1% of the office's total term salary, set by the party, 15 Del. C. 3103) apply only to major-party primary candidates, not to the unaffiliated petition route or to a presidential candidate using it.
  - note: Both elections-office quotes appear VERBATIM: 'Set filing fees of no more than 1% of the total salary for the term of an office. ( 3103)' (listed under major political parties) and 'File An Unaffiliated Candidate Declaration' (under unaffiliated candidates, with no fee). Re-derivation confirms the unaffiliated path in Chapter 30 has no fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option. Correct.

### District of Columbia
- **signatures:** 1% of DC registered electors (144th-day count); 4,583 in 2024; recomputes each cycle; max 2x
- **deadline:** 90th day before election, by 5:00 p.m., in person (Aug 7, 2024)
- **risk:** All citations grounded verbatim. Core operative rules verified against primary DC Code/DCMR. Two caveats: the per-cycle signature COUNT must be recomputed from the Board's 144th-day registration (do not hardcode 4,583 for a future cycle), and the statute's path is worded "political party which does not qualify," not "independent" — independent status is supported by DCMR 3-1502.2(a) but is a characterization worth confirming with the Board. DC's requirement is the most severe presidential requirement of all 51 jurisdictions and is the subject of ongoing reform lobbying/constitutional criticism (no change to current law).

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: A non-major-party (independent or unqualified-party) presidential candidate must file a nominating petition signed by at least 1% of the District's registered qualified electors as shown by the Board's records as of the 144th day before the presidential election, under D.C. Code 1-1001.08(f). The exact count RECOMPUTES each cycle from the 144th-day registration total (for the 2024 cycle this equaled 4,583 valid signatures; do not rely on this fixed number for any other cycle). The Board accepts at most 2x the minimum for filing (DCMR 3-1503.2). Strictest reading: confirm the cycle-specific number with the Board and treat 1% as the governing rate.
  - note: All 4 citations verified verbatim. The 1% rate is correct and current and directly grounded in statute 1-1001.08(f) and DCMR 1503.1; the 2x cap is grounded in 1503.2; the 4,583 figure for 2024 is corroborated by ballot-access.org. HOLD because (a) the operative signature COUNT is cycle-dependent and must be re-derived from the Board's 144th-day registration, so a fixed number is not a safe live value, and (b) the draft's framing that an 'independent' runs via 1-1001.08(f) is a legal characterization — the statute literally addresses 'a political party which does not qualify under subsection (d),' not 'independent' (DCMR 3-1502.2(a) supports the independent designation but the routing should be confirmed).
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: The nominating petition (with supporting affidavits and each presidential elector's Declaration of Candidacy) must be filed in person at the Board's office no later than 5:00 p.m. on the 90th day before the presidential election (D.C. Code 1-1001.08(f); DCMR 3-1505.2; 5:00 p.m. cutoff per 1-1001.08(q)). For the November 5, 2024 general election this deadline was August 7, 2024.
  - note: All 3 citations verified verbatim. Independently confirmed by date arithmetic: Aug 7, 2024 is exactly 90 days before Nov 5, 2024 (24 + 30 + 31 + 5 = 90). The 5:00 p.m. in-person requirement is grounded in DCMR 1505.2 and 1-1001.08(q). Current and correct; no interpretation needed.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. The 1% requirement is computed District-wide against all registered qualified electors of the District; there is no per-ward, per-precinct, or per-district geographic distribution requirement for the presidential elector petition. DC has no congressional districts or counties.
  - note: Citation verified verbatim. Statute 1-1001.08(f) imposes a single District-wide 1% count with no geographic spread. The ward-based signature thresholds elsewhere in 1-1001.08 apply to Council/State Board of Education seats, NOT to presidential electors. Correct and current.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Only a qualified petition circulator may circulate; signatures on any sheet circulated by an unqualified circulator are invalid (D.C. Code 1-1001.08(b)(2)). Circulators must be at least 18 (DCMR 3-1504.1(c)). Residency is NOT required: non-resident circulators are permitted but must first complete and file, in person at the Board's office, a Non-Resident Petition Circulator Registration Form (swearing they are 18+, providing proof of residence, and consenting to the Board's subpoena power) before circulating (DCMR 3-1504).
  - note: All 3 citations verified verbatim. Statute requires qualified circulators and invalidates signatures otherwise; DCMR 3-1504 expressly authorizes non-resident circulators subject to prior in-person registration and 18+ oath. Correct and current.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Each petition sheet must carry a circulator's affidavit made under penalty of perjury (NOT notarized) stating the circulator is qualified and has personally circulated the sheet, personally witnessed each signer sign, and inquired about each signer's voter status (D.C. Code 1-1001.08(b)(3)). Any sheet lacking a completed circulator's affidavit is not counted (DCMR 3-1505.4). Notarization is required only from a voter who submits a written request to disallow their own signature, not for the circulator's certification.
  - note: Both citations verified verbatim. Statute specifies an affidavit 'made under penalty of perjury' (self-executing, no notary). DCMR 1505.4 confirms sheets without a completed circulator affidavit are not counted, and that the only notarized item is a voter's written request to disallow their own signature. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. Signed petition sheets must be filed with the Board in hard copy and in person (D.C. Code 1-1001.08(b)(3A); DCMR 3-1505.2). Only blank/unsigned petition forms may move electronically (Board to candidate; candidate to circulator; circulator to candidate). There is no remote-online or in-person-digitized signature system for the independent/non-qualified-party presidential petition; signed sheets are filed on paper.
  - note: Both citations verified verbatim. Statute 1-1001.08(b)(3A) requires petition sheets be 'filed with the Board in hard copy,' permitting only electronic transmission of (blank) forms among Board/candidate/circulator; DCMR 1505.2 requires in-person filing. Conclusion (paper, in person) is directly grounded. The 'eSign device' aside is extra context but does not affect the grounded conclusion.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: None. The District imposes no filing fee for presidential ballot access and offers no fee option in lieu of (or in addition to) the signature petition. Ballot access is obtained solely by the nominating petition meeting the 1% requirement (D.C. Code 1-1001.08(f); DCMR 3-1503.1).
  - note: Both citations verified verbatim. This is a negative claim (no fee alternative exists). The statute and DCMR Chapter 3-15 establish the nominating petition as the sole ballot-access mechanism; no fee or fee-in-lieu provision appears anywhere in the reviewed primary sources. Consistent across all sources; correct and current.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the upcoming presidential cycle, please confirm the exact minimum number of valid signatures required for a non-qualified-party/independent presidential nominating petition under D.C. **🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92

  - uses: Each petition signature is verified by the county supervisor by comparing it against the signer's signature in the voter registration system (Fla. **🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92

No fee-in-lieu path is the correct strict reading. Sub-cites accurate.
