### Georgia
- **signatures:** GA: do NOT rely on 7,500 — post-West v. Wittenstein strict reading is per-elector petitions (16 x 7,500 = ~120,000)
- **deadline:** GA: nomination petition by 12:00 Noon 2nd Tue in July; notice of candidacy 4th Mon June to following Fri (recompute each cycle)
- **risk:** Highest risk is signaturesRequired: the GA Supreme Court (West v. Wittenstein, unanimous, 9/25/2024) rejected the single-7,500-petition model and held each presidential-elector candidate must file his/her own nomination petition, implying ~120,000 valid signatures under the strictest reading; treating 7,500 as the operative total would risk ballot access. The cited ballot-access source predates the decision and overstated certainty.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: STRICT: assume a separate nomination petition in the name of EACH of Georgia's 16 presidential-elector candidates, each requiring 7,500 valid signatures = up to ~120,000 valid signatures total. Do NOT plan on a single 7,500-signature statewide petition. (Per-petition number 7,500 derives from Green Party of Georgia v. Kemp; the underlying statute O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(b) still nominally states 1%. West v. Wittenstein, Ga. S. Ct. S25A0178, 9/25/2024, unanimously held each elector-candidate is a 'candidate' who must file his/her own petition.) Recompute and re-verify with the SOS each cycle.
  - note: All four citations ground verbatim. But the draft value ('7,500' as the operative statewide total) is NO LONGER safe. The cited ballot-access.org 9/24 article only reported that the GA Supreme Court HEARD the case and 'oral argument went badly' — it did not report a holding, yet the draft asserted the elector-petition rule as settled. On 9/25/2024 the court ruled UNANIMOUSLY (West v. Wittenstein, affirming an ALJ and two Fulton County Superior Court judges) that West and De la Cruz were disqualified because their 16 presidential electors did not each file a separate petition; the court expressly rejected the argument that the 7,500 standard caps the requirement, and the parties/court acknowledged the strict reading implies ~120,000 signatures (16 x 7,500). Strictest defensible posture for an independent presidential run = per-elector petitions. Interpretation-dependent (court invited legislative clarification; 1% statute un-repealed).
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Nomination petition (O.C.G.A. 21-2-132(e)): file no earlier than 9:00 A.M. on the fourth Monday in June and no later than 12:00 Noon on the second Tuesday in July immediately prior to the general election. Notice of candidacy for President/VP electors (O.C.G.A. 21-2-132(d)(1)): file between 9:00 A.M. on the fourth Monday in June and 12:00 Noon on the Friday following the fourth Monday in June. DATES RECOMPUTE EACH CYCLE.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim against O.C.G.A. 21-2-132 (FindLaw, current as of 3/28/2024). Subsection (e) sets the petition window (fourth Mon June to 12:00 Noon second Tue July); (d)(1) sets the notice-of-candidacy window (fourth Mon June to 12:00 Noon Friday after fourth Mon June). Mechanical date rule, non-interpretive. The 2024 instance (July 9) is a correct illustration but is cycle-specific; rely on the statutory rule, not the hardcoded date.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No geographic distribution requirement: no per-congressional-district or per-county signature minimums. Signatures are a statewide total. Note the sheet-sorting rule (O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(d)): signers resident in different counties/municipalities must sign different sheets — an affidavit/sorting requirement, not a per-area minimum. SEPARATELY note (cross-ref signaturesRequired): post-West v. Wittenstein the petition burden is multiplied per presidential elector, which is a structural, not geographic, multiplier.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim against 21-2-170(b) and (d). It is accurate that Georgia imposes no congressional-district or county distribution minimum on the nomination petition; the only county-linked rule is the different-sheets-per-county sorting/affidavit requirement. The per-elector multiplication identified in West v. Wittenstein is captured under signaturesRequired and is not a 'distribution' requirement, so this field's value stands.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.88
  - uses: STRICT: The petition must be circulated/filed on behalf of, and in the name of, EACH presidential-elector candidate (not the presidential candidate personally) — West v. Wittenstein (Ga. S. Ct. S25A0178, decided 9/25/2024, unanimous) held a presidential candidate cannot petition for himself; the elector-candidates are the 'candidates' who must petition. Statute (21-2-170(d)) requires the circulator's sworn residence address (municipality, street, number) on each sheet; no explicit minimum-age or in-state-voter requirement is imposed on the circulator, but signers must be registered, eligible Georgia electors. A notary who served as a circulator of, or signed as an elector on, any sheet disqualifies those sheets. Confirm circulation/filing mechanics with the SOS.
  - note: Statutory quotes (circulator affidavit, signer eligibility) ground verbatim against 21-2-170. The West v. Wittenstein quote grounds verbatim against the cited ballot-access.org article — BUT that article only reported a HEARING, not a decision, and was titled 'Likely to Rule.' The draft stated the elector-petition holding as settled, which the cited source did not support. Independent verification (Georgia Recorder, 9/26/2024; corroborated by Washington Times / FOX 5) confirms the court DID rule unanimously on 9/25/2024, affirming an ALJ and two Fulton Superior Court judges, that each elector-candidate must file in his/her own name. So the draft's conclusion is now correct but for the wrong/incomplete evidentiary reason. Holding turns on the statutory meaning of 'candidate' — interpretation-dependent; the court invited legislative clarification.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Notarized circulator affidavit required on each sheet (bottom or back), subscribed and sworn before a notary public, attesting: circulator's residence address; that each signer manually signed his/her own name with full knowledge of contents; that each signature was signed within 180 days of the last filing day; and that, to the affiant's knowledge, signers are registered Georgia electors residing in the county/municipality named. No notary may sign as an elector or serve as circulator of any sheet he/she notarized — doing so disqualifies and rejects those sheets (O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(d)).
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim against 21-2-170(d). The draft's added detail (180-day window, county residence attestation) is independently supported by the same subsection's (d)(2)-(4) and (e). The notary-disqualification clause is quoted verbatim. Accurate and non-interpretive.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper (wet-ink). SOS-prescribed petition form is mandatory; each signer must manually sign and print his/her name, and each sheet must carry a notarized circulator affidavit. No remote-online/digitized signature capture is available for a Georgia independent/minor-party presidential nomination petition; collect on paper and file the bound sheets with the Secretary of State (O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(a),(d)).
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim against 21-2-170(a) and (d)(2). 'No forms other than the ones so prescribed shall be used,' combined with 'manually signed his or her own name' and the notarized-affidavit requirement, supports paper/wet-ink. No statutory authorization for electronic capture exists in the cited provisions. Non-interpretive.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: STRICT: Assume a qualifying fee IS owed at the time the notice of candidacy is filed, IN ADDITION TO (not in lieu of) the nomination-petition signatures. The SOS fixes the fee (3% of annual salary if salaried; if not salaried, a 'reasonable fee' not exceeding 3% of income) under O.C.G.A. 21-2-131(a)(2); the exact dollar amount for the presidential office is NOT confirmed from a primary source — treat as owed and confirm with the SOS. A pauper's affidavit may substitute for the FEE only, and only if accompanied by a qualifying petition signed by one-fourth of 1% of statewide registered voters (O.C.G.A. 21-2-132(g)-(h)). The fee/pauper route does NOT replace the nomination-petition signature requirement.
  - note: All three quotes ground verbatim (21-2-131(a)(2); 21-2-132(g); 21-2-132(h)(1)). The draft's structural conclusion (fee is additional; pauper's affidavit replaces only the fee and itself requires a 1/4-of-1% qualifying petition) is correct on the statute. Held conservative because: (1) the draft itself flags the exact 2024 fee amount as UNKNOWN — an unconfirmed value should not auto-go-live; (2) whether/how the fee applies to the office of presidential elector vs the presidential ticket, and its interaction with the per-elector petition structure from West v. Wittenstein, is interpretation-dependent. Confirm amount and applicability with the SOS.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent/political-body presidential candidate in 2028, after West v. Wittenstein (S25A0178), how many nomination petitions and total valid signatures does the SOS require: one statewide petition of 7,500, or a separate petition in the name of each of Georgia's 16 presidential-elector candidates (i.e. 16 x 7,500)?
  - Confirm the precise filing mechanics post-West v. Wittenstein: must each presidential-elector candidate file a nomination petition under his/her own name, and may the candidates be listed together on one petition slate under O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(c), or are separate per-elector petitions required?
  - What is the exact qualifying fee (or 'reasonable fee') the Secretary of State will fix for the office of presidential elector / President for the upcoming cycle, and is it charged per elector or per presidential ticket?
  - Confirm whether the court-imposed 7,500 per-petition standard from Green Party of Georgia v. Kemp still controls the per-petition number, or whether the un-repealed 1% statute (O.C.G.A. 21-2-170(b)) is applied to any petition the SOS now requires.

### Hawaii
- **signatures:** 5,223 sigs (1% of 522,236 — 2024 vote); recomputes each cycle
- **deadline:** Aug 9, 2028, 4:30pm (90th day before Nov 7, 2028 general)
- **risk:** Core numbers (sigs, deadline, no-distribution, fee, paper) are fully grounded and AUTO-LIVE; the two negative findings on circulators and witness/notary are statutory-silence inferences subject to the chief election officer's prescribed petition form (HRS 11-113(c)(2)(B) "other information as determined by the chief election officer"), so they are held pending confirmation of the actual form.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 5,223 signatures of currently registered Hawaii voters (1% of the 522,236 votes cast in the 2024 presidential election). Formula-based: not less than 1% of votes cast at the last presidential election; recomputes each cycle.
  - note: Grounded: OoE page states verbatim '5,223 signatures of currently registered voters' and 'In the 2024 presidential election 522,236 votes were cast'; HRS 11-113(c)(2)(B) states 'not less than one per cent of the votes cast in the State at the last presidential election.' Independently re-derived: 1% of 522,236 = 5,222.36, rounded up to 5,223 — matches OoE. Current and correct for an independent/unqualified-group presidential petition.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 4:30 p.m. on the 90th day prior to the general election (HRS 11-113(c)(2)); for the 2028 cycle, August 9, 2028, 4:30 pm per the Office of Elections.
  - note: Grounded: HRS verbatim 'not later than 4:30 p.m. on the ninetieth day prior to the general election'; OoE page verbatim 'deadline to file a presidential petition is August 9, 2028, 4:30 pm.' Independently verified: 2028 general election is Tue Nov 7, 2028; 90 days prior = Wed Aug 9, 2028 — matches the OoE date exactly. Formula recomputes each cycle.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. Single statewide total (1% of statewide presidential votes); HRS 11-113 imposes no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement.
  - note: Grounded: HRS 11-113(c)(2)(B) requires only 'signatures... which constitute not less than one per cent of the votes cast in the State' — full statutory text contains no district/county language. Ballotpedia confirms a single statewide 1% threshold. Correct negative finding.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Do not rely on 'no circulator requirements' as a planning assumption. Strictest defensible posture: signers must be currently registered Hawaii voters (confirmed by statute/OoE); for circulators, obtain and inspect the chief-election-officer-prescribed petition form before assuming no age/residency/voter-status requirement, since HRS 11-113(c)(2)(B) authorizes the CEO to add 'other information as determined.'
  - note: Grounded: Ballotpedia (state/county petitions page) verbatim 'Hawaii Revised Statutes do not address requirements for petition circulators. Specifically, there are no residency requirements for circulators'; OoE confirms signers must be registered HI voters. Adversarial: the cited Ballotpedia text addresses party-formation/fee-waiver petitions generally, not specifically the 11-113 presidential petition, and 11-113(c)(2)(B) expressly lets the CEO prescribe additional form content. Statutory silence on circulators does not foreclose a form-level requirement; retrieval cannot settle this without the actual prescribed form. Held to avoid risking ballot access.
**🟡 witnessOrNotary** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.62
  - uses: Confirmed and required: a pre-issuance notarized Declaration of Intent from each prospective candidate, plus a sworn application filed at submission. Strictest posture on the petition itself: the statute's enumerated petition contents include no per-page witness/notary, but verify the CEO-prescribed petition form for any circulator affidavit/witness attestation before assuming none.
  - note: Grounded: HRS verbatim requires 'a notarized statement from each prospective candidate of that prospective candidate's intent... Prior to being issued the petition form' and a 'sworn application'; OoE confirms the notarized Declaration of Intent. The candidate-side notarization claim is fully correct. Adversarial: the negative claim that the petition itself bears no witness/notary rests on the statute's enumerated contents (signatures, names, statement of support, address, date) — but 11-113(c)(2)(B) permits CEO-added form content, so the petition-level negative is not fully settleable by retrieval. Held pending inspection of the prescribed form.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: paper. Physical petition form prescribed and provided by the chief election officer, issued only after the notarized Declaration(s) of Intent and application are submitted. No remote_online or in_person_digitized path exists for the independent presidential petition.
  - note: Grounded: HRS verbatim 'A petition that shall be upon the form prescribed and provided by the chief election officer'; OoE verbatim 'Upon receipt of the completed application form and notarized statements of intent, the Office of Elections will issue the petition.' No statutory or OoE basis for any electronic/online signature collection for this path. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. No filing fee for the HRS 11-113 presidential petition and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for president. The HRS ch. 12 filing-fee / petition-in-lieu scheme applies to state/county nomination-paper candidates, not to the presidential petition.
  - note: Grounded: OoE 'To request a presidential petition, submit the following' lists only the application and notarized Declaration — no fee; HRS 11-113 contains no fee provision. Ballotpedia's affidavit/petition-in-lieu-of-fee quote is on the state/county political-candidates page and is expressly tied to 'the district in which the candidate is seeking election' (HRS ch. 12), confirming it does not apply to president. Correct distinction; correct negative finding.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the HRS 11-113(c)(2) presidential petition: does the chief-election-officer-prescribed petition form impose any circulator eligibility requirement (age, Hawaii residency, or voter-registration status) on the person who collects signatures?
  - For the HRS 11-113(c)(2) presidential petition: does the prescribed petition form or its instructions require any per-page circulator affidavit, witness signature, or notarization on the petition itself (separate from the pre-issuance notarized Declaration of Intent and the sworn application filed at submission)?

### Idaho
- **signatures:** 1,000 sigs statewide (flat statutory #, not %) — no distribution requirement
- **deadline:** Declaration + petition due Aug 1; sigs verified & SoS certifies by Sep 1
- **risk:** Core numbers (1,000 sigs, Aug 1 deadline, no distribution, paper wet-ink, no fee) are statutorily grounded and AUTO-LIVE; the one open question is which 34-1807 circulator rules (paid-circulator badge/disclosure, 18+) legally attach to the presidential petition vs. only its non-resident carve-out — held conservatively, confirm with SoS.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 1,000 signatures of qualified electors — a flat statewide number fixed by I.C. 34-708A(1), not a percentage formula. One petition with 1,000 signatures covers both president and vice president (treated as one office). Does not recompute per cycle.
  - note: All three quotes verified verbatim. I.C. 34-708A(1): 'a petition signed by one thousand (1,000) qualified electors'; 34-708A(2): president/VP are 'one (1) office, and only one (1) such petition need be filed.' Independently corroborated by I.C. 34-708(2)(a) ('One thousand (1,000) for any statewide office') and Ballotpedia ('At least 1,000 qualified voters'). Current as of Jan 1, 2024. No distribution/percentage element. Correct and unambiguous.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Declaration of candidacy with attached 1,000-signature petition must be filed with the Secretary of State no later than August 1 of the election year (I.C. 34-708A(1)). Signatures verified no later than September 1, and SoS certifies candidate qualifications no later than September 1 (I.C. 34-708A(3)). Date is fixed in statute, not recomputed per cycle.
  - note: Verbatim: 'must file declarations of candidacy as independent candidates no later than August 1' and 'Signatures on the petitions...shall be verified no later than September 1...The secretary of state shall certify candidate qualifications no later than September 1.' Ballotpedia agrees ('on or before August 1'). The Aug 1 filing date is the controlling, candidate-facing deadline; the two Sep 1 dates are administrative (verification + certification). Correct.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. The 1,000 signatures are a single statewide total with no geographic distribution requirement (no per-congressional-district or per-county minimums).
  - note: I.C. 34-708A(1) requires only 'a petition signed by one thousand (1,000) qualified electors' with no distribution language; 34-708 (statewide office) likewise sets a flat 1,000 with no distribution. The county-clerk certificate in 34-1807(4) references 'Legislative District Number' only as a verification/sorting mechanic — it is not a per-district quota. Adversarial check found no distribution requirement in either statute. Correct.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: For the independent presidential petition, circulators are NOT required to be Idaho residents (explicit carve-out, I.C. 34-708A(3)). STRICTEST POSTURE pending SoS confirmation: comply with the full 34-1807 circulator regime EXCEPT residency — i.e., assume circulators must be at least 18 (the incorporated affidavit form recites 'a resident of the State of Idaho and at least eighteen (18) years of age', residency waived but 18+ assumed to remain), and assume paid circulators must give the 34-1807(2) verbal/printed payment disclosure AND wear a 'paid petition circulator' badge. Signers must each be a qualified elector of Idaho and a resident of the county shown on the sheet.
  - note: Citations grounded verbatim. Adversarial finding: 34-1807's circulator-eligibility provisions are textually scoped to petitions 'for an initiative or referendum' — subsection (1) (18+/residency) and subsection (2) (paid-circulator disclosure + badge) both open with that phrase, and the void clauses (6),(8) reference 'initiative and referendum petitions.' 34-708A incorporates only the verification 'manner' and the affidavit 'form' (and explicitly waives residency). So whether the 18+ requirement and the paid-circulator badge/disclosure legally attach to a PRESIDENTIAL petition is a genuine interpretive question retrieval cannot settle. The draft asserts they do; that is plausible (the affidavit form itself recites 18+) but not certain for the badge/disclosure, which live outside the form. Held conservatively: comply with all of it (over-comply, zero ballot-access risk) and confirm with SoS.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: Notarized circulator affidavit required on each signature sheet. The verification form incorporated by I.C. 34-708A(3) (the 34-1807(3) recall-petition form) contains a sworn circulator affidavit 'Subscribed and sworn to before me...Notary Public' with a notary seal block. In addition, the county clerk examines the sheets and attaches a certificate to the SoS certifying the signers are qualified electors (34-1807(4)). Both notarized circulator certification and county-clerk verification apply.
  - note: All quotes verified verbatim. The notary requirement flows directly from the affidavit FORM, which 34-708A(3) expressly incorporates ('on a form similar to that used for recall petitions...as prescribed by the secretary of state'), so the notarization is part of the incorporated form, not the initiative/referendum-only operative provisions. County-clerk examination (34-1807(4)) is part of the incorporated verification 'manner.' This is the stricter, ballot-access-safe reading; any residual ambiguity only adds verification rigor and does not risk the ballot line. Correct.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper — wet-ink signatures only. I.C. 34-1807(7): 'Any signature that is not a physical signature, including an electronic signature, is void.' No Idaho digital/remote/online petition system exists for an independent presidential petition; the prescribed recall-style paper form with notarized circulator affidavits and county-clerk verification is the only mechanism. No remote_online or in_person_digitized capture available.
  - note: 34-1807(7) verified verbatim. Notably, subsection (7) is NOT textually limited to 'initiative or referendum' (unlike subs 1, 2, 6, 8), and 34-708A verifies 'in the manner prescribed in section 34-1807,' so the wet-ink void applies. Even on the narrowest reading, paper/wet-ink is the strict, ballot-access-safe floor and there is no online alternative for this path. Over-complying with paper carries zero risk. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.80
  - uses: None. No filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for the independent presidential/VP path. The route under I.C. 34-708A is entirely petition-based (declaration + 1,000-signature petition); the statute specifies no fee, and 34-705 (where declarations are filed with the SoS) prescribes no fee for this filing.
  - note: Both quotes verified verbatim. 34-708A specifies no fee; 34-705 ('All candidates for district, state and federal offices shall file their declarations of candidacy with the secretary of state') prescribes no fee. This is an inference from statutory silence (proving a negative), but the petition path is the exclusive mechanism and no fee or fee-in-lieu option appears anywhere in 34-708A/34-708/34-705, consistent with Ballotpedia. The operationally safe posture is identical either way: complete the petition. Correct; minor residual uncertainty reflected in confidence.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential/VP petition under I.C. 34-708A (verified per 34-1807 on the recall-petition form), do the paid-circulator disclosure and 'paid petition circulator' badge requirements of 34-1807(2), and the circulator 18-years-or-older requirement, apply to this petition — given that 34-708A waives only the Idaho-residency requirement for circulators?

### Illinois
- **signatures:** 25,000 valid sigs (1% of last statewide vote or 25,000, whichever is less; 25,000 binds — collect a large cushion)
- **deadline:** ~Late June of election year: 134 days before the general (2024 = June 24); SBE filing window 141-134 days out
- **risk:** All 7 fields citation-grounded verbatim; 6 AUTO-LIVE, 1 CONSERVATIVE-HOLD (feeAlternative — cited sources do not affirmatively state "no fee," so the absence-of-fee claim is unproven by retrieval even though IL has no known fee for this route).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 1% of the number of voters who voted in the next preceding statewide general election OR 25,000 qualified Illinois voters, whichever is less. Recomputes per cycle; because 1% of statewide turnout (~60,000 in 2024 based on ~6M turnout) vastly exceeds 25,000, the 25,000 ceiling is the binding figure and has controlled every presidential cycle for decades. Practical requirement: 25,000 valid signatures of qualified Illinois voters — collect a substantial cushion above 25,000 to survive invalidation/challenge.
  - note: FindLaw 10-3 and NASS quotes verify verbatim (NASS via PDF text extract, OCR line breaks only). Re-derived: IL 2020/2022 statewide turnout is several million, so 1% is far above 25,000 and the lesser figure (25,000) binds. Value correctly preserves the per-cycle recomputation. Strict caveat retained: 25,000 is the floor of VALID signatures; gather well above to absorb challenges.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Statutory rule: file with the Illinois State Board of Elections not less than 134 and not more than 141 days before the general election (10 ILCS 5/10-6). This computes to ~late June of the election year and RECOMPUTES each cycle. For the most recent cycle (2024 general, Nov. 5, 2024) the SBE filing window was June 17-24, 2024, with the deadline Monday, June 24, 2024 at 5:00 p.m. Do NOT reuse the June 24, 2024 date for a future cycle — re-derive from the 134/141-day rule against the specific election date.
  - note: Triple-corroborated: Ballotpedia (141/134-day quote verbatim, line 232), NASS ('no less than 134 prior' verbatim), ballot-access.org ('June 24 is the Illinois petition deadline' verbatim), and IL Candidate Guide ('Not more than 141 nor less than 134 days... 10 ILCS 5/10-6'; window 'June 17 - June 24, 2024'). Value is correct as a rule; the cycle-specific 2024 date is accurate but transient — reliedValue foregrounds the recomputing rule.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. President is a statewide/at-large office; signatures are counted 'in the aggregate' across the state with no per-congressional-district, per-county, or geographic-distribution requirement. The 5,000-per-district floor in 10 ILCS 5/10-3 applies only to district offices (e.g., congressperson after redistricting), not to the statewide presidential petition.
  - note: FindLaw 10-3 quote ('for any office to be filled by the voters of the State at large... in the aggregate') verifies verbatim. Re-derived from full statute text: the district/subdivision 5%-8% and 5,000-signature provisions are expressly tied to district/political-subdivision offices, not at-large offices. No distribution rule applies to President.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Circulator must be at least 18 (or will be 18 by the upcoming general election) and a U.S. citizen; may be from outside the district, county, or state (no Illinois residency required). A circulator may NOT mix petition types: cannot circulate for an independent candidate in addition to a new-party candidate, cannot circulate for more than one new party, and cannot circulate for an established party plus an independent/new party (10 ILCS 5/10-4; Schober v. Young, 322 Ill. App. 3d 996 (4th Dist. 2001)).
  - note: IL Candidate Guide quotes verify verbatim (guide lines 594-596: '18 years of age... can be from outside of the district, county, or state'; 'personally witness all signatures'). Mixing prohibitions confirmed at guide lines 631-648 ('A circulator may not circulate petitions for an independent candidate(s) in addition to candidates for a new political party', etc.). Out-of-state circulators are explicitly permitted by the current official guide.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Both required. The circulator must personally witness every signature and complete/sign the circulator's statement at the bottom of each sheet (certifying address, age, citizenship, and that signatures were given in their presence by registered voters); that circulator's statement must be sworn to and signed by a notary public. Separately, the candidate must swear/affirm and sign a Statement of Candidacy and have it notarized; the notarized Statement of Candidacy must accompany the nomination papers (attached at the front of the packet).
  - note: All four IL Candidate Guide quotes verify verbatim (guide line 596 'must personally witness all signatures'; line 618 'This statement shall be sworn to and signed by a notary'; lines 492-494 'must swear to or affirm... sign... have the statement notarized. The Statement of Candidacy must accompany the nomination papers'). Both the circulator certification and a separate notarization are required.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: paper. Original wet-ink signatures of voters AND the original signature of the circulator are required on physical petition sheets; photocopies or duplicates are not accepted (blank petitions may be photocopied before circulation, but the signer/circulator/notary signatures must all be original). There is NO digital, remote-online, or in-person-electronic signature system for an independent or new-party presidential petition — collection and filing are entirely paper-based with the State Board of Elections.
  - note: IL Candidate Guide quotes verify verbatim (guide line 502 'contain the original signatures of the voters and the original signature of the circulator, and shall not be photocopies or duplicates'; line 607 'Blank nomination petitions may be reproduced prior to circulation. The signatures of the signers, circulator, and the notary public must be original'). Adversarial check: no source indicates any e-signature/online option for this route; the original-signature mandate forecloses it.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Operating assumption: NO filing fee and NO fee-in-lieu-of-signatures for the independent/new-party presidential petition — ballot access is by signature petition only. This is NOT positively confirmed by the cited sources (they describe the petition requirement but do not affirmatively state that no fee exists), so it must be confirmed with the State Board before relying on it. Strict reading: treat the petition as the sole access path, budget for no fee, but verify with SBE that no fee/deposit/bond applies and confirm whether a Statement of Economic Interests is required for the federal office.
  - note: Citation integrity PASSES: both quotes (NASS petition description and FindLaw 10-3) verify verbatim. But this is a NEGATIVE claim — 'no fee exists' — and the cited quotes only describe the signature/petition requirement; neither affirmatively states the absence of a fee or fee-in-lieu. Proof-of-a-negative gap: the IL Candidate Guide contains zero references to any filing fee or dollar amount for this route (strong corroboration the value is likely correct), but retrieval cannot positively establish an absence the sources never address. Strictest defensible posture = HOLD and confirm with SBE rather than treat the no-fee claim as verified.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent (or new-party) candidate for President filing nomination papers with the State Board under 10 ILCS 5/10-3/10-4/10-6, is there ANY filing fee, filing deposit, bond, or fee-in-lieu-of-signatures, and is a Statement of Economic Interests required for the presidential (federal) office? Please confirm there is no monetary filing requirement for this route.

### Indiana
- **signatures:** IN: 2% of last SoS vote (36,943 for 2024 cycle); formula stable, integer recomputes off 2026 SoS race for 2028 — HOLD on exact number
- **deadline:** IN: two-step — county certify by noon local ~June 30, then Election Div by noon ET ~July 15 (2024 dates July 1 / July 15); dates shift each cycle — HOLD on literal dates
- **risk:** All 8 fields grounded verbatim in the official IN SoS 2024 Candidate Guide; primary risks are (a) signature count and deadline dates are 2024-cycle-specific and recompute for 2028, and (b) two inferences not stated verbatim — that the 4,500/500 rule is primary-only and that out-of-state/non-registered circulators are permitted — both held conservatively; never submit assuming non-resident circulators are safe without office confirmation.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.95
  - uses: Formula: 2% of the total votes cast for Secretary of State in the most recent SoS general election, statewide, with any fraction in excess of a whole number disregarded (IC 3-8-6-3). For the 2024 cycle this equals 36,943 (2% of 1,847,179). For 2028 this MUST be recomputed off the 2026 SoS race and is expected to differ; collect a buffer above the formula minimum.
  - note: All three primary-source quotes verified verbatim in the fresh pdftotext extraction (lines 1979-1988, 6771) and the Ballotpedia quote verified at line 244. Math checks: 0.02 x 1,847,179 = 36,943.58 -> floored to 36,943. HOLD reason: today is 2026-06-07; the literal 36,943 is the 2024-cycle figure and is NOT current for a 2028 run (recomputes off the 2026 SoS vote). Strictest defensible posture = rely on the formula, recompute when 2026 SoS totals certify, and over-collect.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.95
  - uses: Two-step statutory rule (IC 3-8-6-10; IC 3-8-6-12): (1) submit petitions to county voter registration offices for certification by 12:00 noon prevailing local time on June 30 of the election year (moves to the next business day if June 30 is a weekend); (2) file the certified petition (CAN-19) plus consent (CAN-20) with the Indiana Election Division by 12:00 noon ET on July 15. For the 2024 cycle the county deadline was noon Mon July 1, 2024 and the Election Division deadline was noon ET Mon July 15, 2024; first day to submit was Jan 10, 2024. Confirm exact 2028 dates with the Election Division.
  - note: Both primary-source quotes verified verbatim (lines 1013, 2001-2008) including the IC 3-8-6-10/-12 cites and the weekend-shift note; Ballotpedia corroborated at line 244 (county no later than noon June 30, SoS by July 15). The two-step structure and times (noon local for county, noon ET for the Division) match exactly. HOLD reason: the literal July 1 / July 15, 2024 dates are 2024-cycle-specific and not current for 2028. Note: Ballotpedia also flags a separate elector-filing deadline (2nd Tuesday in September) — that is a downstream step, not a defect in this field, but the campaign must calendar it separately.
**🟡 distributionRule** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: For an independent/minor-party PRESIDENTIAL petition of nomination there is no statutory per-county or per-congressional-district minimum stated in the guide; the requirement is the single statewide 2% aggregate. HOWEVER, because 'none' is an inference (the guide affirmatively states the 4,500/500 rule only for major-party primary candidates and is silent on any distribution rule for the petition of nomination), confirm with the Election Division before relying on a zero-distribution assumption. Operationally, geographic spread is still prudent since signatures are certified county-by-county.
  - note: Quotes grounded: the President 2%-entire-state EXAMPLE (lines 1986-1988) and the 4,500/500 text (lines 614-616). The 4,500/500 language is explicitly framed as 'Democratic or Republican candidates seeking nomination in the 2024 primary election' (lines 614, 620, 626), strongly supporting the draft's claim that it does NOT apply to petition-of-nomination candidates. But the guide never affirmatively says 'President petition of nomination has no distribution requirement' — so 'None' is a (well-supported) interpretation, not a verbatim statement. Held conservatively per the inquiry; campaign should still spread collection geographically because certification is per-county.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: Anyone may circulate a petition of nomination; the circulator (petition carrier) must complete the petition-carrier certification (signed affirmation under penalties of perjury plus printed name, address, and date of birth) on EVERY petition page before submission, or the page is rejected if not cured by the filing deadline (IC 3-8-2-7). Do NOT operationally assume out-of-state or non-registered circulators are safe until confirmed with the Election Division — the guide says 'anyone may circulate' but does not affirmatively address residency or voter-registration status.
  - note: Verbatim quote grounded at lines 759-760 ('Anyone may circulate a petition of nomination... must complete petition carrier certification on every petition form'). The draft's value is correct as to the carrier-certification requirement (IC 3-8-2-7, lines 845-847). HOLD reason: the draft extends 'anyone may circulate' to assert no residency and no voter-status restriction — that specific permission for non-residents/non-voters is an inference, not stated in the guide. Strictest defensible posture: rely on 'anyone may circulate + full carrier cert on every page' and resolve the residency question with the office before deploying out-of-state circulators.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: No notarization. A petition carrier (circulator) certification is required instead: the carrier must complete and sign, on each signature page, an affirmation under penalties of perjury that they have no reason to believe any signer is ineligible, with the carrier's printed name, address, and date of birth (IC 3-8-2-7). Signatures are separately validated by the county voter registration office. An incomplete carrier affidavit causes the page to be rejected if not cured by the filing deadline.
  - note: Both quotes verified verbatim: the per-page affirmation-under-penalty-of-perjury with name/address/DOB and IC 3-8-2-7 cite (lines 845-847), and 'A petition carrier is required to fully complete and affix their signature to the affidavit at the bottom of each page' (line 1862 and 7 other occurrences). No notarization requirement appears anywhere in the guide. Value is current and correct; no cycle dependence.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: Paper only. Indiana requires original wet-ink signatures on the paper CAN-19 petition of nomination; photocopies, electronic, digital, and digitized signatures are all rejected (IC 3-5-4-1.7(b)). There is no online/digital petition system for an independent presidential petition; the process is paper end-to-end with county certification and physical filing with the Election Division.
  - note: Quote verified verbatim at line 755 ('photocopies of signatures, electronic signatures, digital signatures, or digitized signatures will not be accepted. (IC 3-5-4-1.7(b))'). Confirms a strict wet-signature paper regime. Value is current and correct; no cycle dependence.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. Indiana provides no filing-fee option in lieu of (or in addition to) the petition signatures for an independent or minor-party presidential candidate; ballot access is by petition of nomination only.
  - note: Quote verified verbatim at line 344 ('A minor party (other than the Libertarian Party), or independent candidate in Indiana is nominated for placement on the general election ballot by petition of nomination'). Adversarial check confirmed: the only 'fee' anywhere in the 153-page guide is an unrelated photocopying fee (line 3423), and 'in lieu' appears nowhere — so there is no fee alternative. Value is current and correct.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent/minor-party presidential petition of nomination (CAN-19), may the petition carrier be a non-Indiana resident and/or a person who is not a registered Indiana voter, provided the carrier completes the petition-carrier certification (name, address, DOB) on every page per IC 3-8-2-7?
  - Please confirm that the 4,500-signature / 500-per-congressional-district requirement applies ONLY to major-party (Democratic/Republican) primary candidates for President, and that an independent/minor-party presidential petition of nomination has NO per-county or per-congressional-district distribution minimum — only the statewide 2% aggregate.
  - For the 2028 presidential cycle, what is the certified signature requirement (2% of the 2026 Secretary of State vote) and the exact county-certification and Election Division filing deadlines?

### Iowa
- **signatures:** 3,500 signatures (flat statutory; not a %) + 100 each from 19 counties — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** 5:00 p.m. on 81st day before Nov general election (2024 = Aug 16, 2024) — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** Core petition burden (3,500 sigs, 19-county floor, 81-day deadline, notarized affidavit, paper-only) is fully grounded in Iowa Code 45.1/44.4/45.5 and AUTO-LIVE. Two fields held conservatively: circulator-eligibility (relying on a complete ABSENCE of circulator rules is a negative inference not provable by retrieval; sub-regulatory IAC ch. 721 rules not pulled) and the NPPO convention alternative (the "one attendee per county"/"true independents have no convention option" claims rest on Ballotpedia + un-retrieved Iowa Code ch. 44 classification). Strict posture: rely on the petition route only; never treat the convention as a shortcut.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 3,500 signatures of eligible electors — a flat statutory minimum (not a percentage; does not recompute per cycle), including at least 100 eligible electors each from at least 19 counties (embedded distribution floor). Iowa Code 45.1(1). Same number applies to the unaffiliated 'Nominated by Petition' candidate and to an NPPO candidate using the petition route (45.4 routes petition candidates through ch. 45).
  - note: 45.1(1) verbatim: 'not less than three thousand five hundred eligible electors, including at least one hundred eligible electors each from at least nineteen counties of the state.' Confirmed a flat number, not a percentage, in the statute itself; current (last amended 2022; 2021 amendment to subsec.1 applies to ballots in/after 2022). Ballotpedia corroborates. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 5:00 p.m. on the 81st day before the November general election; earliest filing = 99 days before. For 2024 (Nov 5, 2024): deadline 5:00 p.m. Aug 16, 2024, filing window opened July 29, 2024. Iowa Code 44.4(1)(b), incorporated for petition candidates by 45.4. Recomputes each cycle.
  - note: 44.4(1)(b) verbatim: '...not more than ninety-nine days nor later than 5:00 p.m. on the eighty-first day before the date of the general election to be held in November.' 45.4 incorporation verbatim. Date arithmetic independently verified: Nov 5, 2024 - 81 days = Aug 16, 2024; -99 days = July 29, 2024; Nov 5 2024 is a Tuesday. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: Yes — county distribution requirement: at least 100 eligible electors EACH from at least 19 counties (a subset of the 3,500 total). Stated by county, not by congressional district. Iowa Code 45.1(1).
  - note: 45.1(1) verbatim: 'including at least one hundred eligible electors each from at least nineteen counties of the state.' By county, not district — confirmed. Ballotpedia corroborates. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: Requirements fall on SIGNERS, who must each be an 'eligible elector': U.S. citizen, Iowa resident, at least 17 (must be 18 by Election Day), need not be a registered voter but must meet all qualifications to register; not a disqualified felon, not judged incompetent to vote, not claiming the right to vote elsewhere. Any eligible elector in Iowa may sign for a statewide/presidential office. STRICT HOLD on the asserted COMPLETE ABSENCE of any circulator requirement/attestation — do not operationally assume zero circulator rules until the SOS confirms (see sosInquiries).
  - note: Signer-eligibility facts ground verbatim on the SOS candidate FAQ (citizen/resident/17-must-be-18; 'not required to be a registered voter'; statewide-office signing). However, the claim that there is NO circulator age/residency/voter-status requirement and NO attestation step is a negative inference: chapter 45 and the FAQ do not affirmatively foreclose a sub-regulatory rule (IAC ch. 721 not retrieved). Per strict 'never risk ballot access' posture, HOLD the no-circulator-rules conclusion pending SOS confirmation; the signer facts themselves are reliable.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Petition pages are NOT notarized and need no circulator/witness certification. The candidate's affidavit of candidacy MUST be notarized — nomination papers are rejected if the affidavit lacks the signature of a notary public under ch. 9B (or other officer empowered to witness oaths). Each signature line must include the signer's signature and residential address (street, number, city) to be counted; no per-signature witnessing required. Iowa Code 45.5(2)(c),(5)(d); SOS FAQ.
  - note: SOS FAQ verbatim: 'A candidate's affidavit of candidacy must be notarized. Nomination petitions do not need to be notarized.' 45.5(5)(d) verbatim on notary requirement; 45.5(2)(c) verbatim on signature+residential-address counting rule. Consistent and current. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Wet-ink paper petitions (8.5 x 11 inch pages, securely bound into a single bundle; unbound petitions returned without examination) plus a paper notarized affidavit of candidacy, filed with the Secretary of State. No online/remote-signature system for an independent/NPPO presidential petition. Iowa Code 45.5(1),(3); SOS lists the paper President/VP nomination petition PDF.
  - note: 45.5(1) verbatim ('eight and one-half by eleven inches...substantially the form prescribed') and 45.5(3) verbatim ('securely fastened together to form a single bundle. Nomination petitions that are not bound shall be returned without further examination'). SOS nomination-papers page lists the paper 'Nomination Petition-President & Vice President' PDF under General Election. Chapter 45 has no e-signature provision; physical bound-bundle requirement forecloses remote capture. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: No filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option — the 3,500-signature/19-county petition is the mandatory, SAFE route for the unaffiliated presidential candidate; rely on it exclusively. Do NOT rely on a convention/caucus alternative as an available shortcut: the claim that an NPPO may instead convene (>=500 electors, one attendee per county, certificate filed by the 81st-day deadline) and that a 'Nominated by Petition' unaffiliated candidate has NO convention option rests on Ballotpedia plus un-retrieved Iowa Code ch. 44 and is a legal-classification interpretation (see sosInquiries).
  - note: No-fee part grounds verbatim (SOS FAQ: 'There are no candidate filing fees in Iowa') and is reliable. Convention details ground verbatim on Ballotpedia ('At least 500 eligible voters must attend... at least one attendee from each of the state's counties') but NOT on the retrieved SOS FAQ, which states only that NPPOs may nominate by convention without the 500/per-county specifics. The '>=1 attendee per county' = all 99 counties is an extreme, un-statute-confirmed bar, and the categorical 'true independents have no convention option' is a legal classification not settled by retrieval (ch. 44 not pulled). HOLD: rely solely on the petition route, which is the strictest/safest posture.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Re circulators: For an independent/NPPO presidential nomination petition under Iowa Code ch. 45, is there ANY requirement or attestation imposed on the person who circulates the petition (age, Iowa residency, voter-registration status, or a circulator oath/affidavit), whether in statute or in the Iowa Administrative Code (e.g., IAC ch. 721)? Please confirm there are no circulator requirements beyond each signer being an eligible elector.
  - Re NPPO/independent classification: Can a candidate with NO party or NPPO affiliation (a 'Nominated by Petition' candidate) for President/VP qualify by convention/caucus under Iowa Code ch. 44, or is the 3,500-signature/19-county petition the ONLY available route for a truly unaffiliated candidate? Separately, for an NPPO convention nomination, please confirm the exact attendance requirements (minimum total electors and whether at least one attendee is required from each of all 99 counties) and the filing deadline for the certificate of nomination.

### Kansas
- **signatures:** 5,000 valid signatures (flat statewide, no distribution) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** 12:00 noon Monday before the Aug primary; recomputes each even year (2024: Aug 5, 2024) — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** Signature count, deadline, paper capture, and no-fee-substitute are solid and AUTO-LIVE; the residual risk is in execution rules (per-sheet county collation under 25-303(f), whether the circulator "affidavit" must be notarized, and circulator qualifications) — all held conservatively pending SOS confirmation. Note 2026 is a midterm with no presidential race, so the live presidential deadline must be recomputed for the next presidential even year (e.g., 2028).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 5,000 signatures of qualified (registered) Kansas voters. President is a state-at-large office, so the flat statewide threshold under K.S.A. 25-303(c) applies. Fixed statutory number, not a percentage; does not recompute by cycle. No district/county distribution required.
  - note: Grounded verbatim in K.S.A. 25-303(c) ('any office to be filled by the voters of the state at large... not less than 5,000 qualified voters') and Ballotpedia's 2024 presidential page ('At least 5,000 qualified voters must sign the petition'). Adversarial check: 25-303(d)'s 4% formula and the 25 / 5,000 floor-and-cap apply only to sub-state offices, not to a state-at-large office; the 5,000 figure is fixed in statute and does not recompute. Re-derived independently and could not refute.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: 12:00 noon on the Monday preceding the August primary (K.S.A. 25-305(b)); primary is the first Tuesday of August in even-numbered years (K.S.A. 25-203). For the most recent presidential cycle (2024): primary Tue Aug 6, 2024 → independent nomination petition deadline 12:00 noon Mon Aug 5, 2024. Recomputes each even year (SOS lists 12:00 p.m. Mon Aug 3, 2026 for the 2026 non-presidential cycle). Filed with the Secretary of State for national office.
  - note: Grounded verbatim: 25-305(b) (independent nomination petitions due 'no later than 12:00 noon on the Monday preceding the date fixed for the holding of primary elections in accordance with K.S.A. 25-203'); 25-203 (primary 'first Tuesday of August in even-numbered years'); SOS page ('Independent Nominations: 12:00 p.m. Monday, August 3, 2026'). Adversarial check: President is a national office and 25-305(b) covers 'national... offices' with no presidential petition carve-out (25-305(d) carves out only WRITE-IN candidacy, not petitions), so the August deadline governs. Date arithmetic confirmed (Aug 2024 first Tuesday = Aug 6; Monday preceding = Aug 5). Value is cycle-dependent and the draft flags this; for the next presidential year (2028) the date must be recomputed. AUTO-LIVE for the cited 2024 value with the recompute caveat preserved.
**🟡 distributionRule** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: No per-district or per-county signature-distribution quota: the 5,000 signatures for a state-at-large office (25-303(c)) form a single statewide pool, and 25-303(d)'s per-division percentage applies only to sub-state offices. HOWEVER, K.S.A. 25-303(f) requires that all signers appearing on any single petition sheet reside in the same county and election district of the office sought. Strictest operational reading: organize/collate petition sheets by county so no sheet mixes signers from different counties. Confirm sheet-collation requirement with the SOS before circulating.
  - note: Both quotes grounded verbatim in 25-303. The 'no distribution quota' conclusion is correct and well supported (25-303(c) is a flat statewide number). But 25-303(f)'s same-county/same-election-district per-sheet rule is a genuine operational constraint whose application to a state-at-large petition (the 'election district' being the whole state, yet the 'same county' limit still binding per sheet) is an interpretation retrieval cannot fully settle. Held conservatively (collate by county) to avoid a defective-petition / signature-invalidation risk. SOS inquiry filed.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Statute (K.S.A. 25-303(f)) is silent on circulator age/residency/registration; it requires only that the candidate or 'petition circulator' personally witness each signature and append a signed verification. Because this is an unverifiable negative (an SOS rule or official form could impose qualifications not in the statute), do not rely on 'anyone may circulate.' Strictest defensible posture: have the candidate or a qualified, registered Kansas elector circulate and personally witness every signature, and confirm circulator qualifications with the SOS before deploying volunteers.
  - note: Quote grounded verbatim in 25-303(f). The asserted value is the ABSENCE of a statutory circulator qualification — a negative that retrieval cannot conclusively establish (no SOS administrative rule was located confirming the absence). Defaulting to the strictest interpretation per the over-comply mandate; held pending SOS confirmation rather than published as AUTO-LIVE. SOS inquiry filed.
**🟡 witnessOrNotary** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: A circulator/candidate verification must be appended to each set of petition documents (K.S.A. 25-303(f)) attesting the circulator/candidate personally witnessed every signature. The statute uses the word 'affidavit,' which ordinarily implies a sworn instrument. Strictest defensible reading: treat it as a sworn affidavit and have it notarized (or execute it on the official SOS petition form exactly as prescribed) rather than assume a bare unsworn signature suffices. Confirm notarization requirement and form with the SOS.
  - note: Quote grounded verbatim. The draft concludes 'NOT notarization,' but 25-303(f) expressly calls it 'The affidavit of the candidate or a petition circulator' even while the operative clause requires only a signed verification. 'Affidavit' vs. 'signed verification' is precisely a legal-interpretation conflict retrieval cannot settle, and getting it wrong (unsworn where sworn is required) risks petition rejection. Over-comply: assume notarization may be required; hold and verify with SOS. SOS inquiry filed.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Independent nomination petitions are physical papers carried by circulators; each registered-voter signer must add place of residence and post office address, with a circulator/candidate verification appended to each set. No Kansas online/digital petition system covers an independent presidential nominating petition; petitions are filed in paper form with the Secretary of State.
  - note: Grounded verbatim in 25-303(f) ('signatures... need not all be appended to one paper, but each registered voter signing... shall add... place of residence and post office address'). Statute plainly contemplates physical papers carried by circulators; no statutory or SOS digital-petition pathway exists for this petition type. Re-derived and could not refute. Note: this fixes COLLECTION mode as paper; it does not bear on the circulator-verification execution questions above.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. There is no filing fee that substitutes for signatures for an independent candidate; the valid nominating petition is the only route onto the general-election ballot, and the GEC/SOS fee is paid in addition to (not in lieu of) the petition. The party-primary 'petition OR filing fee' option does not extend to independent candidates.
  - note: Both quotes grounded verbatim on the SOS candidate-information page ('Independent candidates do not run in the primary and may only file to run for office by petition'; footnote 1: 'Independent candidates may file for office only by petition. Upon filing a valid petition and paying the GEC/SOS fee, the candidate's name will be placed directly on the general ballot...'). Adversarial check: the page's general line 'Candidates must file by petition or filing fee' is the party-primary option; the independent-specific footnote confirms petition is mandatory and the fee is additive, not a substitute. Correct and current; AUTO-LIVE.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For a statewide (state-at-large) independent presidential nomination petition under K.S.A. 25-303, does the per-sheet rule in 25-303(f) (all signers on one sheet must reside in the same county and election district of the office sought) require that petition sheets be collated/organized by county, and is there any minimum-per-county or per-congressional-district distribution of the 5,000 signatures?
  - For an independent presidential nomination petition, does the circulator/candidate 'affidavit' required by K.S.A. 25-303(f) have to be sworn and notarized, or does a signed verification without a notary satisfy the statute? Is there an official SOS petition form that prescribes the verification format?
  - Does Kansas impose any qualifications on a petition circulator for an independent nomination petition (e.g., age, Kansas residency, voter registration, or party-affiliation status), beyond the requirement that the circulator or candidate personally witness each signature under K.S.A. 25-303(f)?

### Kentucky
- **signatures:** 5,000 registered voters statewide (no distribution) + $500 fee, both required — KRS 118.315
- **deadline:** File by Fri after 1st Tue in Sept = Sep 8, 2028, 4:00 p.m. local (earliest affix/file Nov 3, 2027)
- **risk:** All 8 fields grounded against primary sources (KRS 118.315, KRS 118.365, SOS 2028 President/Independent packet); quotes verbatim. Adversarial check cleared the KRS 118.591(1) cross-reference in current 118.315(2): 118.591 governs the presidential PREFERENCE PRIMARY petition (party path), NOT the independent general-election petition — no conflict. Two HOLDs are conservative-only (negative inferences about circulator rules / conditional notarization guideline), not refutations; substantive values stand.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 5,000 registered voters statewide. Independent (or political group/organization) presidential ticket files a Nominating Petition (SBE 64 / SBE 64-2) under KRS 118.315, signed by the candidates for President and Vice President and a minimum of 5,000 registered voters (KRS 118.315(2): 5,000 petitioners for an office for which all electors of the state are entitled to vote). Each petitioner must include signature-affixation date, date of birth, and residence address (not a P.O. box); omission of any voids that signature. Signatures may not be affixed before the first Wednesday after the first Monday in November of the year preceding the election (Nov. 3, 2027 for the 2028 cycle).
  - note: KRS 118.315(2) verbatim: '...shall contain five thousand (5,000) petitioners' for statewide office; SOS 2028 packet verbatim confirms '5,000 registered voters' and affix date Nov 3, 2027. Statute is current (eff. June 27, 2025). Adversarial: the new 118.315(2) carve-out 'excluding President of the United States in accordance with KRS 118.591(1)' refers ONLY to the presidential-preference-PRIMARY petition (party endorsement path under KRS 118.591) — it does not alter the independent general-election count. Verified by reading KRS 118.591 in full.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Not later than the Friday following the first Tuesday in September preceding the election, by 4:00 p.m. local time. For 2028 = September 8, 2028, 4:00 p.m. local time. Earliest date to file (and to affix signatures) = first Wednesday after first Monday in November of the prior year = November 3, 2027. Statutory basis: KRS 118.365(6) (window) and KRS 118.365(8) (4 p.m. cutoff). Recomputes each cycle.
  - note: KRS 118.365(6) and (8) verbatim-grounded. Independently re-derived 2028: first Tuesday in Sept 2028 = Sept 5; Friday following = Sept 8, 2028 — matches the SOS 2028 packet's stated 'September 8, 2028' (4:00 p.m. local). No interpretation; arithmetic, statute, and official packet all agree.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. The 5,000 signatures are a single statewide total with no geographic distribution (no per-congressional-district or per-county quota). Petition is for an office 'for whom all the electors of the state are entitled to vote'; signers are 'voters of the same district or jurisdiction from which the candidates seek nomination' (the whole state).
  - note: KRS 118.315(2) sets one flat 5,000 statewide number for statewide office and lists no distribution requirement; SOS petition form's 'undersigned petitioners' clause verbatim confirms a single statewide pool. No distribution language anywhere in the statute or form.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICT: Each signer must be a Kentucky registered voter from the jurisdiction (the state) and must personally list the signature date, date of birth, and a residential address that is NOT a P.O. box; omission of any of these voids that signature (KRS 118.315(2)). Candidates must not be registered members of a political party, and must not have been registered party members on January 1 immediately preceding the election. Do NOT rely on any assumption that a person who merely collects signatures is free of residency/age/registration constraints until confirmed with the State Board of Elections, since that is an absence-of-law inference not settled by retrieval.
  - note: Core signer-eligibility and candidate-party-disaffiliation facts are verbatim-grounded (KRS 118.315(1)-(2)) and correct. HOLD is conservative-only: the draft's claim that 'no statutory age or residency rule is imposed on a person who merely collects signatures' is a negative inference (no circulator block on SBE 64/64-2, no statute found), which retrieval cannot conclusively settle vs. a possible SBE administrative regulation. Over-comply: do not promise an unrestricted out-of-state circulator without SBE confirmation. Inquiry filed.

  - uses: STRICT: No notary/witness affidavit and no per-petition circulator certification appears on the SBE 64 / SBE 64-2 petition; the only sworn element is the candidates' declaration that they possess the constitutional and statutory qualifications (KRS 118.315(2); declaration on the form). ### Louisiana
- **signatures:** 5,000 sigs / 500 per CD (SoS standard; bare statute reads 2,500/250 — collect 5,000/500)
- **deadline:** File 3rd Tue Jul–1st Fri after 3rd Tue Aug (2024: Jul 16–Aug 23); petition to registrars by Jul 24 (T-30)
- **risk:** Signature/distribution count is a statute-vs-agency conflict: RS 18:465(C)(1) literally says 2,500/250 for statewide candidates, but the SoS packet and NASS both say 5,000/500 for the presidential independent slate — collect 5,000/500 (strictest) to avoid rejection. Fee changed $500 (2024 packet) -> $1,000 (current statute); confirm operative fee/dates with SoS each cycle, and the petition path is always available as a fee-free alternative.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: 5,000 signatures of registered voters, with at least 500 from each of Louisiana's 6 congressional districts (collect to this higher standard).
  - note: Citations grounded verbatim (SoS packet + NASS both say 5,000/500). BUT the draft's legal derivation is wrong: RS 18:465(C)(1) — the cross-referenced statewide provision RS 18:1254(B) routes independents into — actually reads 'two thousand five hundred, not less than two hundred fifty of which shall be from each of the congressional districts' (verified at codes.findlaw.com/la, current as of 2023-01-01). So the bare statute yields 2,500/250, not 5,000/500. This is a statute-vs-administering-agency conflict that retrieval cannot settle. Strictest defensible value = 5,000/500 (the SoS's own published, administered standard, which also moots the lower reading), so relied value = 5,000/500. Do NOT rely on 2,500/250.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85

Treat July-24-type certification cutoff as the binding earliest deadline and re-confirm exact cycle dates with the SoS.

### Maine
- **signatures:** 4,000-5,000 registered Maine voters (presidential-elector slate); any Maine voter may sign; no distribution rule — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** CONSERVATIVE-HOLD: statute says July 25 cert / Aug 1 SOS for presidential electors, but Ballotpedia says May 25 / June 1 — treat EARLIER dates (May 25 / June 1) as the safe-harbor; signing not before Jan 1
- **risk:** Two genuine interpretation risks need SOS confirmation before relying live: (1) the presidential-elector filing deadline (statute carve-out July 25/Aug 1 vs. Ballotpedia's May 25/June 1 for independents) — file by the earlier dates to be safe; (2) circulator eligibility (statute is silent, so do not assume non-resident/non-voter circulators are allowed — use Maine resident registered voters). All seven citations grounded verbatim; 2028 is the next presidential year (the 2026 SOS guide is a non-presidential midterm and omits the elector deadlines/figures, so the statute controls).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: At least 4,000 and not more than 5,000 registered Maine voters for the slate of presidential electors (21-A MRS sec 354(5)(A)); petitions for presidential electors may be signed by any Maine voter statewide (sec 354(2)). Flat statutory range, not a percentage of turnout.
  - note: Grounded verbatim at sec 354(5)(A) ('For a slate of candidates for the office of presidential elector, at least 4,000 and not more than 5,000 voters') and sec 354(2) ('except that nomination petitions for presidential electors may be signed by any Maine voter'); Ballotpedia quote also present verbatim. Current per PL 2021 c.273. Independently re-derived from the controlling statute; no refutation found. The 2026 SOS Candidate's Guide omits presidential electors because 2026 is a non-presidential midterm, so the statute is the controlling source for the figure.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.55
  - uses: STRICTEST/SAFE-HARBOR: deliver petitions to the municipal registrar for certification by 5 p.m. on May 25 and file with the Secretary of State by 5 p.m. on June 1 of the election year (the earlier of the two conflicting authorities — meeting these also satisfies the statute's later presidential-elector dates). Signatures may not be collected before January 1 of the election year (sec 354(6)). The statute (sec 354(7)(B), (8-A)) on its face provides a later presidential-elector carve-out of July 25 cert / August 1 SOS filing, but DO NOT rely on the later dates without SOS written confirmation.
  - note: All three statutory quotes grounded verbatim: sec 354(7)(B) July 25 carve-out, sec 354(8-A) August 1 carve-out, sec 354(6) Jan 1 signing floor. ADVERSARIAL CONFLICT: Ballotpedia's general-election 'Independent candidates' section states for an independent presidential candidate that signatures go to registrars by 5 p.m. May 25 and to the SOS by 5 p.m. June 1 — directly contradicting the draft's July 25/Aug 1. The statute is controlling and its carve-out expressly names 'a slate of candidates for the office of presidential elector,' which matches this access path, so the draft's legal reading is likely correct. But which deadline a candidate must actually meet hinges on a legal interpretation (whether the sec 354 presidential-elector carve-out governs the independent presidential petition), the 2026 SOS guide is silent (non-presidential year), and the downside of error is loss of ballot access — so under strictest-interpretation rules the relied value is the earlier safe-harbor date, pending SOS confirmation. Jan 1 signing floor is clean.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95

**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICTEST: do not assume non-resident or non-registered-voter circulators are permitted. Safest practice is to use circulators who are Maine residents AND registered Maine voters. The statute (sec 354(7)(A)) affirmatively requires only that the circulator personally witness all signatures and swear the notarized oath; it imposes no express age/residency/voter requirement, and Ballotpedia states the circulator need not be a Maine resident — but this is a negative inference from statutory silence and should be confirmed with the SOS before relying on out-of-state or non-voter circulators.
  - note: Grounded verbatim: Ballotpedia 'The petition circulator does not have to be a Maine resident...' and sec 354(7)(A) oath language both present. The draft's claim that NO residency/voter requirement applies rests on statutory silence (sec 354 does not affirmatively state circulators may be non-voters; it simply omits the requirement) plus a contrast with the sec 903-A initiative rule. That negative inference is a legal interpretation retrieval cannot conclusively settle, and a wrong assumption can void every signature a disqualified circulator collected. Ballotpedia supports the non-residency reading, but under strictest-interpretation + catastrophic-downside this is a CONSERVATIVE-HOLD pending SOS confirmation.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Notarized circulator certification required: each nomination petition must carry the circulator's oath/affirmation before a notary public (or other authorized officer) that the circulator personally witnessed all signatures and that each signature is genuine and each signer resides in the named electoral division (21-A MRS sec 354(7)(A)). Separately, the candidate's consent must be sworn before a notary (sec 355(3)).
  - note: Grounded verbatim at sec 354(7)(A) (circulator oath before a notary) and sec 355(3) ('The candidate must verify by oath or affirmation before a notary public... that the declaration is true'). Independently confirmed from primary text; both a circulator notarization and a candidate-consent notarization are required. No refutation.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: paper / in-person (wet-ink). No online/remote or digitized signature-collection system exists for candidate nomination petitions.
  - note: Grounded verbatim: sec 354 'A nomination petition shall be on a form provided by the Secretary of State'; sec 354(3) personal-signature language; and the SOS 'Becoming a Candidate' page 'Petitions must be printed double-sided on 8.5 x 14 inch (legal size) paper.' **🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90

This is a negative finding from the controlling qualifying statute, which lists only petition + consent and references no fee; sec 354/355 likewise reference no fee. A fee alternative either exists in statute or it does not — it does not — so this is a factual negative, not a contestable legal interpretation. ### Maryland
- **signatures:** 10,000 valid signatures statewide (firm cap; the lesser-of-10,000-or-1% formula resolves to the 10,000 ceiling for President) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** Declaration of Intent by 1st Mon in July; Certificate of Candidacy + petition by 5pm 1st Mon in Aug (Aug 5, 2024 last cycle); electors certified ≥30 days pre-election — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** 6 of 7 fields AUTO-LIVE on grounded primary sources (EL 5-703, 6-201/203/204, 8-502/503, 4-102, SBE pages). Sole hold: circulatorEligibility — the negative claim that out-of-state/non-registered circulators are permitted is literally accurate in statute and COMAR but is a litigated, risk-bearing point; over-comply by using MD-registered-voter circulators pending SBE confirmation.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 10,000 valid statewide signatures. Statutory formula: lesser of 10,000 registered voters OR 1% of registered voters eligible to vote for the office, floor of 250; for President (statewide) 1% far exceeds 10,000, so the binding number is the 10,000 cap. Count fixed as of January 1 of the primary-election year. New-party path under EL 4-102 is also 10,000.
  - note: All 4 citations verbatim: EL 5-703(e)(1) lesser-of-10,000-or-1%/250 floor; EL 5-703(e)(3) Jan 1 of primary year; SBE candidacy page explicitly states 10,000 for unaffiliated statewide candidates; Ballotpedia corroborates. President-is-statewide so cap binds is settled by SBE's own published guidance, not a contested interpretation. EL 4-102(b)(2)(i) confirms new-party 10,000.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Two statutory deadlines: (1) Declaration of Intent not later than the first Monday in July of the general-election year; (2) Certificate of Candidacy AND completed nomination petition by 5 p.m. on the first Monday in August. For President, the slate of presidential electors must be certified to the State Board at least 30 days before the general election. 2024 first Monday in August = Aug 5, 2024 (verified).
  - note: EL 5-703(c)(3)(i), 5-703(d)(1), 5-703(f)(1), and 8-503(c)(3) all verbatim. SBE 2026 candidacy page corroborates (Declaration July 6, 2026; second deadline Aug 3, 2026). **🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. The unaffiliated/independent presidential 10,000-signature petition is statewide with no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution quota. The 400-signatures-per-congressional-district rule (EL 8-502) applies only to the principal-party PRIMARY ballot, not the independent general-election route.

**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: Circulator must be at least 18 years old when any covered signature is affixed and must be the person in whose presence each signature was affixed and who observed each signing (EL 6-204). STRICTEST DEFENSIBLE POSTURE: although neither EL 6-204 nor COMAR 33.06.03.07/.08 textually requires the circulator to be a Maryland registered voter or resident, treat circulators as Maryland registered voters (and require their MD residence address per COMAR 33.06.03.07) to eliminate any residency-challenge risk to the ballot line, pending SBE confirmation. Each SIGNER must be a registered voter assigned to the county on the signature page (EL 6-203(b)(2)).
  - note: Affirmative claims grounded and correct: EL 6-204(c) 18+ verbatim; 6-204(a) observe-each-signature verbatim; 6-203(b)(2) signer county-registration verbatim. COMAR 33.06.03.07 requires the circulator's residence address; COMAR 33.06.03.08 requires the affidavit to attest signers are registered voters in the State — neither imposes a circulator residency/registration requirement. The draft's NEGATIVE claim (out-of-state/non-registered circulators allowed) is literally accurate but is a heavily litigated point nationally and SBE practice on out-of-state circulators is not settled by retrieved text; under never-risk-ballot-access this requires SBE confirmation, hence HOLD.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Circulator affidavit (NOT notarized). Each signature page must carry an affidavit executed by the circulator who personally observed every signature on that page being affixed; a signature is validated and counted only if attested by that affidavit. No notary is required for petition signature pages. (The Certificate of Candidacy and Financial Disclosure are notarized for state office, but President has no financial-disclosure requirement.)
  - note: EL 6-203(b)(4) (attested by affidavit on the page), 6-201(c)(6) (space for circulator affidavit), 6-204(b) (affidavit contents by regulation) all verbatim. ### Massachusetts
- **signatures:** 10,000 certified voter signatures, statewide aggregate (fixed by statute, no distribution quota) — AUTO-LIVE
