**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 10,000 certified voter signatures, statewide aggregate. Fixed by statute (M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 6 lists 'presidential electors, ten thousand'); not a recomputed percentage. An independent ('Unenrolled') presidential candidate qualifies by filing nomination papers for a slate of presidential electors carrying 10,000 certified signatures. Practitioner guidance: collect well above 10,000 because registrars disqualify non-matching signatures; sec. 7 lets registrars certify the required number increased by two-fifths.
  - note: Verbatim in M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 6 ('signed in the aggregate by not less than the following number of voters: for governor and lieutenant governor, attorney general, United States senator, and presidential electors, ten thousand'). Cross-confirmed by Ballotpedia ('At least 10,000 voters must sign this petition') and its historical table (1992-2012 all 10,000, 'Fixed by statute'). The two-fifths language is verbatim in sec. 7. Adversarial check: legal minimum to QUALIFY is 10,000 certified; the +two-fifths is a registrar certification cap / over-collection mechanic, correctly framed as guidance. Current and correct.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Final filing with the Secretary of the Commonwealth: on or before the LAST TUESDAY IN AUGUST of the presidential-election year, by 5:00 p.m. (M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 10) — this part is solid. STRICTEST local-submission read (over-comply): submit signed nomination papers to local registrars no later than the 28th day before the SOS final filing date, by 5:00 p.m., and ensure local certification is COMPLETE no later than the 7th day before final filing (M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 7 state-office schedule). Treat the earliest applicable date as binding until the SOS confirms which sub-schedule (28-day vs 14-day) governs the presidential-elector petition. Do NOT rely on 'August 20' as a 28-day submission deadline — that date is the 7-day certification mark, not the submission deadline.
  - note: All citations ground verbatim (sec. 10 'last Tuesday in August'; sec. 10 'before five o'clock'; sec. 7 '28th day... seventh day'; Ballotpedia '14th day preceding'; Ballotpedia table '...8/27/2024'). BUT the draft's value is internally inconsistent: it says local submission is 'at least 28 days before' the SOS filing AND that 'For 2024 the local-submission deadline was August 20, 2024' — arithmetically Aug 20 is exactly 7 days before Aug 27 (the 7-day CERTIFICATION mark), not 28 days (which is July 30). Sources also conflict on the submission window: sec. 7 says 28th day for a 'state office,' while Ballotpedia says the 14th day for the presidential petition. Whether the sec. 7 state-office 28/7 schedule even applies to a presidential-elector paper (filed separately under sec. 10) is a legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle. Held; reliedValue set to the strictest (earliest) defensible submission window.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. The 10,000 requirement is a single statewide aggregate ('signed in the aggregate by not less than ... ten thousand'). No per-congressional-district or per-county minimum. Signatures are collected per-city/town only procedurally (each local board certifies only its own voters; signatures from more than one city or town may not appear on the same sheet), but no geographic distribution quota applies.
  - note: Verbatim sec. 6 ('in the aggregate') and sec. 7 ('Signatures shall not be certified ... from more than one city or town per sheet'). Independently confirmed by the 2026 SOS Candidates Guide: 'You do not, however, need to gather signatures from every city and town in your district, or from a certain number of communities in your district.' No distribution requirement exists. Correct and current.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: Massachusetts imposes no statutory eligibility requirement (age/residency/voter-status) on the CIRCULATOR of a nomination paper, and no circulator-registration or circulator-affidavit. The binding constraints are on the SIGNERS: each must be a MA registered voter, signing in person their own name substantially as registered, with their registered address. For a non-party ('Unenrolled') candidate, signatures may be gathered from ANY registered voter (no party-affiliation restriction). A voter physically unable to write may authorize another to sign in the voter's presence. Conservative practice: still use eligible MA-registered circulators since reliance is on signer validity, not circulator status.
  - note: Signer rules verbatim in sec. 7 ('Every voter signing a nomination paper shall sign in person as registered ... any voter who is prevented by physical disability ... may authorize some person'). 2026 SOS Guide verbatim: 'If you are running as a non-party candidate, you can gather signatures from any registered voter in your district' and 'Voters should sign their name as they are registered ... Voters must sign their own name.' Adversarial check: MA law is silent on circulators (no affirmative permission, just no restriction); the value correctly states the ABSENCE of a circulator rule and the value direction is safe (the load-bearing constraint, signer validity, is stated correctly), so no ballot-access risk from relying on it.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: No notarized circulator affidavit and no circulator certification/oath required. Validity rests on official certification: local boards of registrars certify each signer as a registered voter of their city/town. Separately, a non-party ('Unenrolled') candidate must file with the Secretary a registrar-issued certificate stating the candidate is not enrolled in any political party (M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 6) — this is a certificate ABOUT THE CANDIDATE, not a circulator/witness affidavit on the signature sheets.
  - note: Verbatim sec. 6 (Unenrolled certificate from registrars) and sec. 7 (registrars 'check each name ... certify ... and only names so checked shall be deemed ... qualified'). 2026 SOS Guide confirms the non-party Voter Registration Certificate is included on the nomination papers, distinct from any witness oath. No circulator oath/notary exists in the MA scheme. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.94
  - uses: paper. Signatures must be collected on official pre-printed paper nomination papers (yellow or beige for non-party/independent candidates) obtained from the Secretary; signers sign in person ('wet') and papers are physically submitted to local registrars for certification, then physically filed with the Secretary (mail accepted only if it physically arrives by the deadline; postmarks do not count). The SOS guidance states the papers cannot be provided electronically. No digital/remote-online pathway exists for an independent presidential petition in Massachusetts.
  - note: All three quotes verbatim in the 2026 SOS Candidates Guide: 'papers cannot be provided electronically'; 'Nomination papers for party candidates are white in color, while nomination papers for non-party candidates are yellow or beige'; 'the papers must physically arrive at the election office by the deadline. Postmark dates are not enough...'. Consistent with sec. 7 (per-sheet, in-person signing). Paper-only is correct and current. (The MA online-petition / e-signature pathway covers only certain local/initiative contexts, not this petition.)
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. No filing fee for ballot access in Massachusetts and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option; the 10,000 certified signatures are the sole ballot-access qualification. (Separate non-ballot-access obligations exist — FEC statement of candidacy, state OCPF/Ethics filing — but these are not a ballot-access fee and not an alternative to signatures.)
  - note: Ballotpedia's 2024 independent-candidate filing table grounds verbatim in page HTML: columns 'Filing fee' = N/A and 'Filing fee formula' = N/A for Massachusetts (row: Massachusetts | 10,000 | Fixed by statute | N/A | N/A | 8/27/2024). No fee or fee-in-lieu appears in M.G.L. c. 53. Note: the quoted string was collapsed in the markdown extraction but is fully present in the page HTML, so grounding holds. Correct and current.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an INDEPENDENT (non-party) presidential-elector nomination petition filed under M.G.L. c. 53 sec. 10 (last Tuesday in August of a presidential year), what is the exact deadline to SUBMIT signed nomination papers to local registrars for certification, and the deadline for registrars to COMPLETE certification — is it the sec. 7 'twenty-eighth day prior / seventh day prior' state-office schedule, or the 14-day schedule, and please confirm the 2028 calendar dates?

### Michigan
- **signatures:** Signatures DISPUTED: draft says 30,000; statute (1% of 2022 gov vote) = ~44,620 -- HOLD high
- **deadline:** Deadline LIVE: 4:00 p.m. 110th day before general = Thu Jul 18, 2024
- **risk:** Only the signature count is unsafe: the draft's flat 30,000 conflicts with its own 1%-formula citation (MCL 168.590b(2)), which on the 2022 gubernatorial total of 4,461,972 yields ~44,620, and Graveline v. Benson (6th Cir. 2021) separately struck the 30,000+distribution+deadline combination for statewide independents -- collect to the highest plausible number (~44,620) and confirm the exact per-cycle figure and Graveline's effect with the Bureau of Elections; all other fields verified live.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.86
  - uses: At least 1% of the total votes cast for all gubernatorial candidates at the last gubernatorial election (MCL 168.590b(2)). For the 2024 cycle the 2022 governor's race totaled 4,461,972 votes, so the strict statutory floor is approximately 44,620 valid signatures -- NOT the flat 30,000 the draft headlines. Plus the distribution requirement (>=100 in >=1/2 of congressional districts). Collect to the higher number and confirm the exact operative figure and Graveline's applicability with the Bureau of Elections before relying.
  - note: Citations ground verbatim, but the value is self-contradictory and likely understated. The draft headlines 30,000 while its own MCL 168.590b(2) citation states a 1%-of-gubernatorial-vote FORMULA. Independent re-derivation: the 2022 MI governor general election totaled 4,461,972 votes (Whitmer 2,430,505 + Dixon 1,960,635 + others); 1% = 44,620 -- materially above 30,000. The flat 30,000 is the pre-amendment number; the Ballotpedia '30,000' text appears stale. Separately, Graveline v. Benson (6th Cir. 2021) struck the 30,000+distribution+deadline combination for statewide INDEPENDENT candidates (district court set 12,000 interim). The true operative 2024 number (44,620 statutory vs. 30,000 stale vs. 12,000 Graveline interim vs. an administrative figure) is a legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle. Strictest defensible posture: collect to the highest statutory floor (~44,620); over-collecting cannot jeopardize ballot access.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 4:00 p.m. on the 110th day before the general November election. For 2024 that is Thursday, July 18, 2024 (110 days before Nov 5, 2024). MCL 168.590c(2). Signatures must be collected within the 180 days immediately before filing (MCL 168.590b(3)).
  - note: MCL 168.590c(2) text grounded verbatim ('not later than 4 p.m. of the one hundred-tenth day before the general election'); 180-day window grounded in 590b(3); Ballotpedia corroborates. Date arithmetic independently confirmed: Nov 5, 2024 minus 110 days = Thursday, July 18, 2024. Correct, current, no interpretation needed.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Yes. At least 100 registered electors must sign in each of at least one-half (1/2) of the state's congressional districts (MCL 168.590b(4), which expressly lists 'the office of president of the United States').
  - note: MCL 168.590b(4) grounded verbatim and expressly names president; Ballotpedia corroborates. Adversarial caveat: Graveline v. Benson found the geographic-distribution requirement part of the unconstitutional combination for statewide STATE offices -- whether it survives as applied to independent PRESIDENTIAL is unsettled. But the rule is on the books and complying with it cannot harm ballot access (over-compliance), so it is gated live rather than held. The Graveline question is flagged in the SOS inquiry attached to signaturesRequired.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Circulator must be at least 18 and a U.S. citizen; no Michigan residency required, but a non-resident circulator must mark the designated box on the certificate to accept Michigan jurisdiction (MCL 168.544c(3); HB 5152, 2014, removed residency requirements). Petition signers must be registered/qualified electors of the city/township in the petition heading.
  - note: MCL 168.544c certificate text grounded verbatim (18+, U.S. citizen, signed in presence), as is the non-resident-box language and the 544c(3) reference to a 'qualifying petition for an office named in section 590b(4)' (which lists president). Ballotpedia confirms HB 5152 removed all circulator residency requirements. Correct and current.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: No notarization of the petition. Each sheet carries a CERTIFICATE OF CIRCULATOR self-attestation (false statement = misdemeanor); the circulator must sign and date it before filing (MCL 168.544c(5)); it is not sworn before a notary. (The candidate's separate Affidavit of Identity includes a campaign-finance statement signed before a notary -- a distinct document, not the petition.)
  - note: MCL 168.544c(5) sign-and-date-before-filing rule and the misdemeanor warning grounded verbatim; Ballotpedia confirms the AOI campaign-finance statement is the notarized component (a separate document). No petition notarization required. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. Wet-ink paper petition sheets signed in the circulator's physical presence; no remote/online or digitized signature path for an independent presidential qualifying petition in Michigan.
  - note: MCL 168.544c 'each signature on the petition was signed in his or her presence' grounded verbatim; Ballotpedia signer-address requirement grounded. No statutory authorization for electronic collection located. Paper-only is correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None for the independent (no-party) presidential qualifying-petition path -- access is by petition only; no filing fee may substitute. (The $100 fee-in-lieu-of-petition exists only for major-party state LEGISLATIVE nominating petitions.)
  - note: Ballotpedia grounded verbatim: '$100 in lieu of filing a nominating petition' applies to a major party state legislative candidate only; the independent path requires an affidavit of identity plus a qualifying petition with no fee alternative. Sore-loser provision separately confirms an independent cannot use a partisan path/fee. Correct.
**🟢 newOrMinorPartyPath** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Materially different. A new party qualifies under MCL 168.685: petitions equal to not less than 1% of the total votes cast for all gubernatorial candidates at the last gubernatorial election, same distribution rule (>=100 in >=1/2 of congressional districts), same 4 p.m. 110th-day deadline, signatures within 180 days; chairperson and secretary file a signed certificate with the petitions, and the party nominates its presidential candidate by convention. Same circulator-certificate/paper mechanics (685(4) incorporates the 544c form).
  - note: MCL 168.685(1) long quote grounded verbatim (1% formula, 100-in-1/2-districts distribution, 110-day deadline, 180-day window, certificate filing) and 685(4) 'balance...as set forth in section 544c' grounded verbatim. Correct and current. Note: 685's use of the SAME 1% formula corroborates that the independent statewide signature requirement is the 1% formula (~44,620), reinforcing the doubt on the signaturesRequired '30,000' figure.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the 2024 presidential cycle, what is the exact number of valid signatures required for an independent (no-party) presidential qualifying petition under MCL 168.590b -- is it 1% of the 2022 total gubernatorial vote (~44,620), the older 30,000 figure, the Graveline v. Benson interim figure, or another administratively set number?
  - Does the holding of Graveline v. Benson (6th Cir. 2021) lowering/striking the statewide-independent signature and distribution requirements apply to the independent PRESIDENTIAL qualifying petition, or does the full MCL 168.590b(2)/(4) requirement (1% plus 100 signatures in 1/2 of congressional districts) still govern an independent presidential candidate for 2024?

### Minnesota
- **signatures:** 2,000 signatures (statutory cap; 1% of statewide turnout vastly exceeds 2,000)
- **deadline:** 77 days before GE — HOLD: draft date Aug 20 2024 is stale; 2028 cycle = Aug 22 2028
- **risk:** Signatures/fee/notary/distribution/capture all AUTO-LIVE and grounded; the only ballot-access risk is the deadline field, whose stated value (Aug 20, 2024) is for a past cycle — relying on it for a 2028 candidate would be wrong; recompute per cycle and confirm with SOS.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 2,000 signatures from eligible Minnesota voters (Minn. Stat. 204B.08, subd. 3(a): 1% of last statewide general-election turnout or 2,000, whichever is less — 1% far exceeds 2,000, so 2,000 is the operative number).
  - note: Statute quote verbatim at revisor.mn.gov/statutes/cite/204B.08 subd. 3(a). Ballotpedia verbatim ('At least 2,000 eligible voters must sign the petition'). 1% of ~3M MN voters is ~30,000, so 'whichever is less' fixes 2,000 as the cap. Current (2025 statutes).
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Petition must be RECEIVED by 5:00 p.m. on the day at least 77 days before general election day (Minn. Stat. 204B.09, subd. 1(c)). This recomputes each cycle: for the Nov. 7, 2028 GE the date is Aug. 22, 2028 (NOT the draft's Aug. 20, 2024, which was the 2024-cycle date). Confirm exact date/time with the SOS before relying.
  - note: Statutory rule grounded verbatim (204B.09 subd. 1(c): 'may file petitions at least 77 days before the general election day' + 'No affidavit or petition shall be accepted later than 5:00 p.m. on the last day for filing'). BUT the draft's relied VALUE 'August 20, 2024' is stale: today is 2026-06-07 and the next presidential election is Nov 7, 2028, where 77 days before = Aug 22, 2028 (verified by date arithmetic). Relying on the 2024 date for a current candidate would be wrong. Also a latent interpretation: statute phrases the cutoff as 'may file...at least 77 days before' (an earliest-by phrasing) rather than an express last-day; practitioners read the deadline as 77 days before, but exact day/time inclusivity warrants SOS confirmation.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. A single statewide signature total applies (Minn. Stat. 204B.08, subd. 3(a)); no congressional-district, county, or other geographic distribution requirement. Signers need only be eligible Minnesota voters.
  - note: 204B.08 subd. 3(a) sets one statewide number with no per-district/per-county quota anywhere in 204B.07-204B.08. Grounded verbatim. Correct and current.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: SIGNERS must be individuals eligible to vote for the candidate (eligible MN voters), may not sign more than one petition for the same office, and each must subscribe to the 204B.07 subd. 4 oath (both quotes grounded verbatim). No statutory CIRCULATOR age/residency/voter-status rule was located in 204B.07-204B.08 — but treat 'no circulator requirement' as unconfirmed (absence of a rule) and verify with the SOS rather than assuming none.
  - note: Signer requirements and oath are grounded verbatim (204B.08 subd. 2; 204B.07 subd. 4) and correct. The circulator conclusion is a negative inference from statutory silence — defensible, but an absence is inherently harder to verify than a stated rule (SOS guidance or rule could impose one), so I hold it pending SOS confirmation. Strict posture: do not represent to volunteers that there is definitely no circulator restriction.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Petition signatures: NO notarization or witness/circulator certification ('Notarization or certification of the signatures on a nominating petition is not required.', 204B.07 subd. 4). Candidate affidavit: YES, each nominated president/VP candidate must submit a signed, NOTARIZED affidavit of candidacy (204B.07 subd. 2(c)), signed before a notarial officer (204B.09 subd. 1(b)).
  - note: 204B.07 subd. 4 signature-notarization quote grounded verbatim. The affidavit quote is verbatim as a prefix ('...affidavit of candidacy for president or vice president'); the statute continues '...that includes the following information:' — the draft truncated, not misquoted. 204B.09 subd. 1(b) confirms notarial signing. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. No online/digital petition system exists; signatures collected on paper pages bearing the oath, each signer writing residence/mailing address (204B.07 subd. 4). Petition and notarized affidavits submitted by mail or hand and received by 5:00 p.m. on the last filing day; electronic submission statutorily barred (204B.09 subd. 1(e), notwithstanding ch. 325L) except a narrow emergency fax/scan option for out-of-state candidates (subd. 1a(b)).
  - note: 204B.09 subd. 1(e) mail/hand-notwithstanding-325L quote grounded verbatim; 204B.07 subd. 4 signer-address quote grounded verbatim. Subd. 1(e) literally names 'Affidavits,' but subd. 2 also bars electronic for nominating petitions and no online petition system exists, so paper-only is correct in practice and current.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Not applicable / no fee. Presidential electors pay no filing fee (204B.11 subd. 1(b): 'For the office of presidential elector...no filing fee is required'); the 2,000-signature nominating petition is itself the access mechanism. The separate 204B.11 subd. 2 'petition in place of a filing fee' (2,000 for president) is not the operative route because no fee applies.
  - note: Both 204B.11 quotes grounded verbatim (subd. 1(b) no-fee; subd. 2(a) 2,000-signature fee substitute). Draft correctly distinguishes the inapplicable fee-substitution path. Correct and current.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the 2028 general election (Tuesday, Nov. 7, 2028), what is the exact last day and time (5:00 p.m.?) by which a non-major-party presidential elector nominating petition under Minn. Stat. 204B.07/204B.09, subd. 1(c) must be RECEIVED — is it the day 77 days before the election (Aug. 22, 2028), and is that an inclusive/exclusive count?
  - Does Minnesota impose any age, residency, or voter-status requirement on the CIRCULATOR who collects signatures on an independent presidential nominating petition, or do requirements run only to the signers under Minn. Stat. 204B.08, subd. 2?

### Mississippi
- **signatures:** 1,000 signatures (flat statutory floor) + 6-elector slate + $2,500 fee — all three required, AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** 5:00 p.m., 60 days before general election (actual-receipt); 2024 = Sept 6 — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** 6 of 7 fields ground cleanly and triangulate across statute + SOS guide + Ballotpedia. Only circulatorEligibility is held (proving-a-negative on unwritten practice). No field is BLOCKED; ballot-access risk is low if signatures are clerk-certified well before deadline.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 1,000 valid signatures — a flat statutory minimum (written nominating petition signed by not less than 1,000 qualified/registered Mississippi voters), NOT a percentage; same 1,000 applies to a minor party qualifying by petition. Must be accompanied by a slate of 6 presidential electors, each signing a consent/pledge statement.
  - note: Both citation quotes ground VERBATIM: FindLaw 23-15-785(1) ('...written petition signed by at least one thousand (1,000) qualified voters of this state.') and SOS forms page ('...signatures of not less than 1,000 qualified electors of this state, must also be accompanied by a list of Presidential electors...'). Triangulated by Ballotpedia ('At least 1,000 qualified state voters must sign the petition') and the official 2026 SOS Candidate Qualifying Guide, which lists for the independent presidential candidate: petition of not less than 1,000 + 6-elector slate + $2,500 fee. 23-15-785(3) confirms a list equal to the number of electors (6 for MS) each executing the consent statement. 'at least'=floor, so the draft's 'flat fixed number, not a recompute' framing is correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Petition + 6-elector slate + $2,500 fee must be filed with the State Board of Election Commissioners (in the Office of the Secretary of State) by 5:00 p.m. not less than sixty (60) days before the general election. Recomputes each cycle off the November general-election date (2024 example: Sept 6, 2024). If filing by mail, it is an actual-receipt deadline, not postmark.
  - note: FindLaw 23-15-785(2) grounds VERBATIM ('...by 5:00 p.m. not less than sixty (60) days previous to the day of the election.'). 60-day rule corroborated by Ballotpedia ('filed with the secretary of state by 5:00 p.m. 60 days prior to the general election'). Computation verified: Nov 5, 2024 minus 60 days = Fri Sept 6, 2024 (exactly 60 days). Exact Sept 6, 2024 date independently confirmed by news source (gwcommonwealth.com): 'independent and party presidential candidates have to submit all required paperwork and fees by Sept. 6, 2024.' Actual-receipt-not-postmark confirmed verbatim in the 2026 SOS Candidate Qualifying Guide. NOTE: the 2026 guide is a midterm guide (no presidential office in 2026, gen. election Nov 3, 2026); the specific calendar date must be recomputed for 2028 (Nov 7, 2028 -> ~Sept 8, 2028). Rule itself is current and correct; clear statutory computation, not a contestable legal interpretation.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. For an independent (or minor-party-by-petition) presidential candidate the 1,000 signatures may be gathered from qualified voters of the State at large; no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement. The 100-per-district / 500-statewide alternative belongs ONLY to the presidential PRIMARY petition path (Miss. Code 23-15-1093), which does not apply to the independent general-election petition.
  - note: Quote 'written petition signed by at least one thousand (1,000) qualified voters of this state' grounds VERBATIM in 23-15-785. Independently confirmed: 23-15-359(1)(a) sets 'For an office elected by the state at large, not less than one thousand (1,000) qualified electors' with NO geographic breakdown. The 2026 SOS guide shows the 100-per-Congressional-district / 500-statewide alternative only under the Presidential Preference PRIMARY (party-candidate) section, and the independent general-election section reads simply '1,000 ... of the State of Mississippi.' 23-15-1093 governs the primary petition (filed Jan 1-15), confirming the draft's distinction. No district distribution for the independent path.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICT/over-comply default until SOS confirms: treat circulators as potentially required to be Mississippi-qualified electors (registered voters) and residents. The only person-level requirement that retrieval can confirm runs to the SIGNERS (each must be a qualified elector of MS, verified via circuit-clerk certification of registration); no circulator age/residency/voter-status statute or affidavit was found, but absence of an UNWRITTEN administrative practice cannot be proven by retrieval.
  - note: Signer-requirement quote grounds VERBATIM on SOS page ('Be a qualified elector (registered voter) of the State of Mississippi and of the district...'). Adversarial point: the draft VALUE itself flags 'UNKNOWN whether any unwritten administrative practice limits who may circulate.' Confirming a true negative (no circulator rule anywhere, including unwritten SOS practice) is beyond retrieval and is the kind of legal-interpretation question the gate reserves for hold. Structurally, MS has no circulator affidavit and signatures are clerk-certified against the signer's own registration, so circulator identity is largely irrelevant in practice — but under the never-risk-ballot-access mandate I hold and route to the SOS. Added an SOS inquiry.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: No notary and no circulator affidavit. Each petition's signatures must be CERTIFIED by the circuit clerk of the county where the signatures were collected, BEFORE the petition is filed with the Secretary of State; obtain clerk certification well in advance of the qualifying deadline. 'Header' information must be completed on each petition page BEFORE signatures are gathered.
  - note: Both quotes ground VERBATIM. SOS forms page: 'All signatures on petitions for independent or special election candidates MUST be certified by the signer's circuit or municipal clerk respectively before filing with the appropriate office.' 2026 SOS Candidate Qualifying Guide (extracted via pdftotext): 'a. All petition signatures must be certified by each Circuit Clerk's Office of the county from where the signatures were collected, and b. All "header" information must be completed on each petition page prior to obtaining voters' signatures.' Critically, the guide lists these two items expressly under 'As an Independent Candidate for the General Election' for U.S. President, so the requirement is confirmed for the independent presidential petition. No notary requirement appears anywhere.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Wet-ink paper petitions gathered by hand and certified by county circuit clerks; SOS provides only downloadable paper petition forms (President Candidate_Independent Candidate_Petition) that must be printed, signed, and clerk-certified. No digital/online filing exists for the independent presidential petition.
  - note: Quote grounds VERBATIM: FindLaw 23-15-359(11) 'The petition required by this section may not be filed by using the Internet.' Caveat on citation SCOPE: that internet-ban lives in 23-15-359, whose petition language is mirrored by 23-15-785 for the presidential filing; arguably 'this section' refers to 23-15-359's petition, so the ban is not the tightest possible citation for the 23-15-785 presidential petition specifically. BUT the paper conclusion is independently dispositive regardless of that scope question: signatures must be wet-ink and county-clerk-certified (incompatible with online filing), and the SOS publishes only printable paper forms (verified on SOS forms page). Bottom line 'paper' is correct and not interpretation-dependent.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: No fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option exists. A mandatory $2,500.00 qualifying assessment for the Office of President is payable to the MS Secretary of State and is required IN ADDITION to (not instead of) the 1,000-signature petition and the 6-elector slate. Same $2,500 presidential assessment applies to a party nominee. Fee revenue is deposited into the Elections Support Fund.
  - note: Both quotes ground VERBATIM: FindLaw 23-15-359(1)(h) '(h) For the Office of President of the United States, a party nominee or independent candidate shall pay an assessment in the amount of Two Thousand Five Hundred Dollars ($2,500.00).' and SOS forms page ('...submitted with a qualifying fee of $2,500 to the Secretary of State's Office.'). 23-15-359(5) confirms deposit into the Elections Support Fund (23-15-5). The 2026 SOS guide lists, for the independent presidential candidate, BOTH a 1,000-signature petition AND a $2,500 fee AND the 6-elector slate as separate required items — confirming the fee is additive, not an alternative. Field is mislabeled 'feeAlternative' but the substance (no alternative; fee is mandatory and additional) is correct.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential nominating petition under Miss. Code Ann. 23-15-785, are there any requirements (residency, age, MS voter registration) governing WHO may circulate/collect the petition signatures, or any written or unwritten administrative practice limiting circulators? (No circulator affidavit appears on the form; please confirm.)

### Missouri
- **signatures:** 10,000 signatures (collect a cushion; statewide statutory floor)
- **deadline:** 15th Monday before Nov general (Jul 29, 2024 last cycle)
- **risk:** All 6 citation sources grounded verbatim; core path (10k sigs, 15th-Monday deadline, paper+notary, elector district distribution) is AUTO-LIVE. Only the circulator-residency rule is held for legal interpretation; treat as MO-resident-required and confirm with SOS.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 10,000 signatures of registered Missouri voters (fixed statutory floor for a statewide office under RSMo 115.321.3; same 10,000 governs the new/minor-party statewide petition under RSMo 115.315.5). For president, ONE petition nominates the full slate of presidential electors, with the presidential and vice-presidential candidates named on each page. Operationally, collect well above 10,000 because the SOS validates signatures and invalidations are common.
  - note: RSMo 115.321.3 ('signed by at least ten thousand registered voters of the state') and 115.315.5 ('at least ten thousand registered voters of the state obtained at large') both grounded verbatim on revisor.mo.gov. 10,000 is a fixed number for statewide office (does not recompute per cycle), unlike the district/county 2%-or-10k-whichever-is-less rule in 115.321.4. Statute says 10,000 registered voters must SIGN; 'valid' is the practical net after SOS review, so a cushion is advisable, but the threshold number 10,000 is correct and current.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 5:00 p.m. on the fifteenth Monday immediately preceding the November general election (RSMo 115.329.1). For the 2024 cycle (general Nov. 5, 2024) this is July 29, 2024 — independently confirmed by date computation. It is a recomputed rule, not a fixed date. Petition cannot be filed before 8:00 a.m. on the day after the prior general election.
  - note: RSMo 115.329.1 grounded verbatim (window between 8:00 a.m. day after prior general and 5:00 p.m. fifteenth Monday before the general). Ballotpedia quote also grounded verbatim. Independently re-derived: counting Mondays back from Nov 5, 2024 (a Tuesday), the 15th Monday is 2024-07-29 — matches the draft exactly.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: No geographic distribution quota on the SIGNATURES (the 10,000 are obtained 'at large'). There IS a distribution requirement on the ELECTOR NOMINEES: at least one qualified resident of each congressional district must be named as a presidential-elector nominee (RSMo 115.321.2). Separately, each petition page may carry signatures from only one county and pages must be numbered in sequence per county (RSMo 115.325.1) — a sheet-organization rule, not a per-county signature quota.
  - note: RSMo 115.321.2 grounded verbatim ('At least one qualified resident of each congressional district shall be named as a nominee for presidential elector'). 'obtained at large' grounded in 115.315.5. The one-county-per-page / numbered-in-sequence rule grounded verbatim in 115.325.1. Draft correctly separates the elector-nominee district requirement from the (absent) signature distribution quota.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICTEST reading: treat the circulator (affiant who obtains signatures) as required to be a resident of the State of Missouri (the statutory affidavit form in RSMo 115.325 recites 'I, ___, a resident of the state of Missouri'). Use Missouri-resident circulators to avoid any page being rejected. Each SIGNER must be a registered Missouri voter of the county shown on the page (felony to sign if not registered); no voter may sign more than one nomination for one office (RSMo 115.323).
  - note: All quotes grounded verbatim in 115.325 (affidavit form) and 115.323. BUT the 'resident of the state of Missouri' language appears in a FORM TEMPLATE recital, not an operative eligibility clause; whether it is an enforceable circulator-residency REQUIREMENT (vs. a recital the affiant happens to make) is a legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle. Added constitutional doubt: circulator-residency requirements have been struck in other states (Buckley v. ACLF line). Strictest defensible posture is to assume MO residency is required and use only MO-resident circulators. Signer requirements (registered MO voter, one-signature-per-office) are clear and grounded.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: BOTH a circulator certification AND notarization are required on EVERY page. Each page carries a CIRCULATOR'S AFFIDAVIT (circulator swears each signer signed in his/her presence and is a registered voter), which must be 'Subscribed and sworn to before me' a Notary Public (notary signature, seal, and commission-expiration appear on the form) — RSMo 115.325.
  - note: Grounded verbatim in the 115.325 statutory form: the circulator's-presence/registered-voter recital, 'Subscribed and sworn to before me this ___ day of ___, A.D.___', 'Signature of Notary', and 'Notary Public (Seal)'. Confirms notarized circulator affidavit per page. Substantial-compliance saving clause ('disregarding clerical and merely technical errors') exists but does not eliminate the notarization requirement.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper (wet-ink). Pages of uniform size, signatures from only one county per page, numbered in sequence per county, each page bearing a notarized circulator's affidavit (RSMo 115.325.1 + the statutory form). No Missouri online/digital signature system covers an independent/new-party PRESIDENTIAL nominating petition; collect and submit on paper to the Secretary of State.
  - note: RSMo 115.325.1 grounded verbatim (uniform pages, one county per page, numbered in sequence). 115.321 'file a petition with the secretary of state' grounded verbatim. The per-page notarized wet-ink affidavit makes paper the operative and strictest-safe capture mode. The 'no digital system exists' point is a negative assertion, but paper is unambiguously sufficient and required by the form, so reliance carries no ballot-access risk.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.82
  - uses: None. There is no filing-fee alternative to (or addition to) the signature petition for an independent or new-party presidential candidate; the 10,000-signature petition (RSMo 115.321 / 115.329) is the sole qualification mechanism on this path. Chapter 115 filing fees apply to party-primary declarations of candidacy, not to independent/new-party petitions. STRICTEST operating assumption: do not rely on any fee shortcut — you must complete the petition.
  - note: Cited quote (115.321.5, 'placed on the official ballot as an independent candidate') grounds verbatim but speaks to ballot placement rather than fees; the 'None' conclusion is a negative claim derived from the absence of any fee-in-lieu provision in 115.321/115.329. 'None' is itself the conservative posture (assuming no fee shortcut never risks ballot access), so AUTO-LIVE is appropriate. If a campaign wanted to rely on a fee path it does NOT exist — so the value cannot mislead toward under-collecting signatures.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent/new-party presidential nominating petition under RSMo 115.321/115.325, must the circulator (affiant) be a Missouri resident as an enforceable eligibility requirement, and is there any age or registered-voter requirement for circulators? Does the office reject pages whose affiant is a non-resident?

### Montana
- **signatures:** 5,000 signatures (5% of last governor's vote OR 5,000, whichever is less; 5,000 cap controls — unchanged by 2025 HB 207, which touched only non-presidential)
- **deadline:** Petition filed with SOS 76 days before general (2024 = Aug 21); signatures to county admins ≥1 week earlier (2024 = Aug 14)
- **risk:** All 7 citations grounded verbatim (NASS PDF verified via download). Four fields AUTO-LIVE; three on CONSERVATIVE-HOLD for legal-characterization questions (distribution-path separation, circulator residency/eligibility, and whether 13-10-202 fees reach a presidential petitioner) — none should be relied on as "no requirement" without SOS confirmation, to avoid ballot-access risk.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Signatures of electors equal to 5% or more of the total votes cast for the successful candidate for governor at the last general election, OR 5,000 electors, whichever is less. The 5,000 cap controls in practice (5% of the 2020 gubernatorial winner Gianforte's ~328,000 votes is ~16,400, far above 5,000), so the operative requirement for an independent presidential petition is 5,000 signatures. Recomputes each cycle off the most recent governor's race.
  - note: All three citations grounded verbatim: MCA 13-10-504(3) (leg.mt.gov), NASS July-2024 PDF (verified via download — quote present p. Montana section), and ballot-access.org ('Presidential independents continue to need 5,000 signatures'). Adversarial: confirmed 2025 HB 207 lowered only NON-presidential petitions (5%->4%); the presidential path under 13-10-504 is unchanged. 5,000 cap independently re-derived from 2020 Gianforte vote (~328k). No interpretation required — statute is explicit.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: The nominating petition must be filed with the Secretary of State no later than 76 days before the general election (statutory rule, MCA 13-10-504(1)). Petition signatures must first be submitted to the county election administrator for verification at least 1 week before the SOS filing deadline (13-10-504(2)). For the 2024 cycle (Nov 5, 2024) this computed to an Aug 21, 2024 SOS deadline and an Aug 14, 2024 county-submission deadline. The calendar dates recompute each cycle off the 76-day / 1-week rule.
  - note: 76-day SOS rule and the '1 week before' county-submission rule both grounded verbatim in MCA 13-10-504(1)-(2). Independently verified the arithmetic: Nov 5 2024 - 76 days = Wed Aug 21 2024; minus 1 week = Wed Aug 14 2024 — both match the draft. Adversarial note: a Ballotpedia 2024 'passed-deadlines' list shows '(August 19)' linked to a 2020 page (appears stale and is NOT relied on); the statutory 76-day rule is authoritative. Both the SOS filing deadline AND the earlier county-verification deadline are binding — captured.
**🟡 distributionRule** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: For the independent / non-qualified-party PRESIDENTIAL petition (MCA 13-10-504), the grounded statutory text imposes only a statewide signature total (5% / 5,000 cap) with no express per-district distribution requirement. STRICTEST reading pending SOS confirmation: do not assume zero distribution requirement — the 1/3-of-legislative-districts distribution rule that appears in the minor-PARTY qualification path (13-10-601, per the NASS summary) must be confirmed by the SOS as NOT applying to a 13-10-504 candidate petition before treating distribution as 'none'.
  - note: Citations grounded verbatim (MCA 13-10-504(3) and NASS PDF). Adversarial: the NASS text confirms the 1/3-of-legislative-districts distribution requirement attaches to the PARTY-qualification path, not the individual candidate petition — strongly supporting 'none' for the independent path. But correctness hinges on a legal characterization (which statutory path binds an independent presidential candidate). Per gate rule, grounded + interpretation -> CONSERVATIVE-HOLD; SOS inquiry filed. Getting this wrong (missing a distribution requirement) would risk ballot access, so over-comply.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: Grounded facts: (a) a petition may be signed ONLY by a qualified Montana elector, and (b) a circulator may not be paid based on the number of signatures gathered (MCA 13-27-102). STRICTEST reading on circulator residency/eligibility: do NOT assume out-of-state or non-elector circulators are permitted, and do not rely on the 'prior residency rule held unconstitutional' assertion. Ballotpedia only states the statutes 'do not specify circulator requirements' — silence is not affirmative permission. Confirm circulator residency/registration/age rules with the SOS before deploying non-resident or non-elector circulators.
  - note: Both citations grounded verbatim: Ballotpedia ('The statutes do not specify circulator requirements (e.g., residency status).') and 13-27-102 (signer must be a qualified MT elector; no per-signature pay). Adversarial: the draft's claims that out-of-state circulators ARE permitted and that a 'prior residency rule was held unconstitutional' are NOT supported by the grounded quotes — they are added legal conclusions from statutory silence. Strictest interpretation treats circulator eligibility as unsettled. CONSERVATIVE-HOLD; SOS inquiry filed. The pay-per-signature ban and elector-signer rule, by themselves, are safe to rely on.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Notarized circulator affidavit required. An affidavit of circulation (in substantially the statutory form) must be attached to each petition sheet/section, in which the gatherer swears the signatures are genuine and signers knew the petition's contents; it must be subscribed and sworn before a person authorized to administer oaths (notarized) and must note the date of the first signature and the circulator's address. MCA 13-10-504(2) expressly requires the 13-27-302 affidavits of circulation.
  - note: Both citations grounded verbatim: MCA 13-27-302 affidavit form ('Subscribed and sworn to before me this ___ day of _________, 20__' + '(Person authorized to take oaths)') and Ballotpedia ('The affidavits must also be notarized.'). The notarization requirement is explicit on the face of the statutory form — no interpretation needed. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Signatures are collected on paper petition sheets, each with a notarized circulator affidavit, then submitted to county election administrators for verification before the petition is filed with the Secretary of State. No remote-online or digitized capture exists for an independent presidential nominating petition in Montana.
  - note: Both citations grounded verbatim: MCA 13-10-504(2) (county-administrator verification/certification) and 13-27-302 ('An affidavit ... must be attached to each sheet or section submitted to the county official'). The physical-sheet + county-submission model is on the face of the statute; no online capture authorized. No interpretation required. AUTO-LIVE.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.65
  - uses: No fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option is offered for the presidential petition; the petition is the access mechanism. STRICTEST reading on whether ANY filing fee is owed: do not assume a $0 fee. MCA 13-10-504 itself contains no fee, but MCA 13-10-202 makes independent and non-qualified-party candidates liable for the same filing fees as party candidates; whether that general fee provision reaches a presidential petitioner under 13-10-504 is a legal-characterization question. Confirm with the SOS that no filing fee is due before treating the petition path as fee-free.
  - note: Both citations grounded verbatim (MCA 13-10-504(1) and NASS PDF). Adversarial: the draft itself flags MCA 13-10-202, which imposes fees on independent / non-qualified-party candidates equal to party-candidate fees. The draft's conclusion that this does not reach the 13-10-504 presidential petitioner is plausible but is an unsettled legal characterization that retrieval cannot definitively resolve, and wrongly assuming no fee could risk a defective filing. Per gate rule, grounded + interpretation -> CONSERVATIVE-HOLD; SOS inquiry filed. (The narrower claim 'no fee-IN-LIEU-OF-signatures alternative is offered' is safe — there is no such substitution path.)

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Distribution: For an INDEPENDENT presidential nominating petition under MCA 13-10-504, is there any requirement that signatures be distributed across legislative or other districts, or is the only requirement the statewide total (5% of last governor's vote or 5,000 electors, whichever is less)? Please confirm the 1/3-of-legislative-districts distribution rule applies ONLY to minor-party qualification under 13-10-601 and not to the 13-10-504 candidate petition.
  - Circulator eligibility: For a 13-10-504 presidential petition, must signature gatherers (circulators) be Montana residents and/or registered Montana electors, or may out-of-state and non-elector circulators gather signatures? Are there any age or registration requirements for circulators beyond the prohibition on per-signature payment in 13-27-102?
  - Filing fee: Does an independent or non-qualified-party candidate for president/vice president filing a petition under MCA 13-10-504 owe any filing fee (e.g., under 13-10-202), or is the petition the sole condition of access with no fee due and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option?

### Nebraska
- **signatures:** 2,500 valid signatures (flat statutory) — count grounded; signer-eligibility scope unresolved (HOLD)
- **deadline:** Petition due Aug 1 of the presidential general-election year (LIVE)
- **risk:** Core figures (2,500 / Aug 1 / no distribution / no fee / paper / notarized affidavit) are grounded in current statute and consensus-confirmed; the one live risk is signer eligibility — Ballotpedia says signers must not have voted in any party primary, a condition absent from the current grounded statutory petition form (32-620.01), so confirm with the SOS before collecting.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.72
  - uses: 2,500 valid signatures (flat statutory number under Neb. Rev. Stat. 32-620(3)(b), not a percentage). STRICT signer-eligibility reading until SOS confirms: each signer must be a registered, qualified Nebraska voter AND (per Ballotpedia's gloss) must not have voted in any party's primary that year. Collect only from voters meeting the stricter condition and over-collect to a healthy cushion.
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-620(3)(b) quote 'A petition signed by not less than two thousand five hundred registered voters' verified verbatim on FindLaw (current as of 2024-01-01); 32-620.01 signer-qualification quote verified verbatim. CONSENSUS: Ballotpedia independently confirms 2,500 registered voters for the independent general-election path. ADVERSARIAL: Ballotpedia adds that signers must be voters 'who did not vote in the primary election of any party' — a restriction ABSENT from the grounded current statutory petition form (32-620.01), which recites only registered/qualified-voter status. Could not reach the official Nebraska Legislature site (Cronet failures) or Justia (CAPTCHA) for a third primary-source confirmation, so the signer-eligibility scope is unresolved. The headline count (2,500) and type (flat statutory, not recomputed) are solid; the signer-eligibility discrepancy forces a strict HOLD on collection criteria.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: August 1 in the year of the presidential general election (for 2024 this was Thursday, August 1, 2024; no weekend/holiday adjustment). The completed application + petition must be filed with the Secretary of State by that date.
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-620 quote 'shall be filed with the Secretary of State by August 1 in the year of the presidential general election' verified verbatim; the 60-day decline-affidavit quote (32-620(4)) also verified verbatim. CONSENSUS: Ballotpedia independently states the petition 'must be filed with the secretary of state by August 1 of the election year.' No statutory ambiguity; the date is fixed and current. Write-in path (second Friday before the election) is correctly flagged as a separate, non-applicable deadline.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. The 2,500-signature requirement is statewide with no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution/quota for the independent (nonpartisan) presidential petition; the county field on the form is identification only.
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-620(3)(b) and the 32-620.01 form county-identification language verified verbatim — neither imposes a distribution quota. CONSENSUS/ADVERSARIAL: Ballotpedia confirms the 100-signatures-per-congressional-district rule applies to the PRIMARY-ballot petition only (party candidates), not the independent general-election petition, exactly as the draft distinguishes. No distribution requirement exists for the independent path.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Circulator must be at least 18 years of age. The statute imposes no Nebraska-residency or registered-voter requirement on the circulator; the circulator must personally witness each signature and disclose paid vs. volunteer status. (Registered-voter/residency requirements apply to signers, not the circulator.)
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-628(3) affidavit quote 'he or she is at least eighteen years of age, that each person whose name appears on the petition personally signed the petition in the presence of the affiant' and the 32-628(4) paid/volunteer-circulator statements verified verbatim. The grounded statutory affidavit recites ONLY the 18-years-of-age qualification for the circulator — no residency or registration clause — so the draft's value is a faithful, non-interpretive reading of the current primary text.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: NOTARIZED circulator affidavit required on every sheet bearing signatures (below the signatures), plus the boldface 'WARNING TO PETITION SIGNERS' statement above the signatures. The affidavit must be subscribed and sworn before a notary public.
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-628(3) quotes verified verbatim — 'Every sheet of a petition which contains signatures shall have upon it, below the signatures, an affidavit' and 'Subscribed and sworn to before me, a notary public, this ______ day of _________ 20____ at_____________, Nebraska. Notary Public ___________________________'. The boldface WARNING is in 32-628(2). Notarization is unambiguous and current; a witness-only attestation is NOT sufficient.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Wet-signature paper process only: statutory sheet layout (>=2.5-inch signature space, <=20 signatures/page, lines >=1/4 inch apart), in-person circulator witnessing each signature, and a notarized per-sheet circulator affidavit. No online/e-signature system covers the Nebraska independent presidential petition; completed petition is returned to the SOS Elections Division by mail or in person.
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-628 quotes 'Petitions shall provide for no more than twenty signatures per page' and the in-person witnessing language verified verbatim; SOS candidate page quote 'Return the completed candidate filing forms and fees to the following address: Secretary of State Attn: Elections Division PO Box 94608 Lincoln, NE 68509-4608' verified verbatim. The statutory requirements (physical layout, in-person witnessing, notarized affidavit) are incompatible with a remote-online flow, supporting 'paper' as current and correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. No filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for the independent (nonpartisan) presidential petition; the 2,500-signature petition is the sole access mechanism under 32-620(3).
  - note: GROUNDED: 32-608(2)(a) fee-bearing-office enumeration verified verbatim — it lists U.S. Senator, state officers, Representatives in Congress, county and city/village officers, etc., and does NOT include President/Vice President; 32-620(3) signature-only requirement verified verbatim. CORROBORATION (32-621, fetched): when a new party forms after the primary, 'all candidates except candidates for President or Vice President of the United States shall pay the filing fee as provided in section 32-608' — independently confirming President/VP are fee-exempt. No fee may be substituted for signatures.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent/nonpartisan presidential nominating petition under Neb. Rev. Stat. 32-620(3), is a person eligible to sign if they voted in a 2024 party primary, or must signers be registered voters who did NOT vote in any party's primary? (The 32-620.01 form recites only registered-voter qualification; Ballotpedia states a no-primary-vote restriction.)

### Nevada
- **signatures:** NV indep pres: 1% of last general's U.S. House vote total (statutory formula); exact 2024 hard number NOT confirmed from primary source — held UNKNOWN
- **deadline:** NV indep pres petition + declaration due 5 p.m. 2nd Friday in Aug (2024: Aug 9); county-clerk submission due 25 working days prior; copy filed with SOS before circulating
- **risk:** All 8 fields citation-grounded (4 source URLs verbatim-confirmed). Core deadline/fee/distribution/capture facts AUTO-LIVE off NRS 298.109. Two CONSERVATIVE-HOLDs: signaturesRequired (no confirmed 2024 hard number — must compute from 2022 NV U.S. House total and confirm with SOS before relying) and witnessOrNotary (statute says "affidavit"; "before a notary public" is from a general-petition secondary source — treat notarization as required). Beware: NRS 298.109 ("independent" path) vs NRS 293.1715 ("minor/new party" path) are DIFFERENT regimes with different deadlines (Aug vs 3rd Fri June) — do not conflate.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Signatures of registered voters equal to not less than 1% of the total number of votes cast at the last preceding general election for the offices of Representative in Congress (NRS 298.109(1)). The exact 2024-cycle hard number is treated as UNKNOWN and MUST be computed from the certified 2022 Nevada U.S. House vote total and confirmed with the Secretary of State before relying.
  - note: GROUND: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed — NRS 298.109 quote present word-for-word on nevada.public.law/statutes/nrs_298.109; NRS 293.1715(2)(c) quote present word-for-word on nevada.public.law/statutes/nrs_293.1715. JUDGE: The 1% statutory formula is CURRENT and CORRECT for an independent presidential candidate. The draft correctly declines to assert an unverified 2024 hard number and sets it to UNKNOWN — the appropriate conservative move (I could not confirm any specific 2024 count from a primary source; Ballotpedia's 2024 table rendered empty). HOLD (not AUTO-LIVE) solely because the operationally usable value (the actual signature count) is unresolved; the formula itself is sound. Note the draft also correctly distinguishes the 1% basis is shared with the NRS 293.1715(2)(c) minor-party path.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Independent presidential path (NRS 298.109): declaration of candidacy + petition of candidacy filed with the Secretary of State no later than 5 p.m. on the second Friday in August of the presidential-election year (2024: Aug 9, 2024). A copy of the petition must be filed with the SOS before it may be circulated. Documents circulated in a county must be submitted to that county clerk for signature verification no later than 25 working days before the August filing deadline. Minor/new-party path (NRS 293.1715(2)(c)) differs: petition due to SOS no later than the third Friday in June.
  - note: GROUND: All three quotes verbatim-confirmed on their cited pages (the 5 p.m. second-Friday-in-August quote and the 25-working-days quote on nrs_298.109; the third-Friday-in-June quote on nrs_293.1715). JUDGE: Independently corroborated — NRS 298.109(1) sets the 5 p.m. second-Friday-in-August deadline and the copy-before-circulation rule; 298.109(2) sets the 25-working-days county-clerk submission. Aug 9, 2024 is the correct second Friday of August 2024. Ballotpedia's 2020 footnote ('Deadline to file petitions with local officials...7/10/2020') is consistent with the 25-working-days-before rule. The draft properly flags the materially different minor-party June deadline so the two paths are not conflated. CURRENT and CORRECT for an independent presidential candidate; no legal interpretation needed.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No statewide-distribution quota for the independent presidential petition (no minimum per congressional district or county). The petition may consist of more than one document; each document must bear the name of a single county and only registered voters of that county may sign it; each county's documents are verified by that county clerk. Signatures are county-segregated but there is no required number per county/district.
  - note: GROUND: Quote ('The petition may consist of more than one document. Each document must bear the name of a county and only registered voters of that county may sign the document.') verbatim-confirmed on nrs_298.109. JUDGE: NRS 298.109(2) contains no per-county or per-district minimum for the INDEPENDENT path — confirmed by full read of the section. ADVERSARIAL CHECK: The Justia copy of NRS 293.1715 shows a subsection 5 imposing a per-petition-district apportionment of the 1% — BUT that applies only to the MINOR-PARTY path (293.1715(2)(c)), NOT to the independent presidential petition (298.109) this field is scoped to. The draft is correctly scoped to NRS 298.109 and the no-quota conclusion holds for that path. CURRENT and CORRECT.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: NRS 298.109 imposes no express age, residency, or voter-registration requirement on the circulator; it requires only the circulator's affidavit that signatures are genuine and were signed in the circulator's presence by persons registered to vote in that county. STRICTEST defensible posture for operations: do not assume out-of-state or non-registered circulators are safe statewide — confirm with SOS, since circulator-eligibility rules are an area of active legal change in many states and Ballotpedia's 'no requirements' statement is secondary.
  - note: GROUND: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed — the NRS 298.109 affidavit quote on nrs_298.109; the Ballotpedia 'Circulators of petitions are not required to be registered voters in Nevada. The statutes do not stipulate any requirements for circulators in Nevada.' quote confirmed word-for-word at line 370 of the political-candidates page. JUDGE: The statute's silence on circulator eligibility is accurately read. HOLD (interpretationRequired=true) because correctness as an affirmative operational rule ('any circulator is fine') rests on (a) a secondary source (Ballotpedia) generalizing from statutory silence and (b) the open legal question of whether SOS practice or any other NRS provision constrains circulators for a presidential petition. Statutory silence does not equal a guarantee; conservative posture is to verify before relying on out-of-state/non-registered circulators.
**🟡 witnessOrNotary** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.75
  - uses: Treat a NOTARIZED circulator affidavit as required: each petition document must contain the circulator's sworn affidavit that all signatures are genuine and were signed in the circulator's presence by persons registered to vote in that county (NRS 298.109(2)). Strictest defensible reading: execute the circulator affidavit before a notary public. No separate notarization of individual voter signatures is required.
  - note: GROUND: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed — the NRS 298.109(2) 'affidavit of the person who circulated the document...' quote on nrs_298.109; the Ballotpedia 'The circulator of the petition must sign, before a notary public, an affidavit on the back of the petition verifying that all signatures were recorded in the circulator's presence.' quote confirmed word-for-word at line 366 of the political-candidates page. JUDGE/ADVERSARIAL: NRS 298.109 itself says only 'affidavit' — it does NOT expressly say 'notary public.' The 'before a notary public' language comes from Ballotpedia's GENERAL petition guidance (tied to minor-party/NRS 293.172 petitions), not from NRS 298.109 specifically. An affidavit is by definition sworn before an officer authorized to administer oaths, which conventionally means a notary, so requiring notarization is the SAFE/strictest posture — but whether NRS 298.109 strictly mandates a notary (vs. any oath-administering officer) is a legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle. HOLD at the notarization-required reading.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: paper. The independent presidential petition is a wet-ink, county-by-county paper document: each signer adds signature, residence address, date, and county of registration; signatures must be in ink; the circulator executes a paper affidavit; documents are physically submitted to each county clerk for verification. No Nevada digital/online signature-collection system covers this petition. (Candidate declaration/filing with the SOS may use the SOS online portal, but signature collection is paper.)
  - note: GROUND: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed — the NRS 298.109 signer-information quote ('Each person signing shall add to his or her signature the address...the date...and the name of the county wherein he or she is registered to vote.') on nrs_298.109; the Ballotpedia 'Each signature must be made in ink. Any signature not made in ink will be disregarded.' quote confirmed word-for-word at line 366. JUDGE: The statutory scheme (county-named documents, signer adds handwritten address/date/county, circulator paper affidavit, physical submission to county clerks for NRS 293.1276-293.1279 verification) is inherently wet-ink paper; no e-signature pathway exists for this petition. CURRENT and CORRECT; no interpretation needed. The 'made in ink' requirement is from general petition guidance but is consistent with and reinforces the statutory scheme.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: There is NO fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative. The $250 filing fee is required IN ADDITION TO the petition signatures, not as a substitute. An independent presidential candidate must both pay the $250 fee and file the qualifying petition. (The fee is refundable within 10 days if the candidacy is ultimately not qualified, per NRS 293.194, but it cannot replace the signature requirement.)
  - note: GROUND: Both quotes verbatim-confirmed — the NRS 298.109(1) 'pay a filing fee of $250 and file...a declaration of candidacy and a petition of candidacy' quote on nrs_298.109; the Ballotpedia presidential-page quote 'must file a declaration of candidacy...pay a $250 filing fee, and file a petition containing the signatures of at least 1 percent...' confirmed word-for-word at line 231 of the presidential-candidates page. JUDGE: 'pay...AND file...a petition' in NRS 298.109(1) is conjunctive — the fee and petition are both mandatory; there is no statutory fee-in-lieu option. The draft's parenthetical refund claim is INDEPENDENTLY corroborated by NRS 293.194 (filing fee 'must be returned to the candidate...within 10 days' after a final determination the petition does not qualify) — a side note that does not affect the central, correct conclusion. CURRENT and CORRECT.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential candidate filing under NRS 298.109 in 2024, what is the exact number of valid registered-voter signatures required (i.e., 1% of the total votes cast for the offices of Representative in Congress at the 2022 general election), and what is the official certified vote-total figure on which that 1% is based?
  - Under NRS 298.109(2), must the circulator's affidavit on each petition document be sworn before a notary public specifically, or may it be executed before any officer authorized to administer oaths — and does the Secretary of State's office require a notary acknowledgment block on the presidential petition of candidacy form?
  - For an independent presidential candidate under NRS 298.109, please confirm the exact 2024 statutory deadlines: (a) the 5 p.m. second-Friday-in-August filing deadline date, and (b) the 25-working-days-before deadline for submitting circulated documents to each county clerk for signature verification.

### New Hampshire
- **signatures:** NH: 3,000 sigs (1,500 per CD, 2 districts) + $250 fee — both required
- **deadline:** NH: Decl. of Intent Jun 3-12, 2026; papers to SOS by 5pm Wed Sep 2, 2026
- **risk:** Core numbers/dates verbatim-grounded in RSA 655:42/655:43/655:19-a and confirmed against the SOS 2026 page; only soft spot is circulator eligibility, which rests on statutory silence (no circulator rule exists) rather than an affirmative statement — held conservatively pending SOS confirmation.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 3,000 signatures of registered voters, 1,500 from each of New Hampshire's 2 U.S. congressional districts. Flat statutory number under RSA 655:42, I (which expressly names 'president' alongside U.S. senator and governor); it is not a percentage and does not recompute by cycle. The separate new/minor political-organization path requires signatures equal to 3% of total ballots cast at the previous state general election, computed by the SOS as 18,808 for 2026 (RSA 655:42, III).
  - note: RSA 655:42, I quote found verbatim in primary source and expressly lists 'president' at 3,000 / 1,500-per-district. 18,808 political-org figure confirmed verbatim on SOS page. Note: the SOS citation used is the GOVERNOR line ($100 AND 3,000), not a president-specific line (the SOS running-for-office page does not enumerate president), but the statute directly grounds the president figure, so the value is correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Two steps for 2026: (1) Declaration of Intent (RSA 655:17-b, presidential) filed with the Secretary of State during the candidate filing window June 3-12, 2026 (RSA 655:14 / 655:14-a: 'first Wednesday in June' = June 3 through 'Friday of the following week' = June 12). (2) Certified nomination papers filed with the Secretary of State no later than 5:00 p.m. Wednesday Sept 2, 2026 (RSA 655:43, I: 'Wednesday one week before the primary'; 2026 primary is Tue Sept 8). Intermediate local deadlines (RSA 655:41): papers to town/ward Supervisors of the Checklist by 5:00 p.m. Aug 5, 2026 (Wed 5 weeks before primary); supervisor certification complete by 5:00 p.m. Aug 26, 2026 (Wed 2 weeks before primary). A filing on the last day must be made in person before the Secretary of State (RSA 655:16 / 655:43, II).
  - note: All four dates independently recomputed against a 2026 calendar and confirmed: June 3 is the first Wednesday in June; June 12 is the Friday of the following week; Sept 2 is the Wednesday one week before the Sept 8 (Tue) primary; Aug 5 = 5 weeks before; Aug 26 = 2 weeks before. RSA 655:43, I and 655:14 quotes found verbatim; SOS page lists June 3-12 filing period and the Aug 5 / Aug 26 / Sept 2 deadlines verbatim.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Yes — geographic distribution by congressional district. Of the 3,000 total, 1,500 must come from each of New Hampshire's 2 U.S. congressional districts, and signers must be registered in the respective district (RSA 655:42, I). Nomination papers must be ordered/grouped by municipality when filed with the Secretary of State (RSA 655:22-a / 655:43, I; SOS page).
  - note: RSA 655:42, I quote and SOS '1,500 from each congressional district ... grouped by municipality' quote both found verbatim. Independently corroborated by RSA 655:22-a (petitions ordered alphabetically by municipality) and 655:43, I ('grouped by municipality').
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: No circulator-specific eligibility requirement is prescribed by statute, BUT this rests on statutory silence rather than an affirmative authorization. RSA 655:40-45 regulates only SIGNERS: each signer must be registered to vote at the state general election, no voter may sign more than one nomination paper for the same office, and each voter must personally sign and date an individual nomination paper; certification of signers is done by the local Supervisors of the Checklist (RSA 655:41), not by a circulator. Strictest defensible operating posture until SOS confirms: do not assume non-resident or non-voter circulators are unrestricted — treat circulator status as UNCONFIRMED, and where practical have signatures gathered by NH-registered voters and never rely on a circulator-collected sheet as a substitute for the signer's own personal signature and date.
  - note: RSA 655:40 signer-rule quote found verbatim. Correctness of 'no circulator requirement' hinges on the inference that statutory silence equals no requirement — retrieval cannot settle whether an unwritten SOS administrative practice or form imposes anything on the collector. Held conservatively and routed to an SOS inquiry; the value itself does not over-promise (it flags UNKNOWN), which is the safe direction.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Petition/nomination-paper sheets are NOT notarized and carry NO circulator affidavit; signer validation is done by the Supervisors of the Checklist of the town/ward where the signer is domiciled or registered, who certify whether the signer is a registered voter there (city clerk may perform this) — RSA 655:41. SEPARATELY, the presidential candidate's own Declaration of Intent MUST be signed by the candidate AND notarized by a notary public — RSA 655:17-b, I. So: notarized candidate Declaration of Intent = YES (required); notarized/witnessed petition sheets or circulator certification = NO (supervisor-of-checklist certification instead).
  - note: Both RSA quotes found verbatim — 655:41, I (supervisor certification) and 655:17-b, I ('signed by the candidate, and notarized by a notary public'). The load-bearing, candidate-facing requirement (notarize the Declaration of Intent) is stated expressly in statute and points in the safe/strict direction, so AUTO-LIVE. The 'no petition notarization' element follows from the statutory scheme (certification runs through supervisors, with no circulator oath anywhere in 655:40-45).
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: paper (wet-ink). RSA 655:40 requires that each voter personally sign and date an individual paper nomination form, dated in the year of the election. Papers are physically submitted to the local Supervisors of the Checklist for certification (RSA 655:41) and the certified papers filed in paper with the Secretary of State, grouped by municipality (RSA 655:43, I). There is no digital/online e-petition system for an independent/nomination-paper presidential nomination in New Hampshire; downloadable PDF forms exist but collection and submission remain paper.
  - note: RSA 655:40 quote ('Each voter shall sign and date an individual nomination paper. Nomination papers shall be dated in the year of the election.') found verbatim; SOS 'submit signed nomination papers to Supervisors of the Checklist' quote found verbatim. No statute or SOS material authorizes e-signature for this route; treating capture as paper is the strict/safe reading.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: A fee is required IN ADDITION TO signatures, not as an alternative. A presidential candidate seeking nomination by nomination papers pays a single $250 fee to the Secretary of State at the time of filing the Declaration of Intent, covering both the presidential and vice-presidential candidate (RSA 655:19-a). This does NOT substitute for the 3,000 signatures — both the $250 fee and the full signature count are required. There is no signature-for-fee swap and no indigence petition-in-lieu path for the nomination-paper route (the RSA 655:48 indigence/petition option applies only to the separate presidential PRIMARY $1,000 fee, not to nomination papers).
  - note: RSA 655:19-a quote found verbatim. Adversarial check confirmed: the only fee-waiver/petition-in-lieu mechanism in Chapter 655 (RSA 655:48, II) is tied to the presidential PRIMARY, not the nomination-paper general-election route, so the draft's 'no swap option' is correct. Both fee and signatures are independently required.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Does New Hampshire impose ANY eligibility requirement (age, NH residency, registered-voter status, or in-state status) on the PERSON who circulates/collects signatures on a presidential candidate's nomination papers under RSA 655:40-45, or is the only personal qualification the one applied to the signer? Please confirm there is no circulator affidavit or circulator-residency rule for the independent/nomination-paper presidential route.

All other fields are grounded and correct.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.55

**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Filed with the Secretary of State before 4:00 p.m. of the 99th day preceding the general election (N.J.S.A. 19:13-9 carve-out for presidential electors not nominated at a party convention). The exact calendar date recomputes each cycle as the 99th day before that cycle's general election.

The statute is explicit and the presidential-elector carve-out is correctly identified; no contested interpretation.
