**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. Flat statewide aggregate of signatures of qualified voters of the entire State; no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement. Petition is addressed to (filed with) the Secretary of State.
  - note: Grounded VERBATIM: 19:13-5 ('...office to be filled by the voters of the entire State...in the aggregate...') and 19:13-3 ('Petitions naming candidates for office to be filled by voters of the entire State...shall be addressed to the Secretary of State'). NJ imposes no geographic distribution requirement for statewide office; uncontested. (Independent of the 800-vs-2,000 dispute, which is about quantity, not distribution.)
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: Circulator need not be a registered voter but must be voter-eligible: at least 18 years of age, a resident of New Jersey, a U.S. citizen, and not otherwise disqualified under the NJ Constitution. The candidate may sign and/or circulate their own petition.
  - note: Grounded VERBATIM in 19:13-7 ('shall not be required to be a registered voter, but shall be voter eligible, which means at least 18 years of age, a resident of this State, a citizen of the United States...'); candidate self-circulation confirmed by 19:13-5. Adversarial note flagged in sosInquiries: the NJ-residency bar may be constitutionally vulnerable as applied to an independent general-election presidential circulator (cf. Arsenault v. Way; Buckley v. ACLF), but that doubt cuts toward MORE circulator flexibility, so using only NJ-resident circulators (the value as written) over-complies and cannot threaten ballot access. Value tracks the statute verbatim → LIVE.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Yes — notarized circulator affidavit. Before filing, the circulator (or a candidate who signs/circulates) must make oath by affidavit before a duly qualified officer (notary) that the petition is made in good faith, that the affiant personally circulated it and saw all signatures made, and verily believes the signers are duly qualified voters.
  - note: Grounded VERBATIM: 19:13-7 ('...shall make oath by affidavit before a duly qualified officer that the petition is made in good faith, that the affiant personally circulated the petition and saw all the signatures made thereto and verily believes that the signers are duly qualified voters') and Ballotpedia ('Petition circulators must complete and sign an affidavit. The affidavit must also be notarized'). Current and uncontested.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Hand-circulated paper nominating petition, wet-ink voter signatures, notarized circulator affidavit, filed with the Secretary of State. No standing digital/online petition system. The COVID-era EO 216 (Jan 25, 2021) was a temporary emergency order and is not available for current cycles.
  - note: Grounded VERBATIM: Ballotpedia quotes EO 216 ('...submitted by hand delivery and electronically'; 'signatures to be collected electronically') and correctly frames it as a one-time 2021 emergency order; 19:13-7's wet-ink affidavit requirement supports paper as the standing default. No permanent e-petition system identified. Current and uncontested.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: None. No filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option; ballot access for an independent presidential candidate is by nominating petition (signatures) only.
  - note: Grounded VERBATIM: Ballotpedia ('File a petition with the required number of signatures for the office being sought, including a guarantee that signers are qualified voters...') and 19:13-5 (signatures of qualified voters). No fee or fee-alternative appears in the statutory petition scheme. Uncontested; note this is a negative finding (absence of a fee mechanism) rather than an affirmative 'fee = $0' statement.

### New Mexico
- **signatures:** Signature % DISPUTED: statute = 0.5% of gov vote (1-8-51(B)->1-7-2(A)); NASS = 3%. HOLD to 3% until SoS confirms.
- **deadline:** Deadline DISPUTED: current statute = 23rd day after primary; NASS/Ballotpedia = 21st. HOLD to earlier (21st) date.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: At least 3% of the total vote cast for governor at the last preceding general election at which a governor was elected (strictest defensible figure pending SoS confirmation). NOTE: the statutory chain (NMSA 1-8-51(B) -> 1-7-2(A)) reads to only one-half of one percent (0.5%); the 3% comes from the NASS summary and Ballotpedia's overview blurb and is NOT supported by the statutes those sources cite. Because over-collecting never risks the ballot line but under-collecting is fatal, plan to 3% until the SoS per-cycle Nominating Petition Calculations document gives the controlling exact number.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-51(B) ('signed by a number of voters equal to the number of signatures required to form a new political party'), 1-8-51(A) (basis = total vote for governor at last election), and 1-7-2(A) ('one-half of one percent of the total votes cast for the office of governor') all verified verbatim on FindLaw; NASS '3%' quote verified verbatim in the downloaded PDF. ADVERSARIAL: re-deriving from primary law gives 0.5% (1-8-51(B)->1-7-2(A)); Ballotpedia's statute-citing detail section also says 'one-half of one percent.' The 3% appears to be a propagated error — even the NASS entry cites 1-7-2/1-8-51, which yield 0.5%. But correctness hinges on a statutory cross-reference interpretation retrieval cannot settle, and the controlling per-cycle SoS calculation could not be retrieved. HOLD to the higher (3%) figure to never risk the ballot line.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: File the declaration of independent candidacy and nominating petition between 9:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. on the 21st day following the primary election (strictest/earliest of the two conflicting dates), pending SoS confirmation. Current NMSA 1-8-52(B) text says the 23rd day, but NASS and Ballotpedia say the 21st; treat the earlier (21st) date as the operative deadline so the filing is never late.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-52(B) 'twenty-third day following the primary election' verified verbatim on FindLaw (current as of Jan 1, 2024); NASS '21st day following the primary election' verified verbatim in the PDF; Ballotpedia detail section independently says '21st day.' ADVERSARIAL: genuine conflict between the current statute (23rd) and two secondary sources (21st) — possibly a recent amendment from 21st to 23rd not yet reflected downstream, or a downstream error. Cannot confirm the operative posted date without the SoS filing calendar. A missed deadline is fatal to ballot access, so HOLD to the earlier 21st-day date.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. New Mexico imposes no congressional-district or county distribution requirement on an independent presidential nominating petition; the requirement is a single statewide number tied to the total vote cast for governor at the last preceding general election.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-51(A) and (B) verified verbatim on FindLaw. ADVERSARIAL: read the full text of 1-8-51 (all subsections A-G) and 1-8-49/1-8-50 — none contains any per-district or per-county allocation for the presidential petition; it is a single statewide figure. **🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No separate statutory circulator qualification. The constraint is on SIGNERS, who must each be a registered voter of New Mexico; a voter may not sign more than one independent-presidential petition. The named presidential electors must be registered NM voters (U.S. senators, U.S. representatives, and persons holding federal offices of trust or profit are ineligible). The Election Code specifies no separate age/residency/voter-status requirement for the person who circulates/collects signatures, as distinct from the signers.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-50(D) presidential petition form ('I, the undersigned, a registered voter of New Mexico...' and the no-double-signing declaration) and 1-8-49(D) (electors must be registered NM voters; federal officeholders ineligible) all verified verbatim on FindLaw. ADVERSARIAL: searched 1-8-49 through 1-8-52 for any circulator affidavit/qualification — none exists for this petition (contrast with states that require a circulator oath). The value's claim of no separate circulator rule is accurate to the statute.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: The candidate's declaration of independent candidacy for president (and vice president) must be a sworn statement made under oath and notarized ('Subscribed and sworn to me this ___ day of ___ / notary public'), per NMSA 1-8-49(B)-(C). The signature petition itself carries no circulator affidavit and no notary block; each signer self-certifies as a registered NM voter on the 1-8-50(D) form. So: notarized sworn candidate declaration = YES; circulator/witness certification or notarization of the petition signatures = NONE.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-49 'I make the foregoing affidavit under oath...' and 'Subscribed and sworn to me this ___ day of ___, ... notary public' verified verbatim on FindLaw; 1-8-50(D) petition form (no notary/circulator block) verified verbatim. ADVERSARIAL: the petition form text in 1-8-50(D) contains only signer self-declarations and no notarization line, confirming the petition itself is not notarized while the candidate's declaration is.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. The statute prescribes a physical paper petition (approximately 8.5 x 11 inches, numbered lines spaced ~3/8 inch apart, multi-sheet petitions firmly secured by staple/fastening per 1-8-50(D),(F)). No online/remote e-signature or in-person-digitized system covers an independent presidential nominating petition in New Mexico; signatures must be collected on the prescribed paper form.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-50(D) ('on paper approximately eight and one-half inches wide and eleven inches long with numbered lines for signatures spaced approximately three-eighths of an inch apart') and 1-8-50(F) ('firmly secured by a staple or other suitable fastening') verified verbatim on FindLaw. ADVERSARIAL: no statutory authorization for electronic/remote signature capture for this petition exists in 1-8-49 through 1-8-52; paper is correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. New Mexico provides no filing fee in lieu of (or in addition to) the signature petition for an independent presidential candidate. Ballot access is obtained solely by filing the notarized declaration of independent candidacy plus the signed nominating petition (NMSA 1-8-49(A)); the statute specifies no fee and no fee-for-signatures alternative.
  - note: GROUNDED: 1-8-49(A) ('Nomination as an independent candidate for president or vice president shall be made by filing a declaration of independent candidacy ... The candidate for president shall also at the same time file a nominating petition with the required number of signatures.') verified verbatim on FindLaw; NASS quote verified verbatim in PDF. ADVERSARIAL: nothing in 1-8-49 through 1-8-52 authorizes a fee alternative for the independent presidential route; the 'None' value is correct.

### New York
- **signatures:** 45,000 valid signatures (statutory cap; 1% of 2022 gov vote = 59,123, so 45,000 controls). 500 from each of half the CDs. Collect a large buffer.
- **deadline:** RECOMPUTE PER CYCLE: file 23 weeks before Election Day (was May 28, 2024). 2028 date NOT yet live — do not rely on the 2024 date.
- **risk:** 3 of 7 fields on CONSERVATIVE-HOLD: deadline is a stale 2024 date that must be recomputed for the live cycle; circulator eligibility relies on a court injunction (use NY-registered witnesses to be safe); fee-alternative is an unverified absence claim. Core signature/distribution/capture/witness rules are AUTO-LIVE.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 45,000 valid signatures, OR 1% of the total votes (excluding blank/void) cast for Governor at the last gubernatorial election, whichever is less. 45,000 is the operative cap: 1% of the 2022 gubernatorial vote (5,912,286 total) = 59,123, which exceeds 45,000, so 45,000 controls for the 2024 cycle. Collected by an independent body on a single statewide independent nominating petition naming the presidential/VP candidates and the slate of electors. Recomputes each cycle.
  - note: Citations verbatim at ELN 6-142, SBOE running-president, and ballot-access.org. Independently re-derived: 1% of 5,912,286 (2022 NY gov total, Hochul 3,140,415 + Zeldin 2,762,581 + minor) = 59,122.86 > 45,000, so the 'whichever is less' clause yields 45,000. Confirmed correct and current for 2024; will remain 45,000 unless gubernatorial turnout falls below ~4.5M. Strict guidance: collect a wide buffer (Diane Sare filed 70,000 for the 45,000 requirement).
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Statutory rule (ELN 6-158(9)): an independent nominating petition for an office filled at the general election must be filed not earlier than 24 weeks and not later than 23 weeks preceding the election. STRICTEST READING: treat the 23-weeks-before-Election-Day Tuesday as the hard filing deadline. For 2024 that was May 28, 2024; for any future presidential cycle this MUST be recomputed and confirmed with the SBOE before relying on it. Each named candidate (incl. president/VP) must file an acknowledged certificate of acceptance no later than the 3rd day after the last day to file the petition. EL 1-106 weekend/holiday rollover may apply.
  - note: All citations verbatim (ELN 6-158(9), SBOE running-president acceptance rule, ballot-access.org May 28 corroboration). Date arithmetic independently confirmed: Nov 5, 2024 minus 23 weeks = Tue May 28, 2024 (= 23rd Tuesday preceding); minus 24 weeks = May 21, 2024. HOLD because the value is a PAST 2024-cycle date and the rule recomputes each cycle — the live actionable deadline for the next presidential election is not yet established and must be recomputed/confirmed. Over-comply: do not let a candidate rely on the stale 2024 date.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Yes - a congressional-district distribution requirement applies. At least 500 signatures, OR 1% of enrolled voters (whichever is less), must come from each of one-half of the state's congressional districts (i.e., from at least half of NY's congressional districts). In practice 500 per district controls, since 1% of enrolled voters in any CD far exceeds 500.
  - note: Verbatim at ELN 6-142(1) and SBOE running-president. Independently confirmed: 1% of enrolled voters per CD vastly exceeds 500, so 500 is the binding per-district minimum across at least half the CDs. Current and correct.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: STRICTEST DEFENSIBLE: use witnesses who are duly qualified (registered) New York voters who have not previously signed a petition for another candidate for the same office. (Signers must themselves be NY registered voters qualified to vote for the office who have not signed a designating petition for it.) The Schmidt v. Kosinski permanent injunction (EDNY) expands eligibility to non-registered/non-resident U.S. citizens who sign the special appended statement, and the SBOE currently publishes this expansion - but a campaign should NOT bet ballot access on the injunction; default to registered-NY-voter witnesses.
  - note: Base rule grounded verbatim at ELN 6-140(1)(b); the Schmidt expansion grounded verbatim at SBOE petition-information and running-president pages (SBOE itself states the witness requirements 'have changed' pursuant to the injunction). HOLD because correctness of the EXPANDED rule hinges on the continued force of a court injunction that retrieval cannot guarantee for a future cycle; the over-comply posture for ballot access is to rely only on the base statutory witness rule. SOS inquiry added to confirm the injunction's continued effect.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.94
  - uses: Each petition sheet requires a signed Statement of Witness by a qualified witness, accepted for all purposes as the equivalent of an affidavit and carrying perjury penalties (ELN 6-140(1)(b)). In lieu of the witness statement, the sheet may instead bear a notarial acknowledgment signed by a notary public or commissioner of deeds who swore each signer (ELN 6-140(2)). A non-resident/non-registered witness (per Schmidt v. Kosinski) uses a special appended statement instead. No separate notarization is required when a qualified witness signs.
  - note: Both quotes verbatim in ELN 6-140 (the witness-affidavit-equivalent clause and the 'In lieu of the signed statement of a witness... notary public or commissioner of deeds shall be accepted' clause). Stable statutory text; current and correct. The witness-OR-notary alternative is squarely on the face of the statute.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: paper. Petitions must be on paper, signed in ink, and circulated by hand; the State Board of Elections expressly states electronic signatures are not acceptable. No digital/online petition system covers an independent presidential nominating petition in New York.
  - note: Verbatim at SBOE petition-information ('These forms can be printed and filled out by hand. Electronic signatures are not acceptable.') and ELN 6-140(1)(a) ('Each sheet... shall be signed in ink'). Current and correct; no e-signature path exists.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: Treat ballot access as petition-only. Assume NO filing-fee, bond, or other alternative to the 45,000-signature independent nominating petition exists for an independent presidential candidate; do not rely on any fee shortcut. (Confirm absence directly with the SBOE.)
  - note: The cited running-president quote describes petition CONTENTS, not fees - it does not state 'no fee alternative,' so the value's core assertion ('None') is NOT grounded by the quote provided; it is an absence/negative inference. The conclusion is very likely correct (NY independent presidential access is petition-only with no statutory fee-in-lieu), but a negative cannot be verified verbatim from the supplied citation. HOLD and confirm with SBOE. The strict posture (petition-only) is conservative regardless.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential nominating petition in the upcoming presidential cycle, what is the exact first and last day to file the petition with the State Board of Elections (the 24-week / 23-week window dates), and the exact deadline for each candidate's certificate of acceptance?
  - Is there any filing fee, bond, or other alternative to the 45,000-signature independent nominating petition for a presidential candidate, or is ballot access for an independent presidential candidate available by petition only?
  - Is the Schmidt v. Kosinski permanent injunction (allowing non-registered/non-resident U.S.-citizen petition witnesses to sign the appended statement) still in full effect for the upcoming cycle, and will signatures witnessed under it be accepted without challenge?

### North Carolina
- **signatures:** NC: 1.5% of last gubernatorial turnout = 83,874 (2024 cycle, NCSBE-confirmed) + 200 from each of 3 districts. AUTO-LIVE.
- **deadline:** NC deadline DISPUTED: statute+NCSBE say noon, day of primary (Mar 2024/2026); Ballotpedia says last Fri June. HOLD on earliest.
- **risk:** Two unresolved legal-interpretation conflicts (presidential petition deadline; whether any filing fee applies to an independent presidential candidate) force CONSERVATIVE-HOLD on deadline and feeAlternative; treat the earliest deadline (noon, day of primary) and a possible fee as binding until NCSBE confirms. All citations grounded verbatim; nothing BLOCKED.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Formula-based: signatures equal to 1.5% of the total number of voters who voted in the most recent general election for Governor, plus at least 200 registered voters from each of three different NC congressional districts. For the 2024 gubernatorial base this equals 83,874 (per NCSBE 2026 Unaffiliated Candidate Fact Sheet). Statewide/presidential path runs through G.S. 163-122(a)(1), with G.S. 163-1(c) confirming an unaffiliated presidential candidate qualifies under 163-122 and nominates electors.
  - note: All three citations ground verbatim (FindLaw 163-122, NCSBE unaffiliated-petitions table, FindLaw 163-1(c)). Formula is current and correct. Adversarial note: the draft labels the 2024 integer UNKNOWN, but the NCSBE 2026 official fact sheet explicitly states 83,874 (1.5% of 2024 gubernatorial turnout) for the statewide path — the figure IS confirmable from a primary source, so I relied on it. Minor wording variance (statute 'voters who voted' vs NCSBE 'registered voters who voted'; Ballotpedia 'votes cast for governor') is immaterial in practice. Value recomputes each cycle.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICTEST: petition signature pages due to the county board of elections by 12:00 noon on the DAY OF THE PRIMARY ELECTION (e.g., noon March 5, 2024; noon March 3, 2026 per NCSBE fact sheet) — the earliest of the conflicting candidate deadlines. County-board verification no later than 15 business days after canvass of the primary. Do NOT rely on any later 'last Friday in June' date until NCSBE confirms in writing.
  - note: Both citations ground verbatim. UNRESOLVED CONFLICT for the PRESIDENTIAL contest: statute 163-122(a)(1) + NCSBE petitions table + NCSBE 2026 fact sheet all say 'noon on the day of the primary'; Ballotpedia (citing FEC) says the independent-presidential petition is due 'no later than the last Friday in June' with electors certified by 'the first Friday in August.' Reconciling these requires legal interpretation retrieval cannot settle (whether a presidential-specific timeline supersedes 163-122). Strictest = earliest deadline (day of primary), which is what the draft adopts; held rather than auto-lived because missing the true deadline is catastrophic. Note the draft omits the possible first-Friday-in-August presidential-elector certification step.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Geographic distribution required: at least 200 registered voters from EACH of three NC congressional districts (minimum 200 from each of three different districts). Petition pages must additionally be divided into sections by the county in which signatures were obtained, for county-level verification.
  - note: Citation grounds verbatim in 163-122(a)(1): 'the petition must be signed by at least 200 registered voters from each of three congressional districts in North Carolina. The petitions shall be divided into sections based on the county in which the signatures were obtained.' NCSBE 2026 fact sheet independently confirms '200 registered voters from three different congressional districts.' Adversarial check cleared a stale Ballotpedia phrase ('each of the state's congressional districts') — the statute and the fact sheet both say THREE, so the draft is correct.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.78
  - uses: NC law regulates SIGNERS, not circulators: each signer must be a qualified registered NC voter residing in the applicable county, and no one may sign on behalf of another. No separate statutory circulator (age/residency/voter-status) requirement found for the unaffiliated petition; circulator-specific eligibility is UNKNOWN (no primary source establishes one).
  - note: All three citations ground verbatim (NCSBE petitions page signer language; 'No one may sign a petition on behalf of another person'; statute signer requirement). The value is itself conservative — it asserts the signer rules and explicitly marks circulator eligibility UNKNOWN rather than claiming none exists. That is the strict posture, so no stricter reading is needed. Field rests on absence of a circulator statute, which is consistent with the primary sources reviewed.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: None / not required. Verification is performed by election officials (Executive Director for statewide petitions, or the county board chair), who check signatures against registration records and attach a signed certificate. No notarized affidavit or circulator certification by the petition gatherer is required by G.S. 163-122 or NCSBE petition instructions.
  - note: Citation grounds verbatim in 163-122(a)(1)(a): the Executive Director examines names, check-marks qualified/registered signers, and attaches a signed certificate stating signatures were checked against registration records. No circulator affidavit/notary appears anywhere in 163-122, the NCSBE petitions page, or the 2026 fact sheet. Correct and not interpretation-dependent.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper only. Signatures must be collected on official paper petition sheets, in ink, with original (wet) signatures; electronic signatures are not counted and signatures cannot be collected electronically. No digital/remote-online capture exists for the NC unaffiliated presidential petition.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim on the NCSBE petitions page: 'Signatures cannot be collected electronically.' and 'Signatures must be originals (please use INK); no electronic signatures will be counted. (Photocopies of signed forms are not accepted by county or state elections offices.)' Paper-only is correct and unambiguous.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.55
  - uses: STRICTEST: do NOT assume the office is fee-free. G.S. 163-122(e) requires an unaffiliated candidate to pay the G.S. 163-107 filing fee for the office OR use the G.S. 163-107.1 petition-in-lieu-of-fee alternative; the NCSBE 2026 fact sheet answers 'Is there a filing fee to run as an unaffiliated candidate? Yes.' Treat a filing fee as potentially due for an independent presidential candidate and budget for the G.S. 163-107.1 fee-waiver petition as a hedge until NCSBE confirms in writing whether President carries a $0 fee.
  - note: Both citations ground verbatim (163-122(e) fee-or-alternative language; 163-107 fee-schedule preamble). BUT the draft's CONCLUSION ('no fee for President') is an inference — the 163-107 table lists no 'President/presidential electors' line, so the draft reasons the fee is $0. This conflicts with the NCSBE fact sheet's plain 'Yes' that unaffiliated candidates owe a filing fee, and resolving it requires legal interpretation (does the missing line mean $0, or does the Board apply another basis?). Underpaying a required fee can void the filing, so strict posture = assume a fee may apply and confirm. Held, not auto-lived.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an unaffiliated/independent candidate for President of the United States under G.S. 163-122, is the petition-filing deadline noon on the day of the primary election (per the NCSBE petitions table and G.S. 163-122(a)(1)), or is there a separate presidential-specific deadline (e.g., the last Friday in June, with presidential-elector certification by the first Friday in August)? Please confirm the controlling date for the current cycle.
  - Does an unaffiliated/independent candidate for President of the United States owe any filing fee under G.S. 163-122(e)/G.S. 163-107 given that the G.S. 163-107 fee schedule lists no line item for President or presidential electors, or is the office fee-free? If a fee applies, what is the amount and does the G.S. 163-107.1 petition-in-lieu-of-fee alternative apply?

### North Dakota
- **signatures:** 4,000 signatures (flat statutory number; no distribution)
- **deadline:** 4:00 p.m. on the 64th day before the general election
- **risk:** 7 of 8 fields AUTO-LIVE and grounded against the SOS guide, NASS summary, and primary statute NDCC 16.1-12-02; only witnessOrNotary is on CONSERVATIVE-HOLD because the exact on-form certification block of SFN 58578 is unverifiable (sos.nd.gov form server returns HTTP 522, reproduced independently).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 4,000 qualified North Dakota electors (flat statutory number, not a percentage; does not recompute per cycle). Independent and non-established-party presidential candidates use the same form (SFN 58578), checking the 'independent candidate' box for the independent path. Authority: NDCC 16.1-12-02(3).
  - note: SOS-guide quote and NASS quote both ground verbatim (SOS running-president.pdf lines 50-53; NASS report lines 803-806). Independently confirmed against primary statute NDCC 16.1-12-02 subsection 3 (FindLaw, current as of Jan 1 2024): 'If the nomination is for the office of president, there must be no fewer than four thousand signatures.' Flat number, current and correct for an independent presidential candidate.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: 4:00 p.m. on the 64th day before the November general election (statutory rule, NDCC 16.1-12-02). The complete filing (petition + affidavit of candidacy + statement of interests + certificate(s) of nomination of presidential electors) must be in the physical possession of the Secretary of State's office by that deadline. The 2024 instance of this rule was September 3, 2024; the date shifts each cycle to the 64th day before that November election.
  - note: SOS-guide quote (lines 85-93) and NASS quote (lines 803-806) ground verbatim. Primary statute confirms: petition 'shall submit ... before four p.m. on the sixty-fourth day before the general election.' Relied value is the recurring 64th-day rule, not the one-cycle Sept 3 2024 date. Physical-possession requirement confirmed in SOS guide.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. A single statewide total of 4,000 qualified-elector signatures; no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement (ND has one at-large U.S. House district). NDCC 16.1-12-02(3).
  - note: NASS quote grounds verbatim (lines 805-806). Adversarially checked the statute: subsection 3 (president) sets only the flat 4,000 figure with no geographic distribution. The 2%-of-district rule in subsection 2 applies to sub-state district offices, NOT to president. No distribution rule appears in SOS guide, NASS summary, or the statute. None confirmed.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Circulators of this presidential nominating petition are NOT required to be ND qualified electors (no age/residency/voter-status requirement on circulators). The petition may not be circulated or signed before January 1 of the presidential election year. Signers must be qualified ND electors (U.S. citizen, 18+, 30 days' ND residency). Note: ND initiative/ballot-measure petitions under ch. 16.1-01 are different (resident circulators + notarized affidavits) and must not be conflated.
  - note: SOS-guide quote grounds verbatim (lines 74-77): 'Petition circulators do not need to be ND qualified electors.' Statute confirms the Jan-1 signing window and exempts presidential petitions from the general form spec (16.1-11-16). Adversarial nuance: statute 16.1-12-02(3) requires the elector NOMINEES to be qualified ND electors, but that is a requirement on the presidential electors named on the petition, not on circulators or signers, so it does not contradict this field.
**🟡 witnessOrNotary** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Strictest posture: ASSUME the SFN 58578 petition may carry a circulator certification or affidavit block that must be completed (and possibly notarized) before filing, and prepare to satisfy it; do NOT assume the signatures need no certification. The candidate Affidavit of Candidacy (SFN 52500) is independently required in any case. Cited sources (SOS guide, NASS, statute 16.1-12-02/16.1-11-16) describe no notary requirement on the signatures, but the exact on-form certification wording is UNCONFIRMED.
  - note: Cited quotes ground verbatim (SOS guide line 59-61; NASS lines 803-806). Statute exempts presidential petitions from 16.1-11-16, and 16.1-11-16 itself contains no notary/circulator-affidavit clause, which supports the draft's reading. HOWEVER the precise certification block printed on form SFN 58578 could not be retrieved: the nd.gov/sos.nd.gov form server returns HTTP 522, which I reproduced independently via both curl and wick. Because the form's actual certification wording could change the answer and cannot be settled by retrieval, held conservatively and an SOS inquiry is filed.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: paper. Signatures are collected on the paper Petition/Certificate of Nomination (SFN 58578); the complete filing must be in the physical possession of the Secretary of State's office by the deadline. ND has no remote/online or in-person-digitized signature-capture system for this presidential nominating petition.
  - note: Both SOS-guide quotes ground verbatim (lines 91-93 and 50-53). Physical-possession requirement plus paper SFN 58578 confirmed by statute (petition 'submitted' to SOS). No online-capture path exists for this petition.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. No state filing fee for the independent/non-established-party presidential nominating petition and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative; the 4,000-signature petition is the sole ballot-access mechanism. The $5,000 figure in the SOS guide is the federal FECA registration trigger (a campaign-finance obligation), NOT a state ballot-access fee.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim (SOS guide lines 89-92; NASS lines 803-806). No filing fee appears in the SOS complete-filing checklist, the NASS summary, or statute 16.1-12-02. The $5,000 FECA figure is correctly characterized as federal, not a state fee. Adversarially: statute lists petition contents only, no fee.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Does the Petition/Certificate of Nomination form (SFN 58578) for a non-established-party / independent presidential candidate require a circulator certification or notarized circulator affidavit, or is the candidate Affidavit of Candidacy (SFN 52500) the only sworn document in a complete filing? Please confirm the exact certification block printed on SFN 58578.

### Ohio
- **signatures:** 5,000 valid (max 15,000); fixed number, no per-district minimum
- **deadline:** 90th day before general (Aug 7, 2024); recomputes each cycle
- **risk:** Core petition rule (5,000 sigs, 90-day, paper wet-ink, no notary) is grounded and AUTO-LIVE; two CONSERVATIVE-HOLDs: circulator residency depends on current injunction status, and the "no fee alternative" rests on a statutory gap (president absent from the 3513.10 fee schedule) that needs SOS confirmation.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 5,000 valid signatures of qualified electors (statewide minimum), with petitions rejected if they purport to contain more than 15,000 signatures. Fixed statutory number, not a percentage; does not recompute by cycle.
  - note: R.C. 3513.257(A) quote confirmed verbatim on FindLaw ('no less than five thousand qualified electors ... no petition shall be accepted ... more than fifteen thousand signatures'). Ballotpedia quote confirmed verbatim (line 234: 'at least 5,000 qualified voters'). NASS report independently corroborates 'at least 5,000 qualified electors.' Independently re-derived and correct for an independent presidential candidate. Minor caveat: the parenthetical extending the same 5,000 threshold to a 'new/minor-party presidential candidate' is loose (minor-party ballot status runs through a separate party-formation/petition mechanism), but it does not affect the independent-candidate value relied upon.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Not later than 4 p.m. of the 90th day before the general election. For 2024 (general election Nov. 5, 2024) this was August 7, 2024. Statement of candidacy + nominating petition + a sufficient slate of presidential electors must be filed with the Secretary of State by that time. The 90-day rule recomputes each cycle. HB2 (2024 special session) moved only the major-party certification deadline to the 65th day; it did not change the independent-candidate petition deadline.
  - note: R.C. 3513.257 quote confirmed verbatim ('not later than four p.m. of the ninetieth day before the day of the general election'). NASS report quote confirmed verbatim (lines 846-848) and independently corroborates the 90th-day independent-candidate deadline AND the HB2 note that the 65th-day change applies only to MAJOR-PARTY certification (NASS lines 835-839), exactly as the draft claims. Date arithmetic independently verified: 90 days before Nov 5, 2024 = Aug 7, 2024 (Wednesday). Statute also confirms the presidential-elector slate must be submitted at filing. Value is current and correct; the specific date is cycle-specific and recomputes.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. The 5,000-signature requirement is a single statewide total; no minimum number of signatures per congressional district or per county. Mechanically, each petition paper must contain signatures of electors of only one county and separate papers are used per county, but no geographic distribution minimum is imposed.
  - note: R.C. 3513.257(A) and R.C. 3513.261 quotes both confirmed verbatim on FindLaw. Independently re-derived: 3513.257 sets one statewide aggregate (5,000) with no district/county allocation; 3513.261's one-county-per-paper rule is a sorting/validity mechanic, not a distribution quota. Adversarial note worth flagging to staff (does not change the gate): 3513.261 further provides that if a single petition paper mixes counties, the board counts only signatures from the majority county and invalidates the rest — a paper-integrity rule, still not a geographic distribution minimum.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: A circulator of a nominating petition for presidential electors must be at least 18 years of age (R.C. 3503.06(C)(1)(b)). STRICTEST POSTURE: also assume the circulator may need to be an Ohio resident — the general residency requirement in R.C. 3503.06(C)(1)(a) is on the books and is reported as non-enforced only by virtue of the Citizens in Charge v. Husted injunction, an enforcement-status fact that retrieval cannot durably confirm as current. Plan for resident, 18+ circulators. Circulators need not be registered voters. Signers must be registered Ohio electors qualified to vote on the candidacy (R.C. 3501.38(A)).
  - note: R.C. 3503.06(C)(1)(b) quote (age 18, presidential-elector petition) confirmed verbatim; Hamilton County 2024 guide quote confirmed verbatim (lines 47-50, including the Citizens in Charge v. Husted citations); R.C. 3501.38(A) signer-qualification quote confirmed verbatim. The age-18 and signer requirements are AUTO-LIVE-grade. HOLD is driven solely by the residency claim: whether the statutory Ohio-residency requirement is currently unenforced depends on the live status of a federal injunction, which is a currency/legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle to the strict standard. Defaulting to the over-comply posture (assume residency may apply) avoids any ballot-access risk.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: No notarization required. Each petition paper requires a circulator statement made UNDER PENALTY OF ELECTION FALSIFICATION (not before a notary) attesting to the number of signatures, that the circulator witnessed the affixing of every signature, that all signers were to the best of the circulator's knowledge and belief qualified to sign, and that every signature is genuine. Each petition must also carry the boldface warning that election falsification is a fifth-degree felony.
  - note: R.C. 3501.38(E)(1) circulator-statement quote and 3501.38(J) boldface-felony-warning quote both confirmed verbatim on FindLaw. R.C. 3513.261's prescribed petition form independently shows the same circulator declaration ('under penalty of election falsification ... witnessed the affixing of every signature') with no notary jurat. Statute uses 'penalty of election falsification' rather than notarization throughout. Value is current and correct; no notary/witness requirement exists.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Signatures must be collected on the official paper nominating petition with signatures affixed in ink or indelible pencil. Ohio provides no remote-online or in-person digital signature system for an independent presidential nominating petition; the petition is wet-ink paper filed with the Secretary of State.
  - note: R.C. 3513.261 quote ('All signatures on nominating petitions shall be written in ink or indelible pencil') and R.C. 3501.38(B) quote ('Signatures shall be affixed in ink') both confirmed verbatim on FindLaw. Independently re-derived: ink/indelible-pencil wet-signature paper petition, no statutory e-signature alternative for nominating petitions. The specific form name 'Form 3-O' is non-load-bearing color not appearing in the cited statutory quotes, but the substantive paper/wet-ink mode is fully grounded and correct.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.68
  - uses: Treat ballot access as obtainable only via the 5,000-signature nominating petition; there is no money-payment alternative to gathering signatures for an independent presidential candidate. STRICTEST POSTURE: do not assume a fee can substitute for signatures, and confirm with the SOS whether any nominal filing fee is nonetheless owed at filing under R.C. 3513.261. The 3513.10(A)/(B) fee tables and the 3513.10(G) 'statewide office' definition do not list president/vice-president, creating an interpretive gap as to what (if any) fee 3513.261's cross-reference produces.
  - note: R.C. 3513.261 fee-cross-reference quote and R.C. 3513.10(G) 'statewide office' definition quote both confirmed verbatim on FindLaw. Adversarial finding: the draft's CONCLUSION (no fee alternative; president absent from the fee schedule) is correct as far as the texts go, but bridging '3513.261 says pay the 3513.10(A)/(B) fee for the office' with '3513.10 lists no fee for president' requires a legal interpretation (does the office owe $0, or is the fee provision simply inapplicable?) that retrieval cannot definitively settle. Because the load-bearing point for ballot access is that signatures are the route (which is safe regardless), HOLD with the over-comply posture and route the fee-amount question to the SOS.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential (president/vice-president) nominating petition filed under R.C. 3513.257, is a petition circulator currently required to be an Ohio resident, or does R.C. 3503.06(C)(1)(b) (age 18 only) plus the Citizens in Charge v. Husted injunction mean no residency requirement is enforced for the 2024/2028 cycle?
  - For an independent candidate for president/vice-president, is any filing fee owed at the time of filing the nominating petition under R.C. 3513.261? The 3513.10(A)/(B) fee schedule and the 3513.10(G) 'statewide office' definition do not list president/vice-president — please confirm the fee amount (if any) and that there is no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative.

### Oklahoma
- **signatures:** 3% of last gubernatorial vote (34,599 for 2024); recomputes each cycle — HOLD on the stale number
- **deadline:** July 15 of presidential election year (fixed statutory date) — LIVE
- **risk:** All 7 citations grounded verbatim in primary sources. Hard mechanics (deadline, notary, paper-only capture, $35,000 fee) are AUTO-LIVE. Holds are on the cycle-stale signature number and three negative-inference claims (no distribution quota, circulator residency) that retrieval cannot settle — over-comply by treating the formula (not 34,599) as live and assuming no distribution/residency relief beyond what the form states.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: At least 3% of the total votes cast in the last General Election for Governor. The signature count recomputes each presidential cycle off the most recent gubernatorial general election; rely on this formula, not a fixed number. (For the 2024 cycle the figure was 34,599 = 3% of 1,153,284, but that is a prior-cycle number and the 2028 figure depends on the Nov. 2026 gubernatorial vote, not yet held as of 2026-06-07.)
  - note: GROUNDED: packet lines 101-111 (3% language + Total Votes 1,153,284 / 34,599) and NASS lines 867-868 confirmed verbatim. Independently re-derived: 1,153,284 x 3% = 34,598.52 -> 34,599, and 2022 gubernatorial total of 1,153,284 confirmed against Ballotpedia citing OK SEB certified results. The 3% RULE is correct and current. HOLD reason is temporal currency, not citation failure: 34,599 is the 2024-cycle figure; the live number for the next cycle is not yet determinable. Strictest treatment is to rely on the formula and avoid presenting the stale count as the current requirement.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: July 15 of the presidential election year. An independent presidential candidate must file the Statement of Candidacy (with petition or filing fee) with the Secretary of the State Election Board no later than July 15 of a presidential election year (26 O.S. Sec. 10-101.1(A)(1)). For 2024 the last day was Monday, July 15, 2024.
  - note: GROUNDED: packet line 144 (statute: 'no later than July 15 of a presidential election year'), line 35 ('Monday, July 15, 2024'), and NASS line 869 confirmed verbatim. Fixed statutory date, not a cycle-variable number, so it remains live. The draft's '30 days' detail is correctly the Secretary's petition-sufficiency determination window (packet lines 38, 166), not a separate candidate deadline; it does not affect the July 15 filing deadline.
**🟡 distributionRule** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Strictest defensible: treat the single-county-per-page rule as a binding mandatory format requirement — each petition page must contain only registered voters from one Oklahoma county; do not mix counties on a sheet. Do NOT assume any relief beyond this: presence/absence of a per-county or per-district signature-distribution quota is not established by the form and should be confirmed with the Election Board before relying on 'no quota.'
  - note: GROUNDED: packet lines 113 and 163 ('Each page... shall contain the names of registered voters from a single county') confirmed verbatim. But the draft's headline conclusion ('no geographic distribution quota') is a NEGATIVE INFERENCE (proving absence of a requirement) that retrieval cannot settle. The single-county-per-page rule IS confirmed; whether a distribution minimum exists elsewhere in 26 O.S. is not. Hold and over-comply by treating the per-page county rule as strict and not assuming quota relief.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Confirmed: circulator must be at least 18 years old and attest all signatures were signed in their presence; signers must be registered Oklahoma voters of the county listed on the page (packet lines 358, 373). STRICTEST treatment of the unconfirmed part: assume the circulator may also need to be a registered Oklahoma voter/resident — do NOT rely on the claim that there is 'no residency requirement beyond age 18' until confirmed with the Election Board.
  - note: GROUNDED: packet line 373 ('at least eighteen (18) years old and that all signatures... were signed in my presence') and line 358 (signer voter-certification) confirmed verbatim. The age-18 and in-presence requirements are solid. But the draft's assertion that the packet imposes 'no separate Oklahoma-residency requirement on the circulator' is a NEGATIVE INFERENCE; circulator residency/voter-registration status is genuinely ambiguous from the form. Hold and assume the stricter requirement pending office confirmation.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Notarization required in two places: (1) the candidate's Statement of Candidacy oath must be witnessed by a notary public; and (2) each petition page's circulator affidavit ('TO BE COMPLETED BY PERSON CIRCULATING PETITION') must be signed and sworn before a notary public.
  - note: GROUNDED: packet line 152 ('the candidate's signature shall be witnessed by a notary public'), line 372 ('TO BE COMPLETED BY PERSON CIRCULATING PETITION'), and line 379 ('Signed and sworn to before me on') all confirmed verbatim. Both notarization points are directly stated in the statute text and the prescribed form. No interpretation needed.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: paper. Oklahoma uses a paper petition on the form prescribed by the Secretary of the State Election Board (packet Page 10), circulated and signed in wet ink, organized by county, with a notarized circulator affidavit. There is no online/remote or digitized-signature system for an independent presidential petition; the only non-petition alternative is the paper filing fee. Submission is by mail, private delivery service, or in person.
  - note: GROUNDED: packet line 114 ('Candidates must use the provided petition form (Page 10)') and lines 58-60 ('may be submitted by mail, private delivery service or in person') confirmed verbatim. No evidence of any electronic/online signature path; paper-only is the correct and current capture mode.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Yes — a filing fee may be submitted in lieu of the petition. For the current/2024 cycle the fee is $5,000 per Presidential Elector; Oklahoma has 7 electors, so the total is $35,000, payable by cashier's check or certified check to the Secretary of the State Election Board (campaign checks, personal checks, and cash are not accepted). Statutory per-elector basis: 26 O.S. Sec. 10-101.1 referencing the fee in Sec. 20-102.
  - note: GROUNDED: packet lines 90-96 ('thirty-five thousand dollars ($35,000.00)... five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) for each Presidential Elector... seven (7) Presidential Electors... Campaign checks, personal checks, and cash cannot be accepted') and line 168 ('in lieu of the petition... a filing fee... may be submitted') confirmed verbatim. Minor currency caveat: the per-elector fee is statutorily tied to 26 O.S. Sec. 20-102; the $5,000/$35,000 figures are the packet's stated amounts for the current cycle, so they are grounded for now but worth reconfirming each cycle (captured in the SOS inquiry).

### Oregon
- **signatures:** ~23,744 valid signatures (1% of 2020 presidential vote, 2,374,321); confirm SOS-certified count
- **deadline:** Filing deadline Aug 25, 2026 (70th day before 11/3 election); submit by ~Aug 11 for guaranteed verification
- **risk:** Core ballot-access rule is solid and grounded; treat the precise signature count and circulator eligibility details as unconfirmed (over-collect signatures; do not assume any circulator-eligibility leniency) until SOS confirms.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Petition path (Individual Electors): valid signatures of active registered Oregon electors equal to not less than 1% of the total votes cast for all candidates for presidential electors at the last general election (ORS 249.735). For the 2024/2026 baseline (2020 Oregon presidential total = 2,374,321) that is approximately 23,744 (1% rounded up), but the operative requirement is the EXACT figure certified by the Secretary of State for the cycle; collect a comfortable cushion above 23,744. Names of the presidential electors must be filed with the petition. Alternative: nomination by an Assembly of at least 1,000 electors gathered in one place for no longer than 12 hours.
  - note: All three citations confirmed verbatim: NASS PDF (lines 902-905: '...signatures of individual electors equal to not less than 1% of the total votes cast for all candidates for presidential electors...names of the presidential electors must be filed with the petition'), Ballotpedia ('...at least 1 percent of the total votes cast for presidential electors...'), Wikipedia total 2,374,321 (the official Total row). Independent re-derivation: 1% of 2,374,321 = 23,743.21, rounds up to 23,744 -> draft's ~23,744 is correct. CONSERVATIVE-HOLD because the precise operative count is set/certified by the SOS each cycle (draft itself flags this); the '~23,744' is a derived estimate, not the certified figure. The 1% legal rule itself is unambiguous; only the exact number needs SOS confirmation. Strictest defensible stance: treat 23,744 as a floor, over-collect, and verify the certified number before relying on it.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 70th day before the general election (ORS 249.722). For the November 3, 2026 general election that date is August 25, 2026. The certificate of nomination / petition signatures and the names of presidential electors must be filed by this deadline. SOS strongly advises submitting signatures earlier for verification time (the 2024 advice was 8/13/24); the 2026 guaranteed-verification signature submission date is on or about August 11, 2026 (signatures must be received at least 10 business days before the filing deadline).
  - note: Independently verified the date math: Election Day 2026 = Tuesday Nov 3, 2026; 70 days before = Tuesday Aug 25, 2026 (exact match). SOS 2026 calendar row confirmed: 'August 25, 2026 / Last day for nonaffiliated or minor political party candidate, other than elected incumbent...to file certificate of nomination / 249.722 / -70' (calendar lines 1514-1558; reassembled across the PDF table columns, every token verbatim). NASS 70th-day quote verbatim (PDF lines 902-905). Ballotpedia 8/13/24 advice verbatim (line 592). The Aug 11, 2026 guaranteed-verification date is corroborated in the SOS calendar (lines 1398-1400) and the manual's 10-business-day rule (lines 1066-1067). Statutory date, no interpretation.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None for a nonaffiliated/independent presidential candidate. The 1%-of-presidential-vote petition is a single statewide total with no per-county or per-congressional-district distribution quota. Signers should sign a petition sheet designated for their county of residence for sorting/verification only, which is not a distribution requirement. The 100-signatures-per-congressional-district rule applies to major-party statewide partisan petitions-in-lieu-of-fee and to nonpartisan statewide offices (Labor Commissioner, appellate judges), NOT to the nonaffiliated presidential petition.
  - note: Both citations confirmed. NASS quote verbatim (flat statewide 1%, no distribution language). SOS manual county-sheet quote is verbatim but split across the PDF two-column break: 'Sign a petition sheet that is designated for' (line 1903) + 'their county of residence, if applicable.' (line 1932) form one continuous bullet. Independently confirmed the draft's congressional-district caveat is correct: the 100-per-CD rule appears at manual lines 740-742 (major-party statewide partisan petition) and lines 1384-1401 (nonpartisan statewide: Labor Commissioner, appellate judges), and is absent from the Individual Electors presidential petition definition. Line 1796 confirms county sorting is a verification convenience ('sheets are sorted by county if required'), not a quota. No real interpretation needed; primary sources are unambiguous.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: Do NOT assume any circulator-eligibility leniency. Confirmed by the manual: every circulator must personally witness each signature and complete the circulator certification with a legal signature and date; an insufficient certification rejects the sheet; circulator pay status must be designated on the SEL 114 prospective-petition form. The candidate must be registered to vote as a nonaffiliated voter at least 180 days before the filing deadline (deadline to register nonaffiliated = February 26, 2026). UNVERIFIED and treated strictly: the manual does NOT affirmatively state there is no circulator age/residency/voter-registration requirement (the draft infers this from silence), and it does NOT affirmatively state that paid circulators must register with the SOS for candidate petitions. Pending SOS confirmation, assume circulators may need to meet eligibility requirements and that paid circulators may need to register.
  - note: All three citations confirmed verbatim (manual lines 1816-1819 circulator definition; lines 917-918 prospective petition / pay status; lines 904-906 180-day nonaffiliated registration; cross-confirmed Feb 26, 2026 at quick-guide line 8 and manual line 907). 'Personally witness each signature' also verbatim (lines 1826/1830). DISAGREE / interpretationRequired because the VALUE makes two claims weaker than the sources support: (1) 'no age/residency/voter-registration requirement' is inferred from ABSENCE of a stated rule -- absence is not proof none exists (the draft openly flags this), and (2) 'Paid circulators must be registered with the SOS' is NOT affirmatively stated in the manual (the manual only references 'a paid circulator's registration' in the legal-signature definition, lines 1842/1979). Strictest defensible interpretation: do not rely on circulator leniency; assume eligibility limits and paid-circulator registration may apply until SOS confirms. Routed to sosInquiries.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Individual Electors petition path: NO notarization. The circulator must personally witness each signature and complete a circulator certification (legal signature + date) on each signature sheet; an incomplete/insufficient certification rejects the sheet. Notarization is required only for the alternative Assembly of Electors path (SEL 115 certificate of nomination executed and notarized by the assembly's presiding officer and secretary) and for the minor-party SEL 110 form.
  - note: All three citations confirmed verbatim: certification-by-signing quote (manual lines 1977-1978), 'Personally witness each signature collected' (lines 1826/1830, split across columns), and 'Notarized form SEL 115...executed by the presiding officer and secretary of the assembly' (lines 1056-1057). Independently confirmed the SEL 110 minor-party notarization claim (manual lines 296, 893-894, 2257). The Individual Electors path nowhere requires notarization. Correct and current; no interpretation.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.94
  - uses: paper. The candidate files the prospective petition / certificate of nomination and gathers wet-ink signatures on Elections Division-issued paper signature-sheet templates; circulators must personally witness and certify each sheet. The manual states minor party and nonaffiliated candidates in the general election must file paper forms. ORESTAR is used only for the separate Voters' Pamphlet statement and fee-based primary/nonpartisan filings, not for collecting the nonaffiliated presidential nominating-petition signatures. No remote-online or digitized signature system covers an independent presidential petition.

**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: There is NO filing-fee alternative to the signature requirement for a nonaffiliated presidential candidate. Ballot access at the general election is obtained ONLY by (1) the Individual Electors petition (1% of presidential vote) or (2) an Assembly of at least 1,000 electors. No fee-in-lieu path exists. A separate optional Voters' Pamphlet filing fee exists solely to appear in the pamphlet (payable or substitutable with a separate pamphlet petition) and is not a route onto the ballot.
  - note: All three citations confirmed: quick-guide Individual Electors quote verbatim incl. source typo 'By submit' (lines 10-12); NASS Assembly-of-1,000 quote verbatim (PDF lines 907-908); Voters'-Pamphlet pay-or-petition quote verbatim (quick-guide lines 35-39). Independently confirmed the two-and-only-two ballot routes for nonaffiliated candidates (quick-guide lines 9-13; manual Individual Electors / Assembly sections) with no fee-in-lieu option onto the ballot. The Voters' Pamphlet fee is explicitly a separate publication matter, not ballot access. Correct; no interpretation.

### Pennsylvania
- **signatures:** President: 5,000 valid signatures (court-fixed) + $200 fee — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** Deadline HOLD: not a fixed Aug 1 — first day of Aug, rolled to next business day (Aug 3 in 2026); confirm per cycle
- **risk:** All 8 fields grounded verbatim, but every citation is the 2024 (presidential-cycle) DOS instructions; today is 2026 (a midterm with no presidential race) so the next live cycle is 2028. Substantive rules (5,000 sigs, no distribution, paper-only, fee-plus-sigs, circulator no-residency/no-affidavit) re-confirmed unchanged in the 2026 instructions, but the date-specific deadline is stale and the circulator age/registration qualification is unknown — these two are held.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 5,000 valid signatures of qualified registered electors of Pennsylvania for President (statewide nomination papers under 25 P.S. § 2911 et seq.). The 2% statutory calculation in § 2911(b) is not enforced per Constitution Party of Pa. v. Cortés (E.D. Pa. Feb. 1, 2018); DOS applies a fixed 5,000 for President, U.S. Senator, and Governor, and 2,500 for all other statewide offices.
  - note: Quote verbatim in NASS PDF (PA section) and in the PB 2024 instructions both narratively ("...except for the offices of President of the United States, United States Senator, or Governor, which require 5,000 signatures") and in the signature table ("President of the United States 5,000"). Re-confirmed UNCHANGED in the active 2026 DOS instructions (same 5,000 language) and independently corroborated by Ballotpedia. Court-order basis stated correctly.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: Do NOT treat the deadline as a fixed "August 1." The statutory/consent-decree deadline is the first day of August, administered by DOS and rolled to the next business day when Aug 1 falls on a weekend/holiday: it was August 1, 2024 (Thu) for the 2024 presidential cycle but August 3, 2026 (Mon, because Aug 1, 2026 is a Saturday) for the 2026 cycle. For the next presidential cycle (2028), Aug 1 is a Tuesday, so the operative date is likely Aug 1, 2028 — but this MUST be confirmed against DOS's published 2028 calendar before relied upon. Filing is with the Bureau of Elections / Secretary of the Commonwealth, Room 201 North Office Building, Harrisburg, by 5:00 P.M. on that date. Strictest posture: assume the earliest plausible date (first business day of August), never assume any date later than the first of August is safe.
  - note: Quotes are grounded verbatim in PB 2024 instructions, but they are 2024-specific (circulation Feb 14–Aug 1, 2024). The draft generalizes this to "August 1 of the election year," which is FALSE: the active 2026 DOS instructions set the deadline to August 3, 2026 (Aug 1 is a Saturday). The deadline recomputes per cycle and is calendar-dependent; correctness for a current/2028 independent presidential candidate cannot be settled by retrieving the 2024 document. Held to strictest interpretation.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None for President. There is no per-congressional-district or per-county minimum for a statewide presidential nomination paper — only the single statewide total of 5,000. Signers are organized by county solely as a clerical matter (each two-sided sheet must contain signers from one county, with that county noted); there is no per-county/per-district minimum. The historical "severe distribution requirement" applied only to statewide STATE offices, not to President.
  - note: "County of Signers" quote and the 5,000 table entry are verbatim in PB 2024. The 2026 instructions confirm the same county-per-page clerical rule with no per-county minimum for statewide. Ballotpedia citation note 19 independently confirms the distribution requirement attaches to statewide STATE office, not President. No distribution minimum for President is correct and current.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.85
  - uses: No in-state residency requirement and no circulator affidavit requirement for political-body nomination papers (covers independent/minor-party presidential papers) — both eliminated by amendment to 25 P.S. § 2911(d); the circulator need not be a PA resident. UNKNOWN whether any minimum-age or voter-registration qualification applies to the circulator: DOS instructions specify only that residency and the affidavit were removed and are silent on circulator age/registration. Strictest posture: do not assume any person may circulate; treat circulator age/registration as an open question pending DOS confirmation.
  - note: "...eliminated the in-state residency requirement and the affidavit requirement for circulators of nomination papers for all political bodies" is verbatim in PB 2024 and re-confirmed verbatim in the 2026 instructions. The grounded claim is correct and current. Held only because the draft itself flags an UNKNOWN (circulator age/registration) that retrieval cannot resolve; an SOS inquiry is added rather than asserting "anyone may circulate."
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Circulator: a "Statement of Circulator" must be filled in and signed on every sheet after all signatures are obtained, but the notarized circulator affidavit was eliminated (no notarization of the circulator statement). Candidate: must file a Candidate's Affidavit, normally notarized; under Act 2020-15 (signed Apr 20, 2020) the candidate may instead submit an unsworn Candidate's Declaration along with the affidavit in lieu of notarization.
  - note: "Every sheet... Statement of Circulator filled in and signed" and the Act 2020-15 unsworn-statement language are verbatim in PB 2024; the candidate notarization/declaration language is verbatim on the live DOS third-party page. All re-confirmed UNCHANGED in the active 2026 instructions. Correct and current.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Signatures must be collected on the official two-sided printed nomination paper (legal-size 8.5 x 14, printed 2-sided head-to-head); each signer personally signs with printed name, residence, and date (wet ink). Filing is in person or by mail; no online/digital signature-collection system exists for political-body/presidential nomination papers — DOS provides only blank printable forms.
  - note: "Nomination papers must be printed 2-sided on 8 1/2 x 14\" paper, head to head" verbatim on the live DOS third-party page; "Each signer must personally sign... printed name, place of residence and the date of signing" verbatim in PB 2024. The 2026 instructions confirm "Pages are double-sided." Paper-only with no e-signature option is correct and current.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: $200.00 filing fee for President, required IN ADDITION TO (not in lieu of) the 5,000 signatures — there is no signature-vs-fee alternative; both are required. The fee must accompany the nomination papers, paid by certified check or money order payable to the "Commonwealth of Pennsylvania" (no personal checks or cash).
  - note: "For Statewide offices (President of the United States...) — $200.00" and the CERTIFIED CHECK/MONEY ORDER payment language are verbatim in PB 2024; NASS confirms "a $200 fee, and nomination papers containing the signatures of 5000 qualified electors." The 2026 instructions and the live DOS page confirm the certified-check/money-order requirement. PA has no fee-vs-signature substitution; fee is additive. Correct and current.
