  - For an independent/political-body candidate for President of the United States, what is the exact last day to file statewide nomination papers in the next presidential cycle (2028), given that the deadline is administered as the first day of August rolled to the next business day (e.g., Aug 1 in 2024 but Aug 3 in 2026)?
  - Other than the eliminated in-state residency and affidavit requirements, does Pennsylvania impose any minimum-age or voter-registration qualification on a circulator of political-body nomination papers?

### Rhode Island
- **signatures:** 1,000 signatures (flat statewide aggregate) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** File w/ local board 60 days before general (Sep 6 in 2024) — HOLD: date recomputes each cycle
- **risk:** 7 of 8 fields grounded and AUTO-LIVE; only the deadline is held because the specific calendar date is cycle-specific and one cited URL (justia §17-14-12) was unreachable, though the operative 60-day statutory rule is grounded verbatim elsewhere.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 1,000 signatures of registered voters, in the aggregate (a flat statewide number, not a percentage). Per RI Gen. Laws § 17-14-7(a), nomination papers of an independent candidate for presidential elector must be signed, in the aggregate, by at least 1,000 voters. Fixed statutory figure; does not recompute per cycle.
  - note: All three citations ground VERBATIM: findlaw §17-14-7(a) ('signed, in the aggregate, by at least one thousand (1,000) voters'); SOS Nominations page table ('President of the United States | 1000'); Ballotpedia presidential page ('This petition must contain 1,000 signatures'). Adversarial check: the §17-14-7 'for the 2020 election only' reduction to 500 applied ONLY to US Senator and Representative in Congress, NOT to presidential elector, and has expired — so president remains at 1,000. Current and correct.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.82
  - uses: Operative candidate deadline: signed nomination papers must be returned to the local Board of Canvassers no later than 60 days before the general election (RI Gen. Laws § 17-14-11(a)). For Nov 5, 2024 that date was September 6, 2024 (matching the SOS official calendar). Separately, local boards must file certified papers with the Secretary of State no later than 54 days before the election (§ 17-14-12; Sept 12, 2024). STRICT reliance: treat the 60-day-before-general local-board filing as binding and RECONFIRM the exact calendar date against the SOS election calendar for each cycle — the specific date recomputes annually.
  - note: Facts grounded: findlaw §17-14-11(a) ('shall be filed not later than sixty (60) days prior to the general election') VERBATIM; SOS page ('Presidential Electors | September 6') VERBATIM; §17-14-12 54-day boards-to-SOS deadline VERBATIM on findlaw. Date math confirms Nov 5 2024 −60d = Sep 6, −54d = Sep 12. Held (not AUTO-LIVE) for two reasons: (1) the cited justia URL for §17-14-12 returned a CAPTCHA and could not be grounded at the cited URL (the fact is grounded on findlaw instead) — citation-integrity gap; (2) 'September 6' is cycle-specific and recomputes, and two distinct deadlines exist (60-day candidate→local board vs 54-day local board→SOS) — relying on a stale calendar date could risk ballot access, so the durable statutory rule plus a per-cycle reconfirmation is the strictest defensible posture.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. No per-congressional-district or per-county signature quota; the requirement is a single statewide aggregate of 1,000 voters (RI Gen. Laws § 17-14-7(a)). A procedural per-sheet organization rule applies (not a distribution quota): each nomination-paper sheet lists one city/town at the top and may carry only signatures of voters registered in that city/town, because that sheet is verified by that locality's Board of Canvassers.
  - note: Both citations ground VERBATIM: findlaw §17-14-7(a) (aggregate 1,000); SOS page ('Signers on a nomination paper must be from the city or town listed at the top of the nomination paper'). Adversarial check confirmed the city/town rule is an organizational/verification mechanism, not a geographic distribution minimum — there is no minimum-per-locality quota. Characterization is accurate.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: The signature collector (circulator) may be any person 18 years of age or older (410-RICR-20-00-10 §10.4(A)). No circulator residency requirement, no requirement that the circulator be a registered voter, and no restriction on paid circulators. Signers must be RI registered voters eligible to vote for the office and need not be members of the candidate's party.
  - note: Both citations ground VERBATIM against the CURRENT regulation (amendment effective 07/22/2024): reg §10.4(A) ('A collector, who may be any person 18 years of age or older, must personally witness...'); Ballotpedia political-candidates page ('The relevant statutes do not specify any additional circulator requirements (such as residency or pay status)'). Note for downstream use: this same regulation requires the collector to execute a NOTARIZED affidavit (see witnessOrNotary). Current and correct.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Notarized circulator affidavit required. The collector must personally witness each signature and must sign and attest BEFORE A NOTARY PUBLIC that each signer appeared personally and signed in the collector's presence; the collector must also provide their printed name, residence address, and telephone number on the nomination paper (410-RICR-20-00-10 §10.4(A), adopted under RI Gen. Laws § 17-14-10).
  - note: Citation grounds VERBATIM in the current 07/22/2024 regulation, including the (sic) truncated phrase 'in the presence of the.' which appears in the source itself. 'shall sign and attest before a notary public' confirms notarization is mandatory, not optional witnessing. Current and correct.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. In-person, paper-based process: the candidate (or authorized designee for federal/presidential papers) obtains physical nomination papers from the Department of State's Elections Division (148 W. River Street, Providence); signers sign in person with name and residence as on the voting list; the collector witnesses each signature in close physical proximity and executes a notarized affidavit; signed papers are returned to local Boards of Canvassers for manual verification. No online/remote-digital or digitized petition system exists for a presidential petition in RI.
  - note: All three citations ground VERBATIM: SOS page ('Federal offices: You must obtain your nomination papers from the Department of State's Elections Division, 148 W. River Street, Providence, RI.'); reg ('Every voter signing a nomination paper shall sign in person with his or her name, place of residence, and street number, as it appears on the voting list.'); reg definition of 'Presence' ('close physical proximity coupled with awareness sufficient...'). No evidence of any electronic petition pathway. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. Rhode Island has no filing fee for ballot access and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option; qualification is by nomination papers (signatures) only.
  - note: SOS quote grounds VERBATIM ('In order to be on the ballot, you will need to obtain a specified number of valid signatures on your nomination papers. All candidates for federal, state and local public office need nomination papers.'). Adversarial check: searched the SOS Nominations page and both Ballotpedia pages for any filing-fee or fee-in-lieu provision — none found; RI ballot access is signature-only. This is an absence-of-evidence finding but is consistent across all sources, hence AUTO-LIVE.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential candidate in the [next] general election, please confirm the exact date by which signed nomination papers must be returned to the local Board of Canvassers (the 60-days-before-general date) and the separate date by which local boards must file certified papers with the Secretary of State (54 days before), so we can verify both against the official election calendar.

### South Carolina
- **signatures:** 10,000 valid signatures (statewide cap; 5% of registered electors but capped at 10k, which always controls)
- **deadline:** Noon, July 15 of general-election year (next Monday if July 15 is Sat/Sun)
- **risk:** All seven fields grounded against primary sources (verbatim) and corroborated by Ballotpedia; six AUTO-LIVE. Only captureMode held: digitized signatures are permitted but the SEC explicitly warns they may be unverifiable, so rely on paper to avoid any ballot-access risk.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 10,000 valid signatures of active, registered South Carolina voters (statewide cap). Statutory basis: 5% of qualified registered electors of the office's geographic area, capped at 10,000 for any office (S.C. Code 7-11-70). For statewide President, 5% of ~3.39M registered voters (~170k) far exceeds the cap, so 10,000 always controls. Electorate baseline = registrations 120 days before the election.
  - note: Both citations verbatim in sources (7-11-70 statute; scvotes.gov 'valid signatures of 10,000 active, registered'). Independently corroborated by Ballotpedia (5% / max 10,000) and by the SEC page's live registered-voter count of 3,392,645, confirming the cap controls. The cap is a fixed hard number; it could only stop controlling if SC registration fell below 200,000, which is impossible.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Noon (12:00 p.m.) on July 15 of the general-election year, filed with the State Election Commission. If July 15 falls on a Saturday or Sunday, the deadline is noon the following Monday (S.C. Code 7-13-351). For Nov 2024 this was Monday, July 15, 2024.
  - note: 7-13-351 quote verbatim in fetched statute; scvotes.gov presidential-section quote verbatim. Ballotpedia corroborates July 15. Draft correctly tracks the statute's 'Saturday or Sunday' rule (the SEC general petition section drops 'Saturday', but the statute and the presidential-specific section both include it). July 15, 2024 was indeed a Monday. Note: a Governor-declared emergency grants +5 days (7-13-351), an omitted contingency, not a defect in the standard deadline.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. No geographic distribution requirement. For statewide President the petition is a single statewide aggregate with no per-county or per-district minimum. Administrative formatting only: no single petition page may contain signatures of voters from different counties (S.C. Code 7-11-80(4)) — a per-page sorting rule, not a distribution quota.
  - note: 7-11-80(4) and scvotes.gov 5% quotes both verbatim. Statute imposes no geographic spread requirement; the one-county-per-page rule is correctly characterized as formatting, not a quota.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None specified. S.C. petition statutes (7-11-70, 7-11-80, 7-11-85) impose no circulator/collector requirements (no oath, age, residency, or voter-status). The petition form collects only signer information; there is no circulator role. Validity rests on matching each signer against county registration records.
  - note: 7-11-80(3) quote verbatim. Confirmed no circulator role exists anywhere in 7-11-70/80/85. 'None specified' is the correct, accurate statement of SC law.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. No circulator affidavit, witness, or notarization requirement for the petition pages. The 7-11-80 form has only the statement of purpose and voter-signature columns. Validity is determined by county boards matching signatures against original registration applications (S.C. Code 7-11-85). (Separately the candidate self-certifies qualifications and files a Statement of Economic Interests, but the petition pages need no notary/witness.)
  - note: 7-11-85 verification quote verbatim. No notary/witness/affidavit block exists on the petition form per 7-11-80. Accurate.
**🟡 captureMode** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: paper (original pen-and-ink petition pages on 8.5 x 14 bond paper, filed with the State Election Commission). Photocopies are NOT accepted. The SEC permits 'digitized signatures' (human-readable, drawn on touchscreen/stylus, with an accompanying Certificate of Completion) as an OPTIONAL add-on, but expressly warns the petitioner 'assumes the risk that such differences may render the signature unverifiable,' and there is no dedicated e-petition portal. Cryptographic 'digital signatures' are NOT accepted. To never risk ballot access, treat capture as paper-primary and do not rely on digitized signatures for the bulk of the 10,000.
  - note: All three digitized/digital quotes verbatim on scvotes.gov, so the field is fully grounded. Held because the draft's 'hybrid' label is an operational interpretation that retrieval cannot settle: the SEC explicitly disclaims reliability of digitized signatures and provides no e-petition system, so leaning on the digital path could jeopardize the ballot line. Strictest defensible mode = paper; digitized signatures are permitted-but-risky, not a true digital capture channel.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: None. No filing fee for petition candidates and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for an independent presidential petition. Filing fees apply only to candidates seeking a party nomination by primary. (A local jurisdiction could require a fee in addition to a petition, but that does not apply to a statewide presidential petition filed with the SEC.)
  - note: Both scvotes.gov quotes verbatim ('candidates filing by petition do not pay a filing fee'; the local-jurisdiction caveat). No fee-in-lieu path exists for the petition route; accurate.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an independent presidential petition (10,000 signatures), will the State Election Commission accept digitized (touchscreen/stylus + DocuSign Certificate of Completion) signatures on the same footing as pen-and-ink for the full 10,000, and are there any volume, format, or assembly conditions that affect how digitized signatures are counted toward the 10,000-signature requirement?

### South Dakota
- **signatures:** 3,502 valid sigs (1% of combined 2022 gov vote, 350,166) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** First Tue in Aug, 5:00 PM CT (Aug 6, 2024) — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** 6 of 7 fields AUTO-LIVE on grounded primary statute + SOS sources; only circulatorEligibility is CONSERVATIVE-HOLD because SD's resident-circulator rule is constitutionally contested and 12-1-4 was amended (SL 2025, partly eff. 1/1/2026) so the 2024-cycle residency text is uncertain — strictest path (SD-resident, 18+ circulators) does not risk ballot access.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 3,502 valid signatures for the 2024 cycle (1% of the 350,166 total combined vote cast for Governor at the 2022 election). Recomputes each cycle off the most recent certified gubernatorial total. SDCL 12-7-7.
  - note: Both citations grounded verbatim: SDCL 12-7-7 ('not less than one percent of the total combined vote cast for Governor at the last certified gubernatorial election') and the SOS 2024 page ('Independent: 3,502 signatures (1% of the total vote for governor in 2022 - 350,166)'). Re-derived: 1% of 350,166 = 3,501.66 -> 3,502. Ballotpedia's dedicated presidential page independently confirms the same combined-gubernatorial-vote basis (distinct from the per-party 1% basis used for partisan candidates). Operative SOS figure is correct and current.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Certificate of nomination with nominating petitions, declaration of candidacy, and VP certification must be filed with the Secretary of State by the first Tuesday in August at 5:00 p.m. central time before the election (August 6, 2024 for the 2024 general). Mailing by registered mail by the deadline is timely. Petitions may not be circulated before January 1 of the election year. SDCL 12-7-7; 12-6-4.1.
  - note: SDCL 12-7-7 grounded verbatim ('after December thirty-first and by the first Tuesday in August at 5:00 p.m. central time before the election ... If the certificate of nomination is mailed by registered mail ... it is timely submitted'). SDCL 12-6-4.1 grounded verbatim at its section URL ('No petition or certificate of nomination ... may be circulated prior to the first day of January'). First Tuesday in August 2024 = Aug 6, 2024 (Aug 1, 2024 was a Thursday). Confirmed by Ballotpedia ('filed by 5:00 p.m. on the first Tuesday in August'). Note: the draft cites the chapter URL /Statute/12-6 for the 12-6-4.1 quote; the text lives at section 12-6-4.1, which I fetched and confirmed verbatim.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. Single statewide total (1% of the statewide combined gubernatorial vote); no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement for a statewide independent presidential candidate. Filed with the Secretary of State because the office is voted on in more than one county.
  - note: SDCL 12-7-7 grounded verbatim; the statute imposes only a single statewide 1%-of-combined-gubernatorial-vote total with no geographic distribution. Reviewed full chapter 12-6 (incl. 12-6-7) and found per-county/per-district splits only for legislative/county offices and vote-center counties, not for statewide/presidential petitions. No distribution requirement applies.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICTEST: Use only circulators who are South Dakota residents (actual fixed permanent dwelling, lives/usually sleeps there for the requisite consecutive days per SDCL 12-1-4) and at least 18 years old (SDCL 12-1-3(12)). Signers must be registered voters entitled to vote for the office; a party-affiliated voter may sign an independent's petition only if they have not previously signed another petition for that office (SDCL 12-6-8). Do NOT rely on non-resident circulators.
  - note: All quoted text grounded verbatim: SDCL 12-1-3(12) ('a resident of the State of South Dakota as defined under 12-1-4, who is at least eighteen years of age'), 12-1-4 residency definition, and 12-6-8 signer-eligibility/cross-party provision. HOLD for two reasons: (1) SD's resident-circulator requirement has a known constitutional vulnerability (federal courts have enjoined SD resident-circulator requirements in the ballot-measure context), so whether a non-resident circulator's signatures can lawfully be rejected is a legal-interpretation question retrieval cannot settle; (2) SDCL 12-1-4 was amended by SL 2025 ch 57 and ch 58 (the latter eff. Jan 1, 2026), so the current 'thirty consecutive days' text may not be the exact version in force for the 2024 cycle the draft labels it for. The over-comply path (SD-resident, 18+ circulators) never risks ballot access, so it is the relied value; sent an SOS inquiry to confirm enforcement and the applicable residency standard.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: Circulator certification under oath (verification by the circulator on each self-contained sheet), not a per-signer notarized affidavit. The circulator's verification may NOT be notarized by the candidate the petition nominates. Falsely attesting is a Class 6 felony. SDCL 12-6-8; 12-1-3(11).
  - note: Grounded verbatim at SDCL 12-6-8 ('The petition must be verified under oath by the persons circulating the petition. The verification ... may not be notarized by the candidate whom the petition is nominating. Any person ... who falsely attests to the verification is guilty of a Class 6 felony') and SDCL 12-1-3(11) (form contains 'the verification of the circulator'; multi-sheet petitions each separately verified). Correct and current. (Draft cites chapter URL /Statute/12-6; the operative text is at section 12-6-8, fetched and confirmed verbatim.)
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Physical paper nominating petitions, wet-ink signatures by registered voters, verified under oath by a resident circulator on each self-contained sheet. No remote/online or in-person-digitized e-signature system exists for SD candidate petitions. SDCL 12-1-3(11); 12-6-8.
  - note: Grounded verbatim: SDCL 12-6-8 ('The circulator or the individual who signs the petition shall add the address at which the individual is currently registered to vote, the county ..., and the date of signing'; 'A nominating petition for any election shall be a self-contained sheet of paper') and 12-1-3(11) (each sheet self-contained and separately verified). The self-contained-paper-sheet + handwritten signer info + circulator oath structure confirms paper-only; no statutory e-signature petition portal for SD candidate petitions. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: None. No filing fee in lieu of or in addition to the signature requirement for an independent presidential candidate. Ballot access is obtained solely by filing the certificate of nomination with the required petition signatures. SDCL 12-7-7; chapter 12-6.
  - note: SDCL 12-7-7 grounded verbatim; it conditions nomination only on filing the certificate with the required petition signatures and prescribes no fee alternative. Reviewed full chapter 12-6 and found no filing-fee-in-lieu provision for nominating petitions. Absence-of-fee-alternative independently confirmed; no contrary provision located.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For the 2024 general election cycle, did South Dakota enforce the SDCL 12-1-3(12)/12-1-4 requirement that a nominating-petition circulator be a South Dakota resident (and what residency definition, e.g. the 30-consecutive-day standard, applied), given federal litigation over resident-circulator requirements? Please confirm whether a non-resident circulator's signatures would be rejected for an independent presidential petition.

### Tennessee
- **signatures:** 275 signatures (25 × 11 electors), statewide, no distribution — VERIFIED
- **deadline:** Noon CT, 3rd Thursday in August (Aug 15, 2024) — physical receipt, no postmark — VERIFIED
- **risk:** Core ballot-access facts (275 sigs, Aug deadline, paper, no fee) are grounded and independently corroborated; two negative-fact fields (circulator eligibility, no notary) rest on statutory silence — circulator field has zero citations (BLOCKED) and notary held conservative; confirm both with TN SOS before relying on unrestricted circulators or unwitnessed pages.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 275 signatures (25 registered voters per elector × 11 electors). Signers must be registered voters anywhere in Tennessee; no per-county or per-district distribution. Candidate must also sign. Recomputes after each census-driven reapportionment of TN's electoral votes.
  - note: Both citations verbatim: FindLaw TCA 2-5-101(b)(1) ('twenty-five (25) or more registered voters for each elector allocated to the state'; 'must designate the full number of electors') and SOS guide ('at least two hundred seventy-five (275) voters registered anywhere within the State'). Independently corroborated by Ballotpedia (lines 98, 229: '25 voters per state elector (275 total)') and that TN was allocated 11 electoral votes in 2012/2016/2020/2024. Math 25×11=275 is current through 2030 census cycle. Per-elector formula recompute claim is correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 12:00 noon Central time on the third Thursday in August of the election year (Aug 15, 2024 for that cycle). Original petition plus one certified duplicate must be physically received by the deadline; a postmark does not suffice. If the deadline falls on a Saturday, Sunday, or state holiday it moves to noon on the previous business day (TCA 2-5-101(g)(2)). Recomputes each cycle.
  - note: SOS quotes verbatim ('third Thursday in August'; 'A postmark will not suffice'). TCA 2-5-101(g)(2) text confirmed verbatim on FindLaw: deadline on Sat/Sun/state holiday moves to noon previous business day. Ballot Access News (2024-08-13) and Ballotpedia independently confirm Aug 15, 2024 and the third-Thursday rule (changed from third Tuesday in 2021). Third-Thursday-in-August derives from the general (a)(1) rule (third Thursday of third calendar month before a November election) and is stated explicitly in the SOS guide.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: No distribution requirement on petition signatures — the 275 signers may be registered voters anywhere in Tennessee. A separate distribution rule applies only to the elector slate: 11 electors total, 1 resident from each of the 9 congressional districts plus 2 at-large electors who may reside anywhere in the state.
  - note: Both SOS quotes verbatim ('voters registered anywhere within the State'; '1 elector from each of Tennessee's 9 congressional districts, and 2 additional electors who may be residents of any part of the state'). The signer-vs-elector distinction is explicit in the guide, not an inference. Ballotpedia corroborates 9 congressional districts and 11 electors. Structural fact, not a contested legal interpretation.
**🔴 circulatorEligibility** — BLOCKED · 0.90
  - uses: none
  - note: Field has ZERO citations, so it cannot be grounded per gate rules. The assertion (statute/guide silent on circulator qualifications) is consistent with the full TCA 2-5-101 text I read and with the SOS guide — no circulator provision appears — but a negative claim with no supporting citation is unverifiable as drafted. Strictest posture: do NOT assume circulators are unrestricted; confirm with TN SOS before using non-resident or paid circulators. SOS inquiry added.
**🟡 witnessOrNotary** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: As read, TCA 2-5-101 and the SOS guide impose no per-sheet witness/notary/circulator-affidavit requirement; the only signer-verification rule is that each signer include the residence address shown on the signer's voter registration card (TCA 2-5-101(b)(2)). TREAT AS UNCONFIRMED until the TN SOS confirms no notarization/oath is required, since this rests on statutory silence.
  - note: Cited quote is verbatim from TCA 2-5-101(b)(2) ('must include the address of the signer's residence as shown on the signer's voter registration card in order for that person's signature to be counted'). I confirmed the full statute text contains no witness/notary/affidavit provision. BUT the cited quote only establishes the signer-address rule; the 'no notary required' conclusion is an inference from statutory silence that retrieval cannot fully settle — hence held conservatively. SOS inquiry added.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. Physical paper petition only: candidate picks up the petition from the Division of Elections (in person or by mail) and files the wet-ink original plus one certified duplicate by the deadline; a postmark does not suffice and faxed/emailed documents are not accepted. No remote-online or in-person-digitized e-signature system exists for this petition.
  - note: Both SOS quotes verbatim (90-day pick-up window, in person or mailed; 'A postmark will not suffice'; certified-duplicate photocopy definition). Physical-receipt requirement plus the write-in section's 'No faxed or emailed documents will be accepted' support paper-only. No e-signature pathway found in any source. Current factual matter.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. No filing fee for an independent presidential nominating petition, and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option. The petition signatures are the sole path to the general-election ballot.
  - note: SOS quote 'There are no filing fees.' is verbatim; filing-location quote (note the source's own 'with with' typo) is verbatim. No fee-in-lieu provision appears in TCA 2-5-101 or the SOS guide. The 'no fee-in-lieu' claim is supported by the affirmative 'no filing fees' statement plus absence of any alternative path; uncontested.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Does Tennessee impose any age, residency, or voter-registration requirement on a person who circulates or collects signatures for an independent presidential nominating petition under TCA 2-5-101, or may a non-resident/paid circulator collect signatures?
  - Does an independent presidential nominating petition under TCA 2-5-101 require any circulator affidavit, oath, witness, or notarization on each petition sheet, or is the signer's residence address the only verification requirement?

### Texas
- **signatures:** TX independent pres: 113,151 valid sigs for 2024 (1% of prior presidential total); non-primary voters only — number confirmed, but verify cycle recompute
- **deadline:** TX deadline: 2nd Monday in May = May 13, 2024; circulate only after March 5 primary — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** Grounding clean on all 8 fields (every quote verbatim; 113,151 = round-up of 1% of 11,315,056 2020 TX total). Two holds: signatures (mixes the minor-party gubernatorial base into the independent rule) and circulatorEligibility (self-flagged UNKNOWN, an unprovable absence claim). Default strict pending SOS confirmation.

**🟡 signaturesRequired** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.90
  - uses: For the independent presidential path only: at least 1% of the total vote received in Texas by all candidates for president in the most recent presidential general election. For the 2024 cycle this equaled 113,151 valid signatures of registered voters who did NOT vote in either party's presidential primary that year (recomputes each cycle off the prior presidential vote; 1% of the 2020 total of 11,315,056 rounds up to 113,151). No geographic/territory requirement on signers. (Strict scope: the minor/convention-party qualification — 5% statewide nominee threshold or 1% of the most recent gubernatorial vote — is a DIFFERENT path with a DIFFERENT base and does not apply to an independent candidate; do not conflate.)
  - note: All quotes verbatim. 192.032(d)=1%; SOS=113,151; 192.032(e)=no territory; 192.032(f)/(g)=non-primary voters/invalid if signed on or before primary. Math checks: 1% of 11,315,056 (2020 TX total, confirmed via Wikipedia) = 113,150.56 -> 113,151. HOLD because the draft value bundles the convention/minor-party path (gubernatorial-vote base) into the independent rule, which is out-of-scope for accessPath=independent and could mislead; the 'recomputes each cycle' framing is also a derived gloss not stated verbatim in a citation. Independent number itself is correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: The application and accompanying petition must be filed with the Secretary of State no later than the second Monday in May of the presidential election year — May 13, 2024 for the 2024 cycle. The petition may not be circulated until after the March 5, 2024 presidential primary; a signature is invalid if signed on or before the date of the primary or by anyone who voted in a presidential primary that year.
  - note: 192.032(c) 'second Monday in May' verbatim; SOS 'no later than May 13, 2024' and 'circulated beginning after March 5, 2024' verbatim. May 2024 Mondays = 6th, 13th, so 2nd Monday = May 13 (date arithmetic confirmed). 192.032(g) invalidity quote present. Correct and self-executing, no legal interpretation needed.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. There is no per-congressional-district or per-county distribution requirement for the independent presidential petition; the statute expressly provides that a signer's voter registration need not be in any particular territory, so signatures may be gathered statewide with no geographic spread.
  - note: 192.032(e) quote 'A petition signer's voter registration is not required to be in any particular territory.' verbatim. Independently confirmed against NASS (no distribution language for the TX independent presidential petition, unlike states such as Virginia which NASS lists with a 400-per-district requirement). Negative claim but directly supported by the express statutory text.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: UNKNOWN / not established by retrieval. Secs. 141.064-141.065 prescribe the circulator's DUTIES (point out and read each statement, witness each signature, ascertain dates, verify each signer's registration, and execute a notarized affidavit) but do not by themselves establish that there are NO eligibility limits. Do not represent that 'any person' may circulate; treat circulator qualifications as unconfirmed and assume the petition must be circulated by a competent adult able to witness signatures and swear the notarized affidavit, pending SOS confirmation.
  - note: Both cited section headers/quotes are verbatim (141.064 'A person circulating a petition must:'; 141.065(a) affidavit clause). But the field's substantive claim is a NEGATIVE/absence assertion ('no statutory provision restricts circulator eligibility') that two cited duty-sections cannot prove — the value even self-flags UNKNOWN. Cannot ground the non-existence of a restriction from these sources; strictest stance is to hold and ask the SOS rather than assert open eligibility.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Notarized circulator affidavit required. Each part of the petition must include an affidavit of the circulator, executed before a person authorized to administer oaths (notarized), stating the circulator pointed out and read each required statement to each signer, witnessed each signature, verified each signer's registration status, and believes each signature genuine. A single notarized affidavit covers all signatures gathered by that circulator if notarization is on or after the date of the last signature obtained.
  - note: 141.065(a) 'executed before a person authorized to administer oaths in this state' and 141.065(c) single-notarized-affidavit quote both verbatim. Directly on point and applies to the independent presidential petition via 192.032(b)(3)(A)->141.062. No interpretation needed.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper (wet-signature). Signers must sign in their own handwriting; the circulator must witness each signature in person and a notarized circulator affidavit is required per part. No online/remote or digitized-signature system exists for an independent presidential petition in Texas — the SOS publishes only PDF forms (Application 2-38f, Petition 2-39f).
  - note: 141.063(b) 'The signature is the only information that is required to appear on the petition in the signer's own handwriting.' verbatim; 141.064(1) read-each-statement quote verbatim; SOS 'Independent Candidate's Petition for President (PDF)' verbatim. Wet-ink/witnessed paper process follows directly from witnessing + per-part notarized affidavit. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.85
  - uses: None. Ballot access for an independent presidential candidate is by petition only — there is no filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option for this office. Sec. 192.032 requires the application to be accompanied by a qualifying petition and the consent statements, and lists no filing-fee alternative. (The fee-or-petition election available to Texas primary/partisan candidates does not apply to this independent presidential path.)
  - note: 192.032(b)(3) 'be accompanied by:' quote verbatim — the statutory list of what accompanies the application is exhaustive and contains only the petition and written consents, no fee or fee-in-lieu. SOS independent section (quote verbatim) describes application+petition with no fee. The absence is supported by an exhaustive statutory enumeration rather than mere silence, so 'no fee alternative' is reliable without legal interpretation.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an INDEPENDENT presidential candidate's petition under Tex. Elec. Code 192.032, are there any statutory or administrative qualifications on who may circulate the petition (e.g., must the circulator be a registered Texas voter, of a minimum age, or a U.S. resident), or may any person circulate it?
  - Does the independent presidential candidate's signature requirement of 1% of the most recent presidential vote recompute each presidential cycle off the prior presidential general election total (i.e., for 2028 it will be 1% of the 2024 Texas presidential vote), and is the 113,151 figure specific to the 2024 cycle only?

### Utah
- **signatures:** 1,000 valid registered-voter signatures statewide (flat statutory number) + $500 fee
- **deadline:** DISPUTED: signatures due June 15 (20A-9-502(5)(a)); Aug 15 only for running-mate/VP filing — treat June 15 as binding for signatures
- **risk:** Only real exposure is the deadline: statute sets June 15 for signature submission while 504 sets Aug 15 for the running-mate/VP step; collect and submit signatures by June 15 to never risk the ballot line. Circulator non-residency relied on a 2015 snapshot; current statute dropped the residency clause but confirm before staffing non-resident circulators.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: 1,000 signatures of registered voters statewide — a flat statutory number set by Utah Code 20A-9-502(5)(a)(ii)(A) for an office filled by the voters of the entire state (President); not a percentage and does not recompute by cycle. Each must be a VALID signature certified by the county clerks.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim. FindLaw 20A-9-502(5)(a)(ii)(A) (current as of Jan 1, 2025) sets 'at least 1,000 registered voters residing within the state' for statewide offices; Ballotpedia independently confirms 1,000 for an independent presidential candidate. President is an office filled by Utah voters statewide. Note clerks count/certify only valid holographic signatures of registered voters (502(5)(b)-(c)), so collect a cushion above 1,000.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: STRICTEST READING: submit the 1,000 signatures to the county clerks AND file the certificate of nomination + $500 fee with the Lieutenant Governor no later than 5 p.m. on JUNE 15 of the general election year. The August 15 date in 20A-9-504(2) on its face governs only (a) selection of the unaffiliated running mate and (b) the VP candidate's compliance with 20A-9-202(7) — NOT the signature/petition submission. Operate to the earlier June 15 date to avoid any risk to ballot access; confirm with the Lt. Governor's office before relying on August 15 for signatures.
  - note: DISAGREE with the draft's headline that Aug 15 is the presidential SIGNATURE/petition deadline. Primary text conflicts: 20A-9-502(5)(a) sets the signature-submission deadline at 'no later than 5 p.m. on June 15,' and 20A-9-503(1) ties certificate filing + fee to that same 502(5)(a) deadline (June 15). 20A-9-504(2)(a) only requires the presidential candidate to 'select a running mate' by Aug 15, and 504(2)(b) requires the VP to satisfy 20A-9-202(7) by Aug 15 — neither sets the signature deadline. Ballotpedia (secondary) says petition filed 'no later than August 15,' contradicting the plain June 15 statutory text. The draft itself flags the June 15 vs Aug 15 tension and that the Lt. Gov used discretion amid 2024 litigation. Correctness hinges on a legal interpretation retrieval cannot settle; strictest defensible posture is the earlier June 15 for signatures. Aug 15 grounds verbatim but the VALUE's interpretation (Aug 15 = signature deadline) is not supported by the statute it cites.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. No geographic distribution requirement — a single flat statewide total of 1,000 valid registered-voter signatures, with no minimum per congressional district or county. Packets are submitted to the county clerk where the majority of that packet's signatures were collected, but that is an administrative routing rule, not a distribution quota; the 1,000 total is statewide.
  - note: Quote grounds verbatim in current 20A-9-502(5)(a)(ii). The statute imposes only a single statewide 1,000 threshold for a statewide office; the per-political-division minimums in (5)(a)(ii)(B) apply only to sub-state offices, not President. The 'county clerk where the majority of signatures were collected' language is a submission-routing rule, correctly characterized as not a distribution requirement.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: Circulator (the person who witnesses each signature and signs the verification) must be at least 18 years old; need NOT be a registered voter. Residency: the CURRENT statute (FindLaw, current to Jan 1, 2025) requires only age 18 in 20A-9-502(3)(a)(i) and contains no circulator residency requirement, so a non-resident may circulate. CAUTION: the draft's basis for non-residency is the superseded 2015 ut.elaws.us snapshot (which had a presidential-specific residency waiver against a now-removed general residency rule). Confirm current residency rules with the Lt. Governor before staffing non-resident circulators; using Utah-resident circulators is the zero-risk posture. Signers must be registered to vote in Utah (or intend to register before certification) and may sign for only one candidate for the office.
  - note: Age-18 and not-required-to-be-a-registered-voter sub-claims ground in current 20A-9-502(3)(a) and are correct. The non-residency conclusion is also TRUE under current law, but the CITED basis is stale: the ut.elaws.us quote ('A person who is not a resident may sign the verification...for president') is from a January 2015 snapshot whose structure (general residency requirement under 20A-2-105 + presidential carve-out in 502(3)(b)) no longer matches the current statute, which dropped the residency clause entirely (now no residency requirement for any office). So the draft reaches a right answer via outdated authority and a presidential-specific rationale that no longer exists. Because the current contours rest on confirming that no residency requirement survives, treat as CONSERVATIVE-HOLD; strictest safe posture is to not depend on non-resident circulators without office confirmation.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Both required: (1) the candidate's certificate of nomination is a sworn statement that must be NOTARIZED ('Subscribed and sworn to before me... Notary Public (or other officer qualified to administer oaths)'); and (2) each signature packet must include a circulator VERIFICATION attesting that each signer signed in the circulator's presence — signed by the circulator (with residence address and date) but not separately notarized. False verification is a class A misdemeanor.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim in current 20A-9-502: 502(1)(a) ends with the notary jurat (notarized candidate certificate), and 502(1)(c) sets out the circulator 'Verification' signed by the circulator. 502(4) makes false signing/verification a class A misdemeanor. The notarized-affidavit-plus-non-notarized-circulator-verification structure is correctly stated for the current statute.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: paper / wet-ink. The statute mandates handwritten 'holographic' signatures on printed 8-1/2 x 11 signature sheets, each signed in the circulator's physical presence; the county clerk counts/certifies only persons who signed 'with a holographic signature' (20A-9-502(1)(b)(viii)(C), (5)(c)). Treat digital/online capture as NOT available for the unaffiliated presidential certificate-of-nomination petition.
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim in current 20A-9-502 (the 'Holographic Signature of Registered Voter' column heading and the clerk counting 'only those persons who signed with a holographic signature'). The holographic mandate makes wet-ink/paper the legally safe answer, and the draft's conclusion is already the strictest posture. Caveat retained: the draft could not confirm from a primary source that any Utah state-approved signature app covers this specific path, so reliance on digital capture is unverified and should be avoided — which the relied value reflects.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: A $500 filing fee is required IN ADDITION TO the 1,000-signature petition — it is NOT an alternative that can substitute for collecting signatures. An individual filing a certificate of nomination for President pays the $500 fee at filing alongside the petition (20A-9-503(4)(a)); filing and fee are due with the certificate per 20A-9-503(1).
  - note: Both quotes ground verbatim. 20A-9-503(4)(a) requires a $500 filing fee for a presidential certificate of nomination; nothing in 502/503 lets the fee substitute for the 1,000 signatures (503(1) requires the candidate to file the certificate, file the declaration, AND pay the fee, on top of the 502 signature requirement). The fee is additive, not a fee-in-lieu alternative — correctly stated. Ballotpedia independently confirms both the $500 fee and the 1,000 signatures.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an unaffiliated/independent candidate for President of the United States, what is the firm deadline to SUBMIT the 1,000 signatures / certificate-of-nomination petition to the county clerks and to FILE the certificate with the Lieutenant Governor — is it the June 15 deadline in Utah Code 20A-9-502(5)(a)/20A-9-503(1), or the August 15 date in 20A-9-504(2), which on its face governs only selection of a running mate and the VP's 20A-9-202(7) filing?
  - Under the current (post-2024) version of Utah Code 20A-9-502, is there any residency requirement for the person who circulates and signs the verification on an unaffiliated U.S. President certificate-of-nomination petition, or may a non-resident circulate and verify?

### Vermont
- **signatures:** VT: 1,000 valid signatures, flat statewide, no distribution — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** VT deadline CONFLICT: statute/SoS say Aug 1; NASS says June — HOLD to earlier June deadline for planning
- **risk:** Signature count and capture mode are firm; the only material ballot-access risk is the deadline (two authoritative sources conflict — plan to the earlier June date) and unverified-by-omission claims (circulator eligibility) that should be confirmed with the VT SoS before relying on them.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 1,000 valid signatures (flat statewide number, not a percentage), per 17 V.S.A. 2402(b)(1)(A). Only signatures certified by a town clerk as belonging to registered voters count toward the 1,000.
  - note: GROUNDED: 2402(b)(1)(A) '...for presidential and vice presidential offices, 1,000' verified verbatim on FindLaw; SoS 2024 form 'For President - 1,000' verified verbatim in extracted PDF text. Independently re-derived: flat statutory number, no percentage, does not recompute per cycle. Town-clerk-certification-only counting confirmed by 2402(a)(4)(B)(ii). Correct and current.
**🟡 deadline** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: PLAN to the EARLIER of the two conflicting authorities: file no later than the second Thursday after the first Monday in June of the election year (the NASS-stated date), even though the controlling presidential-specific statute 17 V.S.A. 2402(d)(1)(A) and the VT SoS form both state 5:00 p.m. on August 1. Filing window opens the fourth Monday in April. All signatures must be town-clerk-certified BEFORE filing, so begin certification weeks earlier. Treat August 1 as the statutory backstop but do not rely on it without SoS confirmation given the documented NASS conflict.
  - note: GROUNDED: statute quote (2402(d)(1)(A) 'not earlier than the fourth Monday in April and not later than 5:00 p.m. on the August 1...') verified verbatim on FindLaw; SoS form 'between Monday, April 22 and 5:00 p.m. on Thursday, August 1, 2024' verified verbatim; NASS quote (June deadline) verified verbatim in NASS PDF. ADVERSARIAL: the draft correctly diagnoses that NASS conflated the independent-presidential path with the 2356/2381 minor-party/general-independent June path (NASS's own citation list is 2103,2319,2356,2381,2382,2385 — it does NOT cite 2402). Ballotpedia INDEPENDENTLY corroborates 'fourth Monday in April...no later than August 1.' So August 1 is almost certainly correct. BUT: a national SoS-association source conflicts on a deadline, no human counsel is available, and missing the true deadline forfeits ballot access while filing early costs nothing — strictest defensible posture is to plan to the earlier June date and confirm with the SoS. Note 2103(13): if the deadline falls on a weekend/holiday it extends to the next business day (Aug 1 2024 was a Thursday, so no shift that cycle); the deadline is date-defined, not a fixed weekday, so re-check the actual calendar date each cycle.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: None. Vermont requires a flat statewide total of 1,000 signatures for President/VP with no geographic distribution requirement (no per-district or per-county minimums). Signatures may be collected anywhere in the state and need not all be on one paper (17 V.S.A. 2402(b)(2)); the only locality dimension is administrative town-clerk certification.
  - note: GROUNDED: '(2) Signatures need not all be contained on one paper' and the flat 1,000 figure both verified verbatim on FindLaw. ADVERSARIAL: re-read all of 2402 — no subsection imposes any geographic/county/district distribution; the per-town element is purely the clerk-certification mechanism, not a distribution minimum. Correct.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: Strictest posture: use only circulators who are themselves Vermont-resident REGISTERED VOTERS until the SoS confirms no circulator restriction. The grounded SIGNER rule is firm: each signer must, at the time of signing, be registered and qualified to vote for the candidate and must indicate their town of residence next to the signature (17 V.S.A. 2354(b)); any number of voters may sign and there is no limit on petitions a voter may sign (2354(a), SoS form). The draft's claim of 'no circulator-eligibility requirement' is an inference from statutory silence, not an affirmative grant, so do not rely on out-of-state or unregistered circulators without confirmation.
  - note: GROUNDED: 2354(b)(1)-(2) signer/town-of-residence quote verified verbatim on FindLaw; SoS form 'no restrictions on the number of petitions a voter may sign. 17 V.S.A. 2354' verified verbatim. ADVERSARIAL: the SIGNER requirements are explicit and correct. The 'no circulator requirement' conclusion rests on ABSENCE of statutory text — retrieval cannot prove a negative, and a restriction could live elsewhere in Title 17 ch. 49 or in SoS administrative guidance. Because mis-assuming out-of-state circulators are permissible could taint signatures and risk ballot access, hold to the strict interpretation and confirm with SoS.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: No notarized affidavit and no circulator oath. The operative requirement is TOWN-CLERK certification: before filing, the town clerk of each town where signers appear to be voters must certify on the statement of nomination that the named signers are registered voters in that town and the total number of valid signers; only so-certified signatures count (17 V.S.A. 2402(a)(4)(B)(i)-(ii)). The candidate's statement also attests each signer is qualified and the residence shown is correct (2402(c)). Comply by routing every petition page through the relevant town clerk for certification BEFORE filing.
  - note: GROUNDED: 2402(a)(4)(B)(i)-(ii) town-clerk-certification quote verified verbatim on FindLaw; SoS form certification-before-filing language verified verbatim. ADVERSARIAL: the AFFIRMATIVE compliance mechanism (town-clerk pre-certification) is explicit and is itself the strict/verification-heavy posture, so the actionable requirement is firm. The 'no notary' element is an absence inference, but nothing in 2402, 2354, or the SoS form suggests an additional notary/oath; the compliance action (get town-clerk certification) is unchanged regardless. Treated as AUTO-LIVE on the affirmative requirement.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. The statement of nomination is a paper form circulated for wet-ink signatures, taken to each town clerk for certification against the voter checklist, then physically filed with the Secretary of State in Montpelier ('filed' = 'deposited in the regularly maintained office of the official', 17 V.S.A. 2103(13); a document is not filed until received at the office). No remote/online digital signature-collection system exists for an independent presidential petition; forms are print-sign-file PDFs.
  - note: GROUNDED: SoS form certify-before-file and 'deposited in the regularly maintained office...' (2103(13)) quotes verified verbatim; 2103(13) full text independently confirmed on FindLaw (also adds the not-filed-until-received and weekend-extension rules). ADVERSARIAL: the 'no online system' element is an absence inference, but the strict/safe posture is identical to the stated value (assume paper, wet-ink, physical filing). Aligned with strict interpretation; AUTO-LIVE.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None. No filing fee for an independent presidential candidate and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures option — the 1,000-signature petition (plus consent forms and three electors) is the sole ballot-access path. The $2,000 fee applies only to MAJOR-PARTY candidates seeking the presidential PRIMARY ballot, not to independent general-election candidates.
  - note: GROUNDED: Ballotpedia quote ('...A primary candidate must also pay a $2,000 filing fee. An independent candidate...must file a petition containing the signatures of 1,000 registered voters.') verified verbatim; SoS form '1,000' requirement verified verbatim and contains no fee reference. ADVERSARIAL: 2402 imposes no fee on independents; the strict compliance action is to collect 1,000 certified signatures, which holds whether or not a fee theoretically existed, so no ballot-access risk arises from the 'no fee' conclusion. Correct; AUTO-LIVE.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - For an INDEPENDENT presidential/VP candidate filing under 17 V.S.A. 2402(d)(1)(A), is the 2028 filing deadline 5:00 p.m. on August 1 (per 2402 and your 2024 candidate form), and NOT the 'second Thursday after the first Monday in June' deadline that the NASS July-2024 summary lists for Vermont? Please confirm the controlling deadline and statute.
  - Does Vermont impose ANY eligibility requirement (age, in-state residency, voter registration) on the PERSON who circulates an independent presidential nomination petition, or may a non-resident / non-registered person circulate so long as every SIGNER is a registered Vermont voter? Is there any circulator affidavit, oath, or registration step?
  - Is there any approved electronic or remote method to collect or submit signatures for an independent presidential nomination petition, or must all signatures be wet-ink on paper, certified by each town clerk, and physically filed at the SoS office before the deadline?

### Virginia
- **signatures:** VA: 5,000 sigs total, ≥200 per congressional district (11 districts) — AUTO-LIVE
- **deadline:** VA: noon of 74th day before election (2024 cycle = Aug 23, 2024) — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** 7 of 9 fields AUTO-LIVE on grounded primary statute (Va. Code 24.2-543). Two HOLDs: captureMode (operative value "paper" confirmed, but draft's form ID ELECT-543(P) is WRONG — current 2024 indep/3rd-party petition is ELECT-242(P); HB89 source CAPTCHA-blocked) and feeAlternative (negative/absence claim not provable from a single quote). No field BLOCKED; all relied values are ballot-access-safe.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 5,000 signatures of Virginia qualified voters total, with at least 200 from each of Virginia's 11 congressional districts. The 5,000 total is the binding figure (11 x 200 = 2,200 < 5,000). Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Statute quote verbatim at vacode.org/24.2-543.txt: 'signed by at least 5,000 qualified voters and include signatures of at least 200 qualified voters from each congressional district.' Ballotpedia quote verbatim. Independently confirmed VA has 11 congressional districts (in effect since 2022 elections; 118th/119th Congress). Binding-total reasoning correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Noon of the 74th day before the presidential election (statutory, recomputes each cycle). For the Nov 5, 2024 general election that date was August 23, 2024. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Statute quote verbatim: 'filed with the State Board by noon of the seventy-fourth day before the presidential election.' Independently computed: 74 days before 2024-11-05 = 2024-08-23 (Friday) — matches draft. Forward-looking operative rule is the 74th-day formula, not the fixed 2024 date.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Yes — distribution requirement: at least 200 qualified-voter signatures from each of Virginia's 11 congressional districts (within the 5,000 total). Elector slate must also include one elector residing in each congressional district plus two at-large. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Both quotes verbatim at vacode.org/24.2-543.txt ('include signatures of at least 200 qualified voters from each congressional district' and 'including one elector residing in each congressional district and two from the Commonwealth at large'). Correct.
**🟢 circulatorEligibility** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: Each signature must be witnessed by either (a) a constitutionally qualified candidate for President (who may witness his own petition), or (b) a Virginia resident who is not a minor and not a felon whose voting rights have not been restored. The witness need not be a registered voter. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Statute quote verbatim. The 'need not be a registered voter' gloss is well-supported by plain text (statute requires only residency + non-minor + non-disqualified-felon, not registration). Minor reading, but settled by the text itself.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.94
  - uses: Two layers: (1) per-page circulator/witness affidavit (VA residency, not a minor, not a disqualified felon) on EACH petition page; (2) a subscribed and notarized oath by each selected elector, filed with the petition. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Both quotes verbatim ('whose affidavit to that effect appears on each page of the petition' and 'a subscribed and notarized oath by each elector'). Corroborated by the official VA elector oath form ELECT-242(C) for independent/third-party electors.
**🟡 captureMode** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: paper. The independent/third-party Petition of Qualified Voters for Electors for President and Vice President is collected on the Department of Elections' prescribed paper form with original wet signatures and per-page witness affidavits; no online/remote filing path was available for the 2024 cycle. NOTE: the operative form number is ELECT-242(P), NOT 'ELECT-543(P)' as the draft stated. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A) + VA Dept. of Elections candidate forms page.
  - note: HOLD for a factual defect, not a legal interpretation. Core value 'paper' is independently grounded by the statute (wet signatures + per-page affidavits) AND the official VA forms page (which lists only paper letter/legal petition forms for the 2024 indep/3rd-party general path). BUT (1) the draft's form ID 'ELECT-543(P)' is WRONG — the current 2024 form is ELECT-242(P); ELECT-543(P) survives only in stale 2020 Korean-language filenames; (2) the HB89/TrackBill citation is CAPTCHA-blocked and could not be grounded, so the prospective-online-system claim is unverified. Relying on 'paper' is the strictest/safest posture for ballot access.
**🟡 feeAlternative** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.78
  - uses: None (treat as petition-only). Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543 contains no filing fee and no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative for the independent/non-party presidential elector petition; verify with the state before relying on any fee path. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: HOLD because this is a negative/absence claim. The grounded statute quote shows the petition path but does not affirmatively state 'no fee'; proving the absence of any fee-in-lieu alternative anywhere in Title 24.2 from a single quote is an inference retrieval did not fully settle. The value is very likely correct (VA presidential ballot access is petition-only), so the strictest defensible posture (assume no fee escape, plan for full petition) is also the safe one. SOS inquiry added.
**🟢 minorPartyPathNote** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: The new/minor-party (party-name) path uses the SAME statute (Sec. 24.2-543) and SAME numeric requirements (5,000 signatures, 200 per congressional district, noon of the 74th day, same witness/notary rules). The only material difference is the ballot LABEL: to appear under a chosen party name the group must additionally have had, for at least six months before filing, a state central committee of registered voters from each congressional district, a party plan and bylaws, and a designated chairman and secretary; otherwise the candidate and electors are designated 'Independent'. Basis: Va. Code Sec. 24.2-543(A).
  - note: Both quotes verbatim at vacode.org/24.2-543.txt (six-month organizational requirement for party name; 'Independent' designation fallback). The same-statute/same-numeric-requirements claim is directly correct — there is no separate numeric scheme for the party-name path.
