  - For an independent/third-party presidential elector petition under Va. Code 24.2-543, is there any filing fee or fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative to the 5,000-signature petition, or is petition the sole ballot-access path? (Confirming no fee provision exists anywhere in Title 24.2 for this petition.)
  - For the 2024+ cycle, what is the correct current Department of Elections form number for the independent/third-party Petition of Qualified Voters for Electors for President and Vice President — is it ELECT-242(P)? And is any online/electronic filing path available, or is original wet-signature paper still required?

### Washington
- **signatures:** 1,000 registered WA voters (flat; conv. attendees)
- **deadline:** Cert+petition to SOS by 1st Fri of Aug (2028: Aug 4)
- **risk:** 7 fields grounded; 6 AUTO-LIVE, 1 CONSERVATIVE-HOLD (circulator eligibility — absence-of-rule cannot be retrieval-confirmed). Watch SOS "last Saturday in July" vs statutory "fourth Saturday" convention-window discrepancy (differs in 2028: Jul 29 vs Jul 22).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: 1,000 signatures of registered Washington voters (flat statewide number; not a percentage). An independent (or minor-party) presidential candidate is nominated by convention, and the certificate of nomination must be accompanied by nominating petition(s) bearing the signatures of at least 1,000 registered Washington voters. These voters must attend a state convention held in support of the candidate; a candidate holding multiple conventions may aggregate signatures across conventions to reach 1,000.
  - note: All 3 citations grounded verbatim. RCW 29A.56.640(5): 'at least one thousand registered voters of the state of Washington'; RCW 29A.56.610 confirms multi-convention aggregation and 100-attendee minimum; SOS page confirms 1,000 signatures. Statute last amended 2013, no newer amendment found; SOS 2028 page still describes same process. Flat number, no interpretation needed.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE
  - uses: First Friday of August of the presidential election year (for 2028 = August 4, 2028). The certificate of nomination (with the petition(s)) must be submitted to the Secretary of State not later than the first Friday of August. Conventions must be held no earlier than the first Saturday in May and no later than the fourth Saturday in July per RCW 29A.56.610 (for 2028: May 6 to July 22). Date recomputes each cycle.
  - note: RCW 29A.56.640(7) 'not later than the first Friday of August' and RCW 29A.56.610 convention-window quote grounded verbatim; SOS quote grounded. Submission deadline value is correct and verified. NOTE discrepancy: SOS website says conventions run to the 'last Saturday in July' while the controlling statute (RCW 29A.56.610) says 'fourth Saturday in July' — these differ in years with five July Saturdays (2028: 4th=Jul 22 vs last=Jul 29). The draft value correctly uses the stricter statutory 'fourth Saturday'. Updated illustrative date from 2024 (Aug 2) to 2028 cycle (Aug 4).
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE
  - uses: None. Washington requires a flat statewide total of 1,000 registered-voter signatures with no geographic distribution requirement across congressional districts or counties.
  - note: RCW 29A.56.640(5) grounded verbatim; statute requires only a statewide total of 1,000 'registered voters of the state of Washington' with no district/county distribution language anywhere in RCW 29A.56.610-.640. Correct.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: Each person who signs the nominating petition must be a registered Washington voter and must attend a qualifying state convention (the convention must be attended by at least 100 registered voters), and no person may sign more than one nominating petition for an office for an election. Treat any circulator as needing to be a registered Washington voter unless the SOS confirms otherwise. UNKNOWN whether a distinct circulator-qualification rule (age/residency/voter-status of the petition collector, as opposed to the signer) exists beyond these signer/attendee requirements.
  - note: RCW 29A.56.630 and 29A.56.610 grounded verbatim (signer must be registered WA voter; no person signs more than one petition; convention needs 100 registered voters). However the field's core claim is an absence-of-law assertion ('no separate statutory circulator qualification') which retrieval cannot affirmatively confirm; the draft itself marks this UNKNOWN. Per strict-interpretation rule, hold and adopt the strictest defensible reading (circulator treated as needing registered-WA-voter status) pending SOS confirmation.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE
  - uses: No notarized circulator affidavit is required on the petition itself. Verification attaches to the certificate of nomination: it must be verified by the oath of the convention's presiding officer and secretary, and must contain a sworn statement from both nominees consenting to the nomination. The certificate must also contain proof of publication of the convention notice (published in a newspaper of general circulation at least ten days before the convention).
  - note: RCW 29A.56.640(2) (sworn consent of nominees) and (4) (verified by oath of presiding officer and secretary) grounded verbatim; RCW 29A.56.620 (newspaper notice at least ten days before convention) grounded verbatim. No petition-level notarized circulator affidavit appears in statute. Correct.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE
  - uses: paper. The petition is gathered on paper from registered voters who physically attend the state convention, and the certificate of nomination plus petitions are submitted to the Secretary of State by mail or by in-person appointment. There is no remote-online or digitized signature system covering an independent presidential nominating petition in Washington (Washington is not among the jurisdictions that allow electronic signing of candidate nominating petitions).
  - note: SOS quote (voters must attend a state convention) grounded verbatim; 2024 candidate guide PDF grounded verbatim ('Call (360) 902-4180 to schedule an in-person appointment, or submit by mail to:' — split across PDF lines 102-103 but exact). Ballotpedia electronic-signing list grounded (Arizona/New Mexico online, Denver/DC eSign) and does NOT include Washington, confirming no e-signature path. Guide's 'online' references are voters' pamphlet only, not petition signing. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE
  - uses: None. There is no filing fee for a presidential candidate in Washington, and there is no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative; the signature/convention requirement is the sole path.
  - note: SOS quote 'There is no filing fee' grounded verbatim; 2024 guide independently confirms 'Washington state does not collect filing fees for the offices of President and Vice President.' No fee-in-lieu provision exists in RCW 29A.56.610-.640. Correct.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Beyond requiring that each petition signer be a registered Washington voter who attends a qualifying state convention, does Washington impose any separate qualification (age, residency, voter-registration, or affidavit) on the person who circulates/collects an independent or minor-party presidential nominating petition?

### West Virginia
- **signatures:** 7,947 sigs (1% of 2020 WV presidential vote; min 25) — recomputes each cycle
- **deadline:** Aug 1 — nomination certificate + $2,500 fee to Secretary of State
- **risk:** 7 of 8 fields AUTO-LIVE on strong primary+consensus grounding; only circulatorEligibility is CONSERVATIVE-HOLD (statute is silent on whether a non-resident/non-registered person may circulate beyond the county-clerk credential requirement — an interpretation gap). No field is BLOCKED. Note the credentials doc is officially "Form P-1," not "P-3" as the captureMode/witness fields imply for the credential.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Signatures equal to at least 1% of the entire vote cast for president in the last preceding presidential election (statewide), but in no event fewer than 25. For the 2024 cycle the threshold was 7,947 (1% of West Virginia's 2020 presidential vote of 794,731). Recomputes each presidential cycle.
  - note: All three citations verified verbatim: §3-5-23 ('not less than one percent... but in no event... less than 25'; also a second sentence keyed to 'any statewide, congressional, or presidential candidate'), NASS report ('equal to at least 1% of the entire vote cast for president in the last preceding presidential election'), and WV Watch ('Kennedy... needed 7,947 signatures'). Independently re-derived: 1% of WV 2020 presidential total (794,731) = 7,947 exactly. Cross-confirmed by Ballotpedia ('1 percent of the total votes cast in the state for president in the most recent election'). The 25 floor is statutory.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.97
  - uses: August 1 preceding the November general election. The nomination certificate (petition) and filing fee must be filed with the Secretary of State no later than August 1 (e.g., August 1, 2024 for the 2024 cycle).
  - note: §3-5-24(a) verbatim: 'All certificates nominating candidates for office under section twenty-three... shall be filed not later than August 1 preceding the November general election.' NASS report verbatim ('no later than August 1st preceding the general election'). Cross-confirmed by Ballotpedia ('by August 1 in the year of the election').
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None for a presidential (statewide) candidate. The 1% threshold is a single statewide total against the entire presidential vote; there is no per-congressional-district or per-county minimum. Separate petition forms per county exist solely for county-clerk verification, with no minimum-per-county quota.
  - note: §3-5-23 quote verified verbatim. Statute measures 1% against the statewide vote with no geographic-distribution language; 'Offices to be filled by the voters of more than one county shall use separate petition forms... for each county' is administrative (verification), not a quota. Ballotpedia describes only a flat statewide 1% with no district distribution (the only 'distribution' reference is to Electoral College apportionment). No source found imposing a per-county/per-district signature minimum.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.60
  - uses: STRICT: The circulator must obtain Official Credentials (Form P-1) from the clerk of the county commission for EACH county in which they canvass and must exhibit those credentials to every voter solicited. Until the SOS confirms otherwise, assume the strictest reading — that a circulator should be a West Virginia resident and a registered voter (matching the residency framing of the credential and the signer requirements) — rather than relying on the absence of an explicit circulator age/residency rule.
  - note: Credentialing requirement verified verbatim in §3-5-23(b) and on the credentials form (extracted from media/413). The statute imposes residency/registration on SIGNERS, not expressly on circulators, and the draft honestly flags this as UNKNOWN. But the credential authorizes soliciting 'voters residing in [county],' leaving genuinely unsettled whether a non-resident/non-registered person may circulate — an interpretation retrieval cannot resolve. Per over-comply mandate, HOLD and query the SOS. (Also: the credentials doc is officially 'Official Form P-1,' which the draft's P-3-centric framing conflates.)
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: No notarized circulator affidavit is required. Each signer personally signs in their own handwriting (or by a duly witnessed mark). The official paper petition (Form P-3) contains only signer rows plus a 'County Use' VLD/INV validity column; county-commission clerks verify signatures against county voter-registration records. There is no sworn circulator certification.
  - note: Both §3-5-23 quotes verified verbatim ('personally signed by duly registered voters, in their own proper handwriting or by their marks duly witnessed' and the clerk-comparison-to-registration-records provision in subsection (e)). P-3 form text extracted directly confirms only signer fields plus a 'County Use / VLD INV' column and no notary/circulator-oath block. Statute imposes no circulator oath or notarization.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Signatures are collected on the Secretary of State's paper 'Minor Party or Independent Candidate Nomination Petition' (Official Form P-3), with separate forms per county, and verified by county clerks. There is NO digital/remote-online or in-person-digitized petition system for an independent presidential candidate in West Virginia.
  - note: Form P-3 PDF (media/414) text extracted and matches the quote verbatim: 'MINOR PARTY OR INDEPENDENT CANDIDATE NOMINATION PETITION... we, the undersigned, are registered voters of ____ County... Official form P-3/Issued by the Office of the Secretary of State (WV Code §3-5-23).' §3-5-23 verbatim: 'Offices to be filled by the voters of more than one county shall use separate petition forms... for each county.' No statute, form, or SOS source indicates any electronic/online signature option; paper is the only mode.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: A filing fee is required IN ADDITION to (not in lieu of) the signature petition. The fee equals 1% of the annual salary of the office, capped at $2,500; for president/vice president the fee is $2,500, paid when the nomination certificate is filed. A separate impecuniosity path (§3-5-8a) lets a candidate unable to pay petition in lieu of the fee (four signatures per dollar of fee), but the standard independent-presidential path is petition PLUS the $2,500 fee.
  - note: NASS quote verbatim ('must also pay a fee equivalent to 1% of the annual salary... must not exceed $2500'). §3-5-24(c) verbatim ('Each candidate shall pay the filing fee required by section eight... at the time of the filing of the nomination certificate'). §3-5-8(a)(1) independently confirms the $2,500 cap for president/VP. Ballotpedia confirms the fee is additive ('In addition, the candidate must pay a $2,500 filing fee') and the §3-5-8a waiver ('four signatures for each dollar of the filing fee'). The draft's framing of the waiver as 'additional signatures' is slightly loose (it substitutes for the FEE, not the nomination petition) but does not affect the relied value for the standard path.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - West Virginia SOS Elections Division: Beyond obtaining county-clerk credentials under W. Va. Code §3-5-23(b), is a petition circulator for an independent presidential nomination certificate required to be (a) a West Virginia resident, (b) a registered voter, and/or (c) at least 18 years old, or may an out-of-state/non-registered person circulate so long as they hold valid county credentials?

### Wisconsin
- **signatures:** 2,000–4,000 valid elector signatures (flat statutory band; AUTO-LIVE)
- **deadline:** 5 p.m. first Tuesday in August of the presidential year (Aug 6 in 2024); circulate from July 1; file with WEC — AUTO-LIVE
- **risk:** All fields grounded; one HOLD — 2025 Act 126 (eff. 2026-03-30) made circulators be qualified WI-resident electors, with a presidential-papers carve-out the stale eLaws citation does not surface, so circulatorEligibility is held to the strictest (WI-resident) reading pending WEC confirmation.

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.96
  - uses: Not less than 2,000 nor more than 4,000 valid signatures of electors — a flat statutory band specific to independent presidential electors voting for the same president/VP candidates (Wis. Stat. 8.20(4)). It is NOT a percentage of votes cast and does not recompute by cycle. Collect a cushion above 2,000 to survive challenges, but do not file more than 4,000.
  - note: Both citations verified VERBATIM. eLaws 8.20(4): 'For independent presidential electors intending to vote for the same candidates for president and vice president, the number of required signatures shall be not less than 2,000 nor more than 4,000 electors.' NASS July-2024 report (downloaded, pdftotext): 'nomination papers containing between 2,000 and 4,000 signatures.' Adversarial check: 2025 Act 126 amended 8.20 but only as to circulator qualifications, not signature counts; no later act changes the band. Value current and correct.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: Nomination papers may be circulated no sooner than July 1 and must be filed no later than 5:00 p.m. on the first Tuesday in August preceding the presidential election (Wis. Stat. 8.20(8)(am)), filed with the Wisconsin Elections Commission. For 2024 this was 5:00 p.m. on August 6, 2024. The date recomputes each presidential cycle.
  - note: Both citations verified VERBATIM. eLaws 8.20(8)(am): 'may be circulated no sooner than July 1 and may be filed not later than 5 p.m. on the first Tuesday in August preceding a presidential election.' Lisbon WI Type-A notice (downloaded, pdftotext, line 12-14): 'Independent candidates for President or Vice President may circulate nomination papers beginning July 1, 2024, and must file nomination papers with the Wisconsin Elections Commission no later than 5:00 p.m. on August 6, 2024.' NASS corroborates filing 'no later than the first Tuesday in August.' Current and correct.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: None for the independent presidential petition. The 2,000–4,000 signatures may be gathered anywhere in Wisconsin (signers must be electors eligible to vote in the state) with no per-congressional-district or per-county minimum. (Separate, materially different path: forming a recognized political party requires 10,000 electors including at least 1,000 in each of at least 3 congressional districts — this is NOT the independent path.)
  - note: Both citations verified VERBATIM. eLaws 8.20(5): 'Signers of each nomination paper shall reside in the same jurisdiction or district which the candidate named therein will represent, if elected.' NASS report: 'A political organization may also become a recognized political party by filing... a petition containing the signatures of at least 10,000 electors, including at least 1,000 electors residing in each of at least 3 separate congressional districts.' Adversarial check: statute imposes only a same-jurisdiction (statewide, for president) residency requirement and no district/county allocation for the independent petition; the distribution rule applies only to the distinct party-formation path. Correct; the contrast is properly flagged.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.80
  - uses: STRICTEST: treat every circulator as required to be a QUALIFIED ELECTOR OF WISCONSIN — i.e., a U.S. citizen, age 18+, a Wisconsin resident at their residence for 28+ days, not serving a felony sentence, not adjudicated incompetent to vote, who intends to support the candidate and signs the s.8.15(4)(a) circulator certification (no notarization). A non-resident-circulator allowance MAY exist for presidential papers, but do not rely on it without written WEC confirmation. If a circulator lists an out-of-state address, WEC strikes the entire page.
  - note: The eLaws quotes (8.15(4)(a) non-resident allowance; 8.20(3) certification-appended) match VERBATIM — but eLaws is a JAN-2017 snapshot and is STALE. 2025 Wisconsin Act 126 (signed/effective 2026-03-30) AMENDED 8.10, 8.15, 8.20, 8.40, 9.10 to require circulators be a 'qualified elector of this state,' removing the old non-resident allowance. WEC's official 2026-04-08 Act 126 memo (fetched) says the change applies 'except Presidential nomination papers,' and notes presidential circulators 'may still be adult U.S. citizens who are not Wisconsin residents but who would be qualified to vote under Wisconsin law.' So the draft's bottom-line outcome is likely correct FOR THE PRESIDENTIAL PATH — but it now hinges entirely on a non-obvious statutory carve-out the stale citation never surfaces, and the general headline is now 'must reside in Wisconsin.' Per over-comply mandate (never risk ballot access), HOLD to the strict WI-resident reading and confirm the carve-out with WEC in writing.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: No notarization required. Each nomination paper requires a circulator certification (signed and dated by the circulator at the bottom of the sheet under s.8.15(4)(a)) attesting that the circulator personally circulated the paper and personally obtained each signature, knows the signers are electors of the required jurisdiction, knows they signed knowingly on the stated dates, and that falsifying the certification is punishable under Wis. Stat. 12.13(3)(a). The certification may be made by the candidate or any qualified circulator.
  - note: eLaws 8.15(4)(a) quote verified VERBATIM, incl. 'personally circulated the nomination paper and personally obtained each of the signatures... aware that falsifying the certification is punishable under s. 12.13 (3) (a)... may be made by the candidate or any qualified circulator.' Adversarial check: Wisconsin uses circulator certification, not a notary/witness; Act 126 changes WHO may certify (qualifications) but does not add a notarization requirement. The no-notary conclusion is unaffected and correct. (Note the linked qualified-circulator definition is the field handled under circulatorEligibility.)
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: paper. Wisconsin requires physical paper nomination papers (EL-167 for independent president/VP) with wet-ink signatures: each signer must legibly print name, list municipality of residence, street and number, and date of signing next to their signature, and a circulator must physically circulate each sheet and sign the certification. There is NO official online/remote-electronic petition for an independent presidential petition; the official filing is paper, delivered to the Wisconsin Elections Commission.
  - note: Both citations verified VERBATIM. eLaws 8.20(5): 'each signer shall legibly print his or her name in a space provided next to his or her signature and shall list his or her municipality of residence for voting purposes, the street and number, if any, on which the signer resides, and the date of signing.' eLaws 8.15(4)(a): 'personally circulated the nomination paper and personally obtained each of the signatures.' WEC pages confirm paper EL-167 forms and in-person filing. No e-signature path exists. Correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.88
  - uses: None. Wisconsin imposes no filing fee for ballot access and provides no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures alternative for independent presidential candidates — qualification is by nomination-paper signatures only (2,000–4,000) plus a declaration of candidacy under s.8.21. (Separately, 2025 Act 43 imposes a fee only to WITHDRAW a name from the ballot — that is not a ballot-access fee and does not create a fee path.)
  - note: Both citations verified VERBATIM. eLaws 8.20(6): 'Nomination papers shall be accompanied by a declaration of candidacy under s. 8.21.' NASS report lists qualification by signatures only with no fee. Adversarial check: I checked for any fee path. The only fee found (WEC FAQ, 2025 Act 43) is for REMOVING a name from the ballot via sworn statement — a withdrawal fee, not an access fee or fee-in-lieu of signatures. No fee-in-lieu exists. Correct.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Confirm in writing: for INDEPENDENT PRESIDENTIAL nomination papers (EL-167) filed for the 2028 general election, does the 2025 Act 126 presidential carve-out still allow a circulator who is an adult U.S. citizen, 18+, not a Wisconsin resident, but who would be qualified to vote under Wis. law — or must all circulators now be qualified Wisconsin-resident electors?

### Wyoming
- **signatures:** 3,891 valid sigs (2% of 2022 U.S. House vote); recomputed each cycle
- **deadline:** File with SOS no later than 70 days before general (2024: Aug 26, 2024)
- **risk:** All 8 fields grounded; statute and SOS form agree. Only open item: circulator qualifications are unstated in primary sources (held conservative). Fee conflict ($200 NASS vs $750) resolved to $750 by W.S. 22-5-208(a)(iii)+22-5-306(b).

**🟢 signaturesRequired** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.93
  - uses: 2% of the total number of votes cast in Wyoming for U.S. Representative in the last general election. For the 2024 cycle this equaled 3,891 valid signatures. (Statewide flat figure; recomputed each cycle from the most recent U.S. House vote total.) Statutory basis: W.S. 22-5-304(a).
  - note: Quotes verified verbatim: SOS form (downloaded+text-extracted, lines 12-16: 'numbering not less than two percent (2%)... 3,891 for the upcoming 2024 General Election (W.S. 22-5-304(a))') and FindLaw W.S. 22-5-304(a). Independently re-derived: 2022 WY U.S. House total = 193,902 votes; 2% = ~3,878, within source-variance of the official 3,891 (corroborates, does not refute). Caveat: statute text reads 'statewide PARTISAN office', but the SOS office-issued independent-presidential form authoritatively applies the same 2% figure and cites 304(a), so this is office-settled, not an open interpretation.
**🟢 deadline** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.95
  - uses: The petition must be filed with the Secretary of State not less than 70 days before the general election. For the 2024 cycle the filing deadline was August 26, 2024. A petition may be circulated for signatures only during the election year (W.S. 22-5-305(a)). Recomputes each cycle (70 days before the November general election date).
  - note: Verified verbatim: SOS form line 22-24 ('Filing Deadline: August 26, 2024. You must file not less than seventy (70) days prior...') and Ballotpedia ('no later than 70 days prior to the general election'). W.S. 22-5-305(a) circulation-window quote verified verbatim on FindLaw. Date is cycle-specific; the 70-day formula is the durable rule, correctly stated.
**🟢 distributionRule** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: None. For president (a statewide office) the requirement is a single statewide total of 2% of the last U.S. House vote; signatures are not allocated per congressional district or county. (W.S. 22-5-304(a) governs statewide office; the per-county/per-district formulas in 22-5-304(b)-(c) apply only to countywide and district offices.)
  - note: Verified verbatim: W.S. 22-5-304(a) on FindLaw and SOS form lines 37-38. Confirmed adversarially that 304(b) is countywide and 304(c) is district — neither applies to a statewide/presidential petition. No geographic distribution requirement exists. WY has a single at-large U.S. House district, so no district split is even possible.
**🟡 circulatorEligibility** — CONSERVATIVE-HOLD · 0.70
  - uses: UNRESOLVED / verify with SOS. Wyoming's petition statutes (W.S. 22-5-304/305/306) and the SOS petition form impose eligibility only on SIGNERS (registered elector, resident in the jurisdiction, eligible to vote for the petitioner). No age, residency, or registration qualification for the CIRCULATOR is stated in any primary source; the form requires only that the circulator certify they personally circulated the petition and give a name and residence address. Treat circulator qualifications as unconfirmed until the SOS verifies; do not assume non-residents may circulate.
  - note: Citations grounded: SOS form circulator verification (lines 66-67) and W.S. 22-5-305(c) signer requirements, both verbatim. The draft's factual reading (no stated circulator requirement) is correct, BUT absence of a stated requirement is not proof none exists in rule/practice; strictest posture holds it open. Hold + SOS inquiry filed.
**🟢 witnessOrNotary** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: Circulator certification (NOT notarized). The petition carries a 'VERIFICATION BY CIRCULATOR' in which the circulator certifies personal circulation and that signatures were made in their presence; there is no notarization requirement on the form. Separately, the presidential and vice-presidential candidates must file sworn statements naming the three presidential electors.
  - note: Verified verbatim against the extracted SOS form: VERIFICATION BY CIRCULATOR block (lines 65-68) and Sworn Statements paragraph (lines 18-20). Confirmed zero occurrences of 'notary'/'notariz' anywhere in the extracted form text. Circulator attestation, not notarization, is correct.
**🟢 captureMode** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.90
  - uses: paper. Signatures must be collected on the printed SOS petition form (which must be approved by the filing office before circulation), and each signer must hand-print name, date of signing, and physical residential address. No online/remote or digitized e-signature system exists for an independent presidential petition in Wyoming; collection and filing are paper-only.
  - note: Verified verbatim: W.S. 22-5-305(b)-(c) on FindLaw and the SOS form's 'The petition shall be approved by the appropriate filing office prior to circulation' (form lines 5-6). Form requires handwritten signer fields and prohibits P.O. boxes. No statutory or SOS e-signature pathway found; paper-only is correct.
**🟢 feeAlternative** — AUTO-LIVE · 0.92
  - uses: $750 filing fee REQUIRED (in addition to, NOT in lieu of, the signatures). The petition is invalid if not accompanied by the fee. Statutory chain: W.S. 22-5-306(b) ties the independent-petition fee to the same fee a primary candidate pays for the same office, and W.S. 22-5-208(a)(iii) sets $750 for any federal office voted on statewide. The NASS July-2024 summary's $200 figure is incorrect and should be disregarded.
  - note: Conflict RESOLVED in verification. SOS form ('Filing Fee: $750 – Candidates for federal offices', line 26) and Ballotpedia ($750) verified verbatim; NASS PDF ($200, line 1178 of extract) verified verbatim as the conflicting source. Decisive primary source: W.S. 22-5-208(a)(iii) = '$750.00 for any federal office voted for by electors of the entire state', combined with 22-5-306(b) (fee = same as primary). $750 is statutorily controlling; NASS $200 is simply wrong/stale. Note this is a mandatory fee in addition to signatures, despite the field name 'feeAlternative' — there is no fee-in-lieu-of-signatures path in Wyoming.

_SoS inquiries:_
  - Wyoming independent presidential nominating petition: are there any qualifications for a petition CIRCULATOR (minimum age, Wyoming residency, or voter registration), or may any person circulate, given the form only requires the circulator to certify personal circulation and give a residence address?
